Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  The questions aim for a difficult level, requiring precise factual recall and conceptual understanding.


**1.  Which of the following accurately describes the properties and applications of Graphene?**

(a)  Graphene is a poor conductor of heat and electricity, making it unsuitable for electronic applications but ideal for thermal insulation.
(b) Graphene, an allotrope of carbon, exhibits low surface area and weak mechanical strength, limiting its use primarily to lubricants.
(c) Graphene's high surface area, biocompatibility, and excellent thermal conductivity make it suitable for applications ranging from solar cells to biosensors.
(d) Graphene, primarily used in pencils, is a naturally occurring, amorphous form of carbon with limited applications in modern technology.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) accurately reflects the key properties and diverse applications of graphene.  Graphene's unique structure gives it exceptional properties: a high surface area due to its single-layer, two-dimensional structure which enhances interactions; good biocompatibility which makes it suitable for biomedical applications; strong mechanical strength for structural applications; and excellent thermal conductivity for applications such as heat dissipation in electronics. These properties support its diverse applications, spanning energy storage (solar cells, fuel cells), electronics (supercomputers), and biosensors, among others.

Options (a), (b), and (d) present inaccurate or incomplete information.  Graphene is, in fact, an excellent conductor of heat and electricity, contrary to (a).  (b) misrepresents graphene's mechanical strength and surface area.  While graphite (a different allotrope of carbon) is used in pencils, (d) wrongly limits graphene's applications.  The existence of the Graphene Innovation Centre in Kerala further underlines its significance in modern technology.


**2. Which statement best characterizes the limitations of Carbon-14 dating?**

(a) Carbon-14 dating accurately determines the age of all organic and inorganic materials, regardless of their age.
(b) Carbon-14's long half-life of 57,000 years makes it ideal for dating extremely old objects, surpassing the limitations of other dating methods.
(c) Carbon-14's unstable nature and short half-life restrict its use to relatively young organic materials, limiting its application to objects less than approximately 50,000 years old.
(d) The constant ratio of C-12 to C-14 in the atmosphere makes Carbon-14 dating highly precise for all materials, regardless of environmental factors.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) correctly highlights the key limitations of carbon-14 dating. The relatively short half-life of carbon-14 (approximately 5,700 years) means that after around 50,000 years, the remaining amount becomes too small to be accurately measured. This restricts its applicability to relatively young organic materials.  The method relies on the decay of carbon-14 after the organism dies, and its effectiveness is hampered by the limited time frame before the isotope becomes undetectable.  Furthermore, the method is unsuitable for non-living things like rocks.

Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect. (a) is false because carbon-14 dating only applies to organic materials. (b) incorrectly states the half-life and its implications. (d) overlooks environmental factors that can affect the C-12 to C-14 ratio and influence the accuracy of the dating.


**3.  A study utilized hybrid nanoparticles of gold and copper sulphide to treat cancer. Which of the following mechanisms best describes their therapeutic action?**

(a)  The nanoparticles directly attack and destroy cancer cells through a chemical reaction, without any heat generation.
(b) The nanoparticles' photoacoustic properties generate light, which directly kills tumour cells.
(c) The nanoparticles' photothermal properties generate heat, killing tumour cells and producing reactive oxygen species (ROS) which are toxic to cancer cells.
(d) The nanoparticles solely rely on their ability to absorb sound waves, thereby eliminating cancer cells.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) accurately describes the dual mechanism of action of the gold and copper sulphide hybrid nanoparticles.  The photothermal property enables the conversion of absorbed light into heat, which directly damages and kills tumor cells.  Concurrently, the heat generation also triggers the production of reactive oxygen species (ROS), which further contributes to the cytotoxic effect on the cancer cells. This combination of heat and ROS enhances the therapeutic efficacy.  The use of an endoscope to deliver the light further highlights the targeted nature of this approach.

Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect. (a) is false because heat generation is a crucial part of the mechanism.  (b) incorrectly attributes the therapeutic effect solely to light generation; it is the heat produced that is primarily cytotoxic.  (d) wrongly emphasizes sound waves; although photoacoustic properties are mentioned for diagnostic purposes, the treatment mechanism is primarily photothermal.


**4.  The Draft National Strategy for Robotics (NSR) in India classifies robots into which of the following categories?**

(a)  Household robots, military robots, and agricultural robots.
(b)  Industrial robots, service robots, and medical robots.
(c)  Aerial robots, underwater robots, and land-based robots.
(d)  Autonomous robots, semi-autonomous robots, and remotely operated robots.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Option (b) correctly identifies the classification of robots under the NSR.  The strategy categorizes robots based on their primary application areas: industrial robots for manufacturing and production; service robots for various non-manufacturing tasks; and medical robots for healthcare applications.  This classification provides a framework for policy and development initiatives related to each category.

Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect. While the categories in (a), (c), and (d) represent types of robots, they don't reflect the specific classification system adopted by the NSR.  The NSR's classification is application-based, not based on operational mode or environment.


**5. Which characteristic is NOT a property of Tantalum?**

(a) High melting point
(b) High corrosion resistance
(c)  Low density
(d)  High ductility


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) correctly identifies the characteristic that is NOT a property of tantalum. Tantalum is a high-density metal, not low-density. Its high density is a significant property contributing to its use in applications requiring weight and durability. The other options (high melting point, high corrosion resistance, and high ductility) are all accurate properties of tantalum.  The high melting point is why it is considered as a substitute for platinum in some applications.


**6.  Which of the following statements about the Advanced Liquid Processing System (ALPS) is FALSE?**

(a) ALPS is used to treat contaminated water at the Fukushima Daiichi Nuclear Power Station.
(b) ALPS removes radionuclides, including caesium and strontium, from contaminated water.
(c) ALPS uses a single chemical reaction to remove all radioactive elements from the water.
(d)  Prior to ALPS treatment, caesium and strontium were removed periodically from the contaminated water.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) is false. ALPS employs a series of chemical reactions, not a single reaction, to remove radionuclides from contaminated water. The complexity of the process is necessary to address the diverse radioactive contaminants present in the water.  The other statements accurately describe the function and application of ALPS in the context of the Fukushima Daiichi accident.


**7. Which of the following is NOT a component of the Hyperloop transportation system?**

(a) A large, sealed, low-pressure tube.
(b)  A pressurized pod propelled by magnetic levitation.
(c)  A conventional rail system.
(d)  Terminals handling pod arrivals and departures.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) is incorrect.  The Hyperloop system does not use a conventional rail system; instead, it relies on a low-pressure tube to minimize friction and allow for high speeds. The other options accurately describe the essential components of the Hyperloop concept. The system's design aims to eliminate the friction associated with traditional transportation systems.


**8.  Which of the following best describes the process of nuclear fusion?**

(a)  The splitting of heavy atomic nuclei into lighter ones, releasing energy.
(b)  The combining of light atomic nuclei into heavier ones, releasing massive amounts of energy.
(c)  The spontaneous decay of radioactive isotopes, releasing energy.
(d)  The controlled chain reaction of fissile materials, releasing energy.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Option (b) accurately defines nuclear fusion. The process involves combining light atomic nuclei (like isotopes of hydrogen) to create a heavier nucleus, releasing a significant amount of energy in the process. This energy release is the basis for the potential of fusion power. The other options describe different processes: fission (a), radioactive decay (c), and nuclear fission chain reaction (d).


**9. Which of the following is NOT an advantage of Small Modular Reactors (SMRs)?**

(a)  Reduced capital investment compared to traditional reactors.
(b)  Potential for cost reductions through mass production.
(c)  Requirement for large, specific sites near water sources.
(d)  Enhanced safety features, including passive safety systems.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) is incorrect.  SMRs are designed to have less restrictive site requirements compared to traditional nuclear reactors, making them deployable in a wider range of locations.  This is a key advantage of SMR technology, addressing the limitations of traditional reactor siting. The other options accurately describe advantages of SMRs.


**10.  Which of the following is a limitation of nuclear fusion power, despite its potential benefits?**

(a) Abundant fuel supply.
(b) Low radioactive waste production.
(c) Difficulty in achieving and maintaining the extreme temperatures and pressures needed for sustained fusion reactions.
(d)  Inherent safety due to the lack of risk of a meltdown.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) correctly identifies a major challenge in nuclear fusion.  Achieving and maintaining the extremely high temperatures and pressures required for sustained fusion reactions remains a significant technological hurdle. While fusion has many potential advantages, this technical difficulty is a key reason why commercially viable fusion power plants are not yet a reality.  The other options represent advantages of fusion power.


Here are some difficult multiple-choice questions (MCQs) based on the provided target content, designed to test various cognitive skills and adhere to the specified criteria.  Each question includes a detailed explanation.

**1.  Which of the following statements accurately describes the role of the  "agglutinates" component found in lunar regolith?**

(a) Agglutinates are primarily composed of volcanic glass, formed during ancient lunar eruptions.
(b) Agglutinates are sharp, angular soil grains with freshly fractured surfaces.
(c) Agglutinates are a unique component found only on the Moon, formed by the welding together of fine particles by micrometeorite impacts.
(d) Agglutinates are mineral fragments originating from the lunar mantle, brought to the surface through volcanic activity.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The correct answer is (c) because agglutinates are indeed a unique characteristic of lunar regolith. They are not simply one type of material (like volcanic glass or sharp soil grains), but rather a composite material.  Micrometeorite impacts are the primary process responsible for their formation. These impacts melt and fuse together fine-grained particles of lunar dust and soil, creating these distinctive, welded aggregates. Option (a) is incorrect because while volcanic glass is present in lunar regolith, it's not the defining characteristic of agglutinates. Option (b) describes the characteristics of individual soil grains, not the composite agglutinates. Option (d) is incorrect because, while some agglutinates may incorporate material from the lunar mantle, their formation is primarily a surface process related to micrometeorite impacts. The unique nature of agglutinates and their formation mechanism are crucial aspects of lunar geology.


**2. A space mission aims to study the origin and composition of solar wind. Which of the following ISRO missions is best suited for this objective?**

(a) Chandrayaan-3
(b) Aditya-L1
(c) Gaganyaan
(d) NavIC


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Aditya-L1 is specifically designed to study the Sun, including the origin, composition, and dynamics of the solar wind.  The mission's in-situ payloads (like ASPEX and PAPA) are directly aimed at measuring particles and plasma in the solar wind near the L1 Lagrange point. Chandrayaan-3 focuses on lunar exploration; Gaganyaan is a crewed mission, and NavIC is a navigation system.  Therefore, only Aditya-L1 directly addresses the question's focus on solar wind research. The detailed description of Aditya-L1's payloads and its location at L1 highlight its suitability for this research.


**3.  Which of the following accurately reflects the primary challenge faced by solar-powered lunar missions during the lunar night?**

(a)  The absence of an atmosphere on the Moon causes extreme temperature fluctuations, making it difficult to maintain spacecraft systems.
(b)  The constant bombardment of micrometeoroids during the lunar night damages sensitive equipment.
(c)  The reduced solar radiation during the lunar night limits the energy available to power the mission's instruments.
(d) The lack of sunlight during the lunar night leads to the accumulation of lunar dust on solar panels, reducing their efficiency.


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The main challenge is the extreme temperature variations. The absence of an atmosphere on the Moon means there's no insulation against the intense solar radiation during the day and the extreme cold of the night. This dramatic temperature swing (from over 120°C to -130°C) can severely impact the electronics and other sensitive components of spacecraft. Options (b), (c), and (d) are all factors that affect lunar missions, but they are not the primary challenges during the lunar night.  Micrometeoroid impacts are a risk throughout the mission, not solely during the night. Reduced solar radiation is the reason for the temperature drop, not the primary challenge itself.  Dust accumulation is a concern, but temperature extremes pose a more significant threat to the survival of equipment.


**4. The development of which of the following technologies is directly associated with the "Jasmine" project, a joint Indian-Ukrainian endeavor?**

(a)  PSLV Orbital Experimental Module (POEM)
(b)  CE-20 Cryogenic Engine
(c)  Semi-Cryogenic Engine (SCE-200)
(d)  Small Satellite Launch Vehicle (SSLV)


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The text explicitly states that the "Jasmine" project, a collaboration between India and Ukraine, was focused on the development of the Semi-Cryogenic Engine (SCE-200).  This engine utilizes a combination of liquid oxygen and RP-1 kerosene. The other options are not linked to the Jasmine project in the provided text.  The details about the transfer of blueprints for the RD-810 engine and its role in the SCE-200's development clearly indicate the connection between the Jasmine project and the SCE-200.


**5. Which of the following statements best describes the unique characteristic of the "Agnilet" engine used in the Agnibaan SubOrbital Technological Demonstrator (SOrTeD)?**

(a) It is a three-stage solid propulsion engine.
(b) It utilizes liquid oxygen and liquid hydrogen as propellants.
(c) It is a 2 MN thrust class liquid rocket engine designed for heavy-lift launch vehicles.
(d) It is a 3D-printed, single-piece, semi-cryogenic engine.


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The passage explicitly highlights that the Agnilet engine is a unique achievement in that it is entirely 3D-printed, a single-piece component, and utilizes semi-cryogenic technology.  The other options describe different engine types and characteristics not associated with the Agnilet engine as described in the provided text. The significance of the Agnilet engine lies in its innovative 3D-printing method and its semi-cryogenic design, making it a notable development in rocket propulsion technology.


**6.  Which of the following ISRO missions successfully demonstrated a gravity assist flyby around another celestial body for the first time?**

(a) Chandrayaan-1
(b) Chandrayaan-2
(c) Chandrayaan-3
(d) Aditya-L1


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The text specifically mentions that Chandrayaan-3's Propulsion Module successfully returned from lunar orbit to Earth's orbit, employing a gravity assist flyby around the Moon—a first for ISRO. The other missions did not involve this type of maneuver. The successful execution of the gravity assist flyby is a significant technological achievement for ISRO and expands the capabilities of its space missions.  The specific mention of this being a "first instance" for ISRO makes it the only correct option.


**7. Which of the following best describes the primary function of the Velocity Trimming Module (VTM) in the Small Satellite Launch Vehicle (SSLV)?**

(c)  It performs the final adjustments to the satellite's orbit.
(d)  It carries the secondary payloads into orbit.

**Explanation:**

The text clarifies that the VTM is the terminal stage of the SSLV, responsible for making the final adjustments to the satellite's orbit.  The other options describe functions performed by other stages of the launch vehicle. The description of the VTM as a "terminal stage" and its "liquid propulsion-based" nature emphasizes its role in precise orbital maneuvering.


**8.  Which of the following accurately describes the classification system used for solar flares based on their energy output?**

(a)  A linear scale, where each increment represents a fixed increase in energy.
(b)  A logarithmic scale, where each letter represents a tenfold increase in energy.
(c)  A numerical scale, where higher numbers indicate stronger flares.
(d)  A qualitative scale, based on visual observations of the flare's intensity.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The text clearly states that solar flares are classified on a logarithmic scale using the letters A, B, C, M, and X, with each letter representing a tenfold increase in energy output. The other options do not accurately reflect the described classification system.  The use of a logarithmic scale is essential for representing the wide range of energy outputs observed in solar flares.  The explanation provides the specific details of the classification system to eliminate any ambiguity.

The other options are significant ISRO centers but are not responsible for SCE development.  The direct mention of LPSC's role makes it the unambiguous correct answer.


**10. The Indian Neutrino Observatory (INO) is designed primarily to study which of the following?**

(a) Gravitational waves
(b) Solar flares
(c) Cosmic rays and neutrinos
(d) Dark matter maps


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The other options are associated with different areas of astrophysics and space research. The specific mention of INO as a "neutrino observatory" and its purpose of observing neutrinos from astrophysical sources makes (c) the most accurate answer.


Here are some difficult multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, designed to test various cognitive skills and avoid simple guessing.  Each question includes a detailed explanation.


**1.  Which organization is responsible for developing the State Energy Efficiency Index (SEEI)?**

(a) The Ministry of Panchayati Raj (MoPR)
(b) The Bureau of Energy Efficiency (BEE), in collaboration with the Alliance for an Energy Efficient Economy (AEEE)
(c) The Ministry of Jal Shakti
(d) The Ministry of New and Renewable Energy

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The State Energy Efficiency Index (SEEI) is a crucial tool for monitoring energy efficiency initiatives across Indian states and union territories.  It's not developed by a single ministry but through a collaborative effort. The Bureau of Energy Efficiency (BEE), a statutory body under the Ministry of Power, plays the central role in developing the SEEI.  The Alliance for an Energy Efficient Economy (AEEE) collaborates with BEE in this process, providing expertise and support.  The MoPR, Ministry of Jal Shakti, and Ministry of New and Renewable Energy are involved in related energy and environmental policies but are not directly responsible for SEEI development.  The collaborative nature of SEEI's creation highlights the multi-faceted approach required for effective energy efficiency management in a federal structure.  The question tests factual recall and understanding of institutional roles in energy policy.


**2.  Which technology uses sodium ions as charge carriers to store and release electrical energy, offering a potentially low-cost alternative to a more established technology?**

(a) Gravity battery
(b) Advanced Chemistry Cells (ACC) battery
(c) Sodium Ion Battery (SIB)
(d) Biodegradable Paper Supercapacitor

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question focuses on identifying a specific battery technology based on its core functionality and comparative advantages.  While gravity batteries, ACC batteries, and biodegradable paper supercapacitors are all alternative energy storage solutions, only the Sodium Ion Battery (SIB) directly uses sodium ions as charge carriers.  This is a key differentiator, making it the correct answer.  The question tests factual recall and the ability to differentiate between various energy storage technologies based on their fundamental principles.  The mention of "low-cost alternative" further directs the respondent towards SIBs, which are being developed as a cost-effective substitute for lithium-ion batteries.


**3. Which international organization jointly established the Codex Alimentarius Commission (CAC)?**

(a) The World Trade Organization (WTO)
(b) The United Nations Environment Programme (UNEP)
(c) The World Health Organization (WHO) and the Food and Agriculture Organization (FAO)
(d) The International Monetary Fund (IMF) and the World Bank

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The Codex Alimentarius Commission (CAC) is a crucial international body setting food standards.  Understanding its establishment is crucial for comprehending global food safety regulations.  The question tests factual recall of the organizations involved in creating the CAC. The WTO, UNEP, IMF, and World Bank are significant international organizations but are not involved in the CAC's establishment.  WHO and FAO's joint role highlights the interdisciplinary nature of food safety, encompassing public health and agricultural production.  The correct answer underscores the importance of international collaboration in regulating food standards and protecting consumer health.


**4. Which of the following is NOT a key amendment introduced in the Water (Prevention and Control of Pollution) Amendment Act, 2024?**

(a) The Central government will prescribe the manner of nomination for the State Pollution Control Boards (SPCB) chairman.
(b)  Several violations have been decriminalized, with penalties replacing imprisonment.
(c) The Act now applies to all states regardless of whether they passed a resolution to amend it.
(d) The Centre can appoint adjudication officers to determine penalties.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question tests understanding of specific legislative changes. Options (a), (b), and (d) accurately reflect key amendments introduced in the Water (Prevention and Control of Pollution) Amendment Act, 2024, shifting power from states to the central government, decriminalizing certain offences, and establishing a central adjudication process.  However, option (c) is incorrect. While the central government now has more power, the act's application remains contingent on states passing resolutions to adopt it.  This reflects the federal structure of India's governance.  The incorrect option highlights a crucial nuance in the legislative process and tests the ability to critically evaluate the details of the amendment.


**5. Which organization launched the Preparedness and Resilience For Emerging Threats (PRET) initiative?**

(a) The United Nations Development Programme (UNDP)
(b) The World Health Organization (WHO)
(c) The World Bank
(d) The International Monetary Fund (IMF)

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** This question assesses knowledge about global health initiatives.  The PRET initiative aims to improve pandemic preparedness, focusing on disease prevention and response.  The WHO, as the leading global public health authority, is the logical and correct entity to have launched this initiative.  The UNDP, World Bank, and IMF, while involved in international development and economic stability, do not have the primary mandate for global health initiatives like PRET. The correct answer demonstrates an understanding of the roles and responsibilities of major international organizations in global health security.


**6. Which of the following is NOT a key finding of the Indian Landslide Susceptibility Map (ILSM)?**

(a) Sikkim has the highest percentage of land area susceptible to landslides.
(b) Arunachal Pradesh has the highest absolute area susceptible to landslides.
(c) Kerala has the lowest percentage of land area susceptible to landslides among non-Himalayan regions.
(d) Approximately 13.17% of India's geographical area is susceptible to landslides.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**  The question tests the ability to recall specific data from a report.  Options (a), (b), and (d) accurately reflect findings from the ILSM. However, option (c) is incorrect.  The ILSM indicates that Kerala, among non-Himalayan regions, exhibits the *highest*, not the lowest, area susceptible to landslides.  This incorrect option acts as a distractor, requiring careful attention to detail to identify the inaccuracy.  The question highlights the importance of understanding regional variations in landslide susceptibility across India.


**7.  The Triple Dip La Niña event of 2020-2023 was unusual because:**

(a) It caused extreme flooding across India.
(b) It was preceded by a strong El Niño event.
(c) It did not follow a strong El Niño event.
(d) It had no impact on India's air quality.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question assesses understanding of a specific climatic event and its atypical characteristics.  Options (a) and (d) are incorrect; the Triple Dip La Niña did impact India's weather patterns and air quality, although in a peculiar way described in the text. Option (b) is also incorrect; the text specifies the event was unusual *because* it was not preceded by a strong El Niño. Option (c) accurately captures the atypical feature of this La Niña event, making it the correct answer.  The explanation demonstrates an understanding of the El Niño Southern Oscillation (ENSO) and the interaction between different climatic phenomena.


**8. Which of the following is not a key component of the National Clean Air Programme (NCAP)?**

(a)  A target to achieve reductions of up to 40% of particulate matter concentrations by 2025-26.
(b) Implementation at the national level by the Central Pollution Control Board (CPCB).
(c)  City Action Plans (CAPs) implemented by the central government only.
(d)  The use of PRANA (Portal for Regulation of Air-pollution in NAC) to monitor implementation.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question tests comprehension of the NCAP's structure and implementation. Options (a), (b), and (d) accurately describe aspects of the NCAP's structure, targets, and monitoring mechanisms. However, option (c) is incorrect. The NCAP involves City Action Plans (CAPs) implemented collaboratively by state governments and their agencies at the state and city levels (municipal bodies), not solely by the central government. This demonstrates an understanding of the federal structure of environmental governance in India.  The incorrect option highlights a crucial detail regarding the implementation strategy of the NCAP.


**9.  Which of the following is NOT a responsibility mandated for local bodies under the Plastic Waste Management (Amendment) Rules, 2024?**

(a) Conducting an annual assessment of plastic waste generated.
(b) Developing infrastructure for waste segregation, collection, and processing.
(c)  Mandating producers to develop waste collection systems.
(d)  Submitting an annual report to the SPCB and PCC.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question evaluates understanding of specific regulations.  Options (a), (b), and (d) correctly identify responsibilities assigned to local bodies under the amended rules. However, option (c) is incorrect.  While producers have responsibilities under the EPR system, the amended rules do *not* mandate producers to develop waste collection systems. This responsibility primarily lies with local bodies.  The incorrect option highlights a critical distinction in the allocation of responsibilities for plastic waste management.  The question tests detailed understanding of the regulatory framework.


**10. Which of the following is NOT an initiative launched by the India Meteorological Department (IMD)?**

(a) National Framework of Climate Services (NFCS)
(b) Weather Analysis and Forecast Enabling System (WAFES)
(c) Panchayat Mausam Sewa Portal
(d)  Global Framework for Climate Services (GFCS)

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The question assesses understanding of IMD's activities. Options (a), (b), and (c) correctly identify initiatives launched by the IMD.  However, option (d) is incorrect. The Global Framework for Climate Services (GFCS) is an initiative launched by the World Meteorological Organization (WMO), not the IMD.  The IMD's National Framework of Climate Services (NFCS) is based on the GFCS but is a separate, India-specific initiative.  The incorrect option tests knowledge of the distinction between global and national climate service frameworks.

**1.  A novel low-pungency mustard variety, developed by Indian researchers, achieved a glucosinolate level comparable to Canola. Which genetic engineering technique was primarily employed in its creation?**

(a)  Genetically Modified Organism (GMO) technology using Bacillus thuringiensis
(b)  Genome Editing (GE) using CRISPR/Cas9 technology
(c)  Recombinant DNA technology involving Bacillus amyloliquefaciens genes
(d)  Traditional cross-breeding methods between Varuna and Early Heera-2 varieties


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly states that the new mustard variety was produced through gene editing of the ‘Varuna’ variety using CRISPR/Cas9 technology.  This technique directly modifies existing genes within the organism, unlike GMO technology which introduces foreign genes. Option (a) is incorrect as it refers to Bt cotton, a different GMO application. Option (c) describes the approach used in developing GM Mustard DMH-11, a distinct process. Option (d) is incorrect because while Varuna was used as a base variety, the low pungency was achieved through gene editing, not solely traditional breeding.  The question tests factual recall and understanding of the differences between various genetic engineering techniques.  The ability to differentiate between GE and GMO is crucial for UPSC aspirants.


**2.  Which type of battery, known for its high energy density and widespread use in electric vehicles, recently saw its co-inventor, John Bannister Goodenough, pass away?**

(a)  Lead-Acid (PbA) battery
(b)  Sodium-Sulfur (Na-S) battery
(c)  Lithium-Ion (Li-ion) battery
(d)  Nickel-Cadmium (Ni-Cd) battery


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage directly links John Bannister Goodenough's passing with the Lithium-Ion (Li-ion) battery.  It highlights Goodenough's contribution to developing a lithium battery with a cobalt oxide cathode. Options (a), (b), and (d) are other battery types discussed but not associated with Goodenough's work. This question tests factual recall, linking a significant figure in science to a specific technological development.  Knowing about key scientists and their contributions is important for the UPSC exam.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on Science and Technology,  meeting the specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging and requires a deep understanding of the subject matter.


**1.  A recent study highlighted the use of a specific isotope in radiometric dating, offering an alternative to a more commonly used but limited method.  Which isotope and its associated technique were featured in this research?**

(a) Potassium-40 and Argon-40 dating
(b) Carbon-14 and Accelerator Mass Spectrometry
(c) Calcium-41 and Atom-Trap Trace Analysis
(d) Uranium-238 and Lead-206 dating

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question focuses on a specific, less widely known application of radiometric dating.  While (a), (b), and (d) are established radiometric dating techniques, the passage highlights the use of Calcium-41 and the Atom-Trap Trace Analysis (ATTA) technique as a novel approach to overcome limitations associated with Carbon-14 dating, particularly its inability to date materials older than approximately 50,000 years.  The other options, while valid dating methods, do not address the specific focus of the research described in the passage.  The use of Calcium-41 represents a significant advancement in the field, making (c) the correct and most relevant answer.  The explanation emphasizes the novelty and importance of the research, aligning with UPSC's focus on current scientific advancements.


**2.  A new variety of mustard, developed using a specific gene-editing technology, has reduced pungency compared to its high-yielding predecessor. What technology was used and what specific component was targeted to achieve this reduction?**

(a) TALEN technology, targeting sinigrin levels
(b) CRISPR/Cas9 technology, targeting glucosinolate content
(c) ZFN technology, targeting myrosinase activity
(d) RNA interference, targeting lipid biosynthesis

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The question tests factual recall and conceptual understanding of genome editing techniques in agriculture. The passage specifically mentions the use of CRISPR/Cas9 technology to reduce the pungency of Indian mustard.  The reduction in pungency is achieved by lowering the glucosinolate content, a key component responsible for the pungent flavor.  Options (a), (c), and (d) represent alternative gene-editing techniques or target different metabolic pathways, making them incorrect.  The correct answer highlights the specific technology and the precise target molecule, demonstrating a thorough understanding of the scientific process involved.


**3.  Which of the following accurately describes the composition and function of a specific type of nanoparticle highlighted for its potential in cancer treatment and detection?**

(a) Iron oxide nanoparticles, enhancing MRI contrast
(b) Gold and copper sulfide nanohybrids, exhibiting photoacoustic and photothermal properties
(c) Silver nanoparticles, exhibiting antimicrobial properties
(d) Quantum dots, exhibiting fluorescence for targeted imaging

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** This question assesses the ability to understand the applications of nanotechnology in biomedicine.  The passage details research using gold and copper sulfide nanohybrids. These nanohybrids possess both photoacoustic and photothermal properties, allowing for both detection (via ultrasound waves generated upon light absorption) and treatment (via heat-induced cell death). Options (a), (c), and (d) describe other nanoparticles with different applications, but none possess the combination of photoacoustic and photothermal properties described in the passage.  The question demands precise knowledge of the nanomaterial's composition and its dual functionalities, making it a challenging yet relevant question for the UPSC exam.


**4.  The Indian Space Research Organisation (ISRO) has made significant strides in developing various launch vehicles. Which of the following ISRO launch vehicles utilizes a unique 3D-printed engine?**

(a) Polar Satellite Launch Vehicle (PSLV)
(b) Geosynchronous Satellite Launch Vehicle Mk III (GSLV Mk III)
(c) Small Satellite Launch Vehicle (SSLV)
(d) Agnibaan SubOrbital Technological Demonstrator (SOrTeD)

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**  This question tests knowledge of India's space program and its technological advancements. The passage explicitly mentions Agnibaan SOrTeD, a suborbital technological demonstrator developed by AgniKul Cosmos, as utilizing an entirely 3D-printed, single-piece, semi-cryogenic engine called the Agnilet engine. The other options, while significant ISRO launch vehicles, do not utilize 3D-printed engines in the manner described.  The question highlights a specific technological innovation and its association with a particular launch vehicle, demanding precise recall of information related to recent developments in the Indian space program.


**5.  A recent report highlighted the use of a specific technology for enhancing oil recovery from depleted reservoirs.  What is this technology and what is its added environmental benefit?**

(b) Steam injection, reducing viscosity

(d) Microbial enhanced oil recovery, utilizing microorganisms

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** This question tests the understanding of both oil recovery techniques and environmental concerns related to energy production. The passage mentions the use of supercritical carbon dioxide for enhanced oil recovery (EOR). The key point is that this method has the added benefit of simultaneous carbon dioxide sequestration, addressing climate change concerns.  Other EOR methods (a), (b), and (d) do not inherently address carbon dioxide emissions in this manner. The question requires careful understanding of the different techniques and their environmental implications, making it a challenging question that aligns well with UPSC's emphasis on sustainable development and environmental issues.


**6.  The World Health Organization (WHO) released updated guidelines for a specific substance, aiming to prevent certain chronic diseases. What substance is this and what are the key recommendations?**

(c) Sodium, reducing daily intake to less than 2000 mg

The passage refers to the WHO's updated global sodium benchmarks, specifically recommending a daily intake of less than 2000 mg of sodium for adults. While the WHO has guidelines for trans fats, sugar, and artificial sweeteners (options a, b, and d), the passage directly addresses the updated sodium benchmarks, and their role in preventing chronic conditions like high blood pressure.  The question demands precise knowledge of the WHO's recommendations regarding a specific nutrient and its impact on public health.



**7.  A specific type of bird flu outbreak prompted significant action in Kerala. What type of avian influenza was involved, and which national action plan was activated in response?**

While other types of avian influenza exist (options b, c, and d), the passage specifically connects the Kerala outbreak to the activation of the national action plan for HPAI, highlighting the severity of the situation. **9.  A new initiative aims to improve the management of a specific type of waste in India.  What type of waste is this, and what governmental body is primarily responsible for its regulation?**

**10. A recent study revealed a relationship between a specific food index and the risk of certain chronic diseases. What is this index, the diseases linked to it, and what factors influence it?**

Options (a), (c), and (d) are other relevant indices, but they do not fully capture the relationship between the index, the specific diseases mentioned, and the factors that influence it, as detailed in the passage. Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on science and technology.  Each question is designed to be challenging and assess various cognitive skills, with detailed explanations provided.


**1.  A novel rechargeable battery system utilizes tanks of electrolyte and a membrane to control electron flow, employing pumps to manage electrolyte circulation. This describes which type of battery energy storage system?**

(a) Standard (non-flow) battery
(b) Redox Flow Battery (RFB)
(c) Lithium-ion battery
(d) Sodium-Sulfur (Na-S) battery

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The question describes a flow battery, specifically highlighting the key characteristics of using tanks of electrolyte, a membrane for electron flow control, and pumps for electrolyte circulation.  Redox Flow Batteries (RFBs) precisely fit this description.  Standard batteries, as the name suggests, do not utilize this flow mechanism; they rely on electrodes immersed in an electrolyte. Lithium-ion and Sodium-Sulfur batteries are both examples of standard (non-flow) batteries, although they differ in their chemical composition and operation. Thus, option (b) is the most appropriate and accurate answer. Options (a), (c), and (d) represent different battery chemistries but not the specific flow-based design described in the question.


**2.  A material exhibits zero electrical resistance below a critical temperature, a phenomenon where electrons pair up into Cooper pairs, gliding unimpeded through the material's lattice. This describes which property?**

(a)  Magnetoresistance
(b)  Thermoelectricity
(c)  Superconductivity
(d)  Semiconductivity

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description perfectly defines superconductivity. The key features mentioned—zero resistance below a critical temperature and the formation of Cooper pairs enabling unimpeded electron flow—are hallmarks of superconductivity. Magnetoresistance refers to changes in electrical resistance due to magnetic fields. Thermoelectricity involves converting heat into electrical energy and vice versa. Semiconductivity describes materials with conductivity between conductors and insulators. Therefore, only superconductivity aligns with the given characteristics.


**3. The process involving two light atomic nuclei combining to form a heavier nucleus, releasing substantial energy in a plasma state, is known as:**

(a) Nuclear Fission
(b) Nuclear Fusion
(c) Radioactive Decay
(d) Chain Reaction

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The detailed description accurately portrays nuclear fusion.  Nuclear fusion is the process of combining light atomic nuclei to produce a heavier nucleus, releasing a tremendous amount of energy.  This process typically occurs in a plasma state—a superheated, ionized gas.  Nuclear fission involves splitting a heavy nucleus into lighter ones. Radioactive decay is the spontaneous emission of particles from an unstable nucleus. A chain reaction is a self-sustaining series of nuclear fissions. Only nuclear fusion matches the description provided.


**4. Which of the following is NOT a type of semiconductor device mentioned in the provided text?**

(a) Diode
(b) Transistor
(c) Integrated Circuit (IC)
(d) Resistor

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The text explicitly mentions diodes, transistors, and integrated circuits (ICs) as semiconductor devices.  Resistors, while crucial components in electronic circuits, are not fundamentally semiconductor devices; they are typically made from materials with stable and predictable resistance. Diodes control the flow of current in one direction. Transistors act as switches or amplifiers. Integrated circuits combine many transistors and other components on a single chip.  Therefore, the resistor stands out as the only option not categorized as a semiconductor device in the given context.


**5.  The Indian Space Research Organisation (ISRO) developed a launch vehicle designed for cost-effectiveness, flexibility, and efficient multiple payload capacity, targeting the small satellite launch market. This describes which vehicle?**

(a) Polar Satellite Launch Vehicle (PSLV)
(b) Geosynchronous Satellite Launch Vehicle Mk III (GSLV Mk III)
(c) Small Satellite Launch Vehicle (SSLV)
(d) Reusable Launch Vehicle (RLV)

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question directly describes the Small Satellite Launch Vehicle (SSLV).  The passage highlights its design for cost-effectiveness, flexibility in accommodating multiple payloads, and its specific purpose of serving the growing small satellite launch market.  PSLV and GSLV Mk III are larger, more powerful rockets not designed primarily for this niche. The RLV is focused on reusability, a different design priority.  Therefore, the SSLV is the only option that precisely fits the description.


**6. Which of the following is NOT a method mentioned for producing lab-grown diamonds?**

(a) High Temperature High Pressure (HTHP) Method
(b) Chemical Vapor Deposition (CVD) Method
(c)  Hydrothermal Synthesis
(d) Laser Ablation

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The text specifically mentions High Temperature High Pressure (HTHP) and Chemical Vapor Deposition (CVD) as methods for producing lab-grown diamonds. While other techniques exist for creating synthetic diamonds, the provided text does not include hydrothermal synthesis or laser ablation.  Therefore, option (c) represents a method not explicitly mentioned within the provided material regarding lab-grown diamond production.


**7.  A type of rechargeable flow battery that uses vanadium ions as active materials, characterized by a longer lifespan but higher initial installation costs, is known as:**

(a) Lithium-ion battery
(b) Sodium-ion battery
(c) Vanadium Redox Flow Battery (VRFB)
(d)  Lead-acid battery

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description accurately defines a Vanadium Redox Flow Battery (VRFB).  The text clearly states that VRFBs use vanadium ions, have a longer lifespan than other types like lithium-ion, and are associated with higher initial installation costs.  Lithium-ion, sodium-ion, and lead-acid batteries do not share these specific characteristics. Therefore, only the VRFB matches the given description.


**8.  A group of 17 silvery-white, soft, heavy metals that occur together in the periodic table, possessing luminescent and catalytic properties crucial for high-end technology and clean energy applications, are collectively known as:**

(a)  Transition Metals
(b)  Actinides
(c)  Rare Earth Elements (REEs)
(d)  Alkaline Earth Metals

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description precisely identifies Rare Earth Elements (REEs). The text explicitly mentions the group of 17 elements, their silvery-white appearance, soft and heavy nature, and their shared occurrence in the periodic table.  Their luminescent and catalytic properties are also highlighted as key to their applications in various technologies, including clean energy.  Transition metals, actinides, and alkaline earth metals do not possess this unique combination of properties and applications.  Therefore, only REEs perfectly fit the given description.


**9. The Indian government established an autonomous business division under Digital India Corporation to oversee the implementation of programs aimed at developing the semiconductor and display manufacturing ecosystem. This refers to:**

(a)  Ministry of Electronics and Information Technology (MeitY)
(b)  India Semiconductor Mission (ISM)
(c)  Bureau of Indian Standards (BIS)
(d)  National Institute of Technology (NIT)

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The text explicitly describes the India Semiconductor Mission (ISM) as the autonomous business division established under Digital India Corporation to manage the programs for developing the semiconductor and display manufacturing ecosystem.  MeitY is a broader ministry, BIS focuses on standardization, and NITs are educational institutions; none of these directly match the described role.  Therefore, only the ISM correctly identifies the entity responsible for implementing the government's semiconductor development programs.


**10. A process of altering the DNA of organisms using site-directed nucleases (SDNs) to make changes such as deletions, substitutions, or additions of nucleotides, is known as:**

(a)  Gene Cloning
(b)  Polymerase Chain Reaction (PCR)
(c)  Genome Editing
(d)  DNA Fingerprinting

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The detailed description defines genome editing.  The use of site-directed nucleases (SDNs) to modify DNA sequences through deletions, substitutions, or nucleotide additions is a core principle of genome editing techniques.  Gene cloning involves producing identical copies of a gene. PCR is a technique for amplifying DNA sequences.  DNA fingerprinting involves analyzing DNA variations for identification purposes. Only genome editing aligns with the described process of targeted DNA modification using SDNs.



Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  The questions aim for a difficult level, demanding precise factual recall and conceptual understanding.


**1.  A novel method for altering an organism's DNA, employing site-directed nucleases (SDNs) to effect changes like deletions, substitutions, or nucleotide additions, is described as:**

(a)  Gene sequencing
(b)  Genome editing
(c)  Gene-drive technology
(d)  Three-parent baby technology

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The question describes genome editing, a precise technique using SDNs to modify DNA. Gene sequencing determines the order of nucleotides, gene-drive technology is a specific application of genome editing, and "three-parent baby" technology refers to mitochondrial replacement therapy.  Genome editing is the broader, encompassing term fitting the description.  The options are designed to be closely related to confuse the candidate, testing their precise understanding of the nuances in biotechnology terminology.


**2. Which technology, crucial for modernizing election processes, utilizes a portable microcontroller-based instrument with a ballot unit, control unit, and a verifiable paper audit trail (VVPAT) for enhanced transparency and voter confidence?**

(a) VVPAT-only system
(b) Electronic Voting Machine (EVM) system
(c)  Blockchain-based voting system
(d)  Biometric authentication system

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The description clearly points to the EVM system, which incorporates the ballot unit, control unit, and VVPAT. While VVPAT is a component, it's not the entire system. Blockchain and biometrics are separate technologies used in various aspects of elections but don't fully encapsulate the described system. The question tests the candidate's knowledge of election technology and their ability to identify the core technology from a detailed description.


**3.  The colorless, odorless, non-flammable, non-corrosive, and extremely cold cryogenic fluid used in food freezing and cryotherapy, but posing risks of cold burns and frostbite if mishandled, is:**

(a)  Methanol
(b)  Ethylene
(c)  Liquid nitrogen
(d)  Carbon dioxide

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description precisely matches the properties and applications of liquid nitrogen. Methanol, ethylene, and carbon dioxide possess different characteristics and applications. The inclusion of the harmful effects acts as a distractor, testing the candidate's complete understanding, not just the common applications.


**4. A measure quantifying how rapidly a carbohydrate-rich food elevates blood sugar levels after consumption, ranking foods on a scale of 0 to 100 relative to pure glucose (GI 100), is known as:**

(a)  Glycemic Load
(b)  Glycemic Index
(c)  Insulin Sensitivity Index
(d)  Blood Glucose Response

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The detailed description defines the Glycemic Index (GI). Glycemic Load (GL) uses GI but adds carbohydrate quantity.  The other options are related to blood sugar but don't precisely match the described metric. The question demands precise knowledge of a specific nutritional index and its definition.


**5. The infectious viral disease primarily affecting cattle, characterized by fever and skin nodules, sometimes leading to death and reduced milk yield, and transmitted by blood-feeding insects, is:**

(a)  Avian influenza
(b)  Swine flu
(c)  Lumpy skin disease
(d)  Meningitis

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description exactly fits Lumpy Skin Disease (LSD). Avian influenza and swine flu affect birds and pigs respectively. Meningitis is an inflammation of brain and spinal cord tissues. The question tests the candidate's knowledge of specific animal diseases and their transmission vectors.


**6.  A non-invasive medical imaging test employing a large magnet and radio waves to produce detailed images of internal structures without ionizing radiation is known as:**

(a)  Computed Tomography (CT) scan
(b)  Positron Emission Tomography (PET) scan
(c)  X-ray
(d)  Magnetic Resonance Imaging (MRI)

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The description accurately portrays MRI. CT, PET scans, and X-rays use ionizing radiation or different imaging principles. The question assesses the candidate's understanding of medical imaging technologies and their underlying mechanisms.


**7.  The method of establishing the age of an object based on the presence of a radioactive isotope and its decay rate, exemplified by carbon-14 dating, is termed:**

(a)  Chronological dating
(b)  Radiometric dating
(c)  Dendrochronology
(d)  Stratigraphic dating

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The question describes radiometric dating. Chronological dating is a broad term. Dendrochronology uses tree rings, and stratigraphic dating relies on rock layers. The question tests the candidate's understanding of different dating methods in archaeology and geology.


**8.  An international food standards body jointly established by the World Health Organization (WHO) and the Food and Agriculture Organization (FAO), headquartered in Rome, with the objective of protecting consumer health and ensuring fair practices in food trade, is the:**

(a)  World Trade Organization (WTO)
(b)  Food Safety and Standards Authority of India (FSSAI)
(c)  Codex Alimentarius Commission (CAC)
(d)  International Organization for Standardization (ISO)

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description perfectly fits the Codex Alimentarius Commission (CAC). WTO deals with international trade, FSSAI is India's food safety body, and ISO focuses on standardization. The question tests the candidate's knowledge of international organizations related to food safety and trade.


**9. A process where two light atomic nuclei combine to form a heavier nucleus, releasing substantial energy, occurring in a hot, charged gas called plasma, is:**

(a)  Nuclear fission
(b)  Nuclear fusion
(c)  Radioactive decay
(d)  Chain reaction

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The description defines nuclear fusion. Nuclear fission is the splitting of a nucleus. Radioactive decay involves spontaneous emission of particles, and a chain reaction is a self-sustaining series of nuclear reactions.  The question tests the candidate's knowledge of nuclear processes.


**10.  The technology involving the cultivation of undifferentiated plant cells, tissues, or organs on synthetic media under aseptic conditions, leveraging the totipotency of plant cells, is known as:**

(a)  Hydroponics
(b)  Aeroponics
(c)  Plant tissue culture
(d)  Genetic engineering

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description defines plant tissue culture. Hydroponics and aeroponics are soilless cultivation methods. Genetic engineering involves direct manipulation of genes. The question tests the candidate's understanding of plant propagation techniques.


**11.  A rechargeable battery where lithium ions move between electrodes during discharge and recharge, utilizing materials like lithium cobalt oxide and lithium manganese oxide, is a:**

(a)  Lead-acid battery
(b)  Nickel-cadmium battery
(c)  Lithium-ion battery
(d)  Sodium-ion battery

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description clearly points to a lithium-ion battery. Lead-acid, nickel-cadmium, and sodium-ion batteries use different chemistries. The question tests the candidate's knowledge of battery technologies.


**12. Advanced nuclear reactors with power generation capacities ranging from less than 30 MWe to 300+ MWe, characterized by small size, modular design, and factory assembly for transportation and installation, are called:**

(a)  Pressurized water reactors
(b)  Boiling water reactors
(c)  Small modular reactors (SMRs)
(d)  Fast breeder reactors

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description fits the characteristics of Small Modular Reactors (SMRs). The other reactor types have different designs and scales.  The question tests the candidate's knowledge of nuclear power plant technology.


**13.  The manipulation or deception of a GPS receiver by broadcasting false signals, thereby compromising the reliability of GPS data, is known as:**

(a)  GPS jamming
(b)  GPS spoofing
(c)  GNSS interference
(d)  Satellite hacking

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The description defines GPS spoofing. GPS jamming blocks signals. GNSS interference is a broader term, and satellite hacking encompasses various cyberattacks. The question tests the candidate's knowledge of GPS vulnerabilities and cyberattacks.


**14. A type of malicious software secretly installed on a device to monitor or steal sensitive information, often used for targeted surveillance and data theft, is known as:**

(a)  Virus
(b)  Worm
(c)  Trojan
(d)  Spyware

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The description accurately defines spyware. Viruses, worms, and Trojans are different types of malware with distinct characteristics. The question tests the candidate's knowledge of cybersecurity threats.


**15. The collection and publication of an individual's private information online, often with the intent to shame or harass, is referred to as:**

(a)  Phishing
(b)  Doxxing
(c)  Cyberstalking
(d)  Identity theft

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The description defines doxxing. Phishing involves deceptive emails. Cyberstalking involves online harassment, and identity theft is the unauthorized use of personal information. The question tests the candidate's awareness of online harassment and privacy violations.


**16. The environment surrounding Earth and other celestial bodies, primarily influenced by solar activities like solar flares and coronal mass ejections (CMEs), impacting technological systems and potentially endangering astronauts, is:**

(a)  Earth's atmosphere
(b)  Magnetosphere
(c)  Space weather
(d)  Solar wind

**17. A constellation of low Earth orbit (LEO) satellites providing global internet coverage, particularly in remote areas, and created by SpaceX, is:**

(a)  OneWeb
(b)  Iridium

**18.  A directed energy weapon (DEW) system generating beams of electromagnetic energy across a broad spectrum of radio and microwave frequencies, potentially damaging or disrupting electronics in targeted systems, is a:**

(a)  Laser weapon
(b)  High-powered microwave (HPM) weapon

**19. A surface-to-air missile featuring an active electronically scanned array (AESA) multi-function radar for search, track, and fire control, capable of intercepting high-speed aerial threats, is the:**

**20. An external combustion engine operating on the principle of compression and expansion to convert thermal energy into mechanical energy, sometimes used to power high-powered microwave weapons, is a:**

(b)  Jet engine
(c)  Rocket engine
(d)  Stirling engine
