Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be difficult, requiring precise factual recall and conceptual understanding.


**1.  A colorless, odorless, non-flammable, non-corrosive, and extremely cold element used in food preservation and cryotherapy is associated with which of the following potential hazards?**

(a)  Increased risk of cardiovascular diseases due to altered lipid metabolism.
(b)  Development of antimicrobial resistance due to its interaction with microorganisms.
(c)  Cold burns and frostbite due to rapid freezing of skin tissue and eye fluid.
(d)  Induction of genetic mutations through interactions with cellular DNA.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description clearly points to liquid nitrogen.  Liquid nitrogen, with its extremely low temperature (-196 °C), poses a significant risk of cold burns and frostbite if it comes into direct contact with human tissue. The rapid freezing effect can cause severe damage to skin and eyes. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect. Liquid nitrogen's primary use is in cryogenic applications and food preservation; it doesn't directly cause cardiovascular issues, antimicrobial resistance, or genetic mutations in the described context.  The question tests factual recall of the properties and hazards associated with liquid nitrogen as described in the target text.


**2.  Which of the following substances, when found in hand sanitizers, has been linked to severe health consequences, including permanent blindness and death?**

(a)  Ethylene, a gas used in artificial fruit ripening.
(b)  Methanol, a volatile liquid also used in the production of certain chemicals.
(c)  Sodium, a mineral found in various food categories and linked to hypertension.
(d)  Glycerol, a byproduct of biodiesel production and a common humectant.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The question highlights the recall of a specific news item regarding methanol's toxicity. Methanol (CH3OH), also known as wood alcohol, has been identified as a dangerous contaminant in hand sanitizers.  Ingestion or absorption of methanol can lead to severe health complications, including nausea, coma, seizures, blindness, central nervous system damage, and death.  Ethylene, sodium, and glycerol, while having various applications, are not associated with these specific severe health consequences from hand sanitizer contamination.  The question tests factual recall of a specific news item and the associated chemical substance.


**3.  A recent scientific study highlighted the correlation between a specific food index and the risk of Type II diabetes and cardiovascular diseases. This index is a measure of how quickly which of the following raises blood sugar levels?**

(a)  Lipids, a type of fat found in food.
(b)  Proteins, the building blocks of cells and tissues.
(c)  Carbohydrates, the body's main source of energy.
(d)  Fiber, a type of indigestible carbohydrate.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question focuses on the Glycemic Index (GI). The GI is a measure of how quickly carbohydrate-containing foods raise blood sugar levels after consumption.  The passage specifically links high GI foods to increased risks of Type II diabetes and cardiovascular diseases.  While lipids, proteins, and fiber are components of food that influence metabolism, the GI specifically focuses on the rate at which carbohydrates increase blood sugar levels.  The question tests conceptual understanding of the Glycemic Index and its relation to specific food components.


**4.  The World Health Organization (WHO) launched a network of global laboratories for early detection and monitoring of specific viruses.  This network, CoViNet, prioritizes surveillance of which of the following virus types?**

(a)  Influenza A viruses, responsible for avian influenza.
(b)  Meningococcal bacteria, causing meningitis.
(c)  Coronaviruses, including SARS-CoV-2 and MERS-CoV.
(d)  Retroviruses, a class of RNA viruses that include HIV.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question demands knowledge of CoViNet's focus. CoViNet, the Coronavirus Network, is a global collaboration of laboratories focused on the early detection, monitoring, and assessment of coronaviruses, including SARS-CoV-2 (the virus causing COVID-19) and MERS-CoV. The other options are incorrect. While influenza A viruses, meningococcal bacteria, and retroviruses are important pathogens, they are not the primary focus of CoViNet. The question tests factual recall of the WHO initiative and its specific viral targets.


**5.  A rare, long-lived radioisotope with a half-life of 99,400 years, produced by cosmic ray interactions in soil, is being explored for radiometric dating.  This isotope is:**

(a)  Carbon-14, commonly used in dating organic materials.
(b)  Potassium-40, used in dating rocks and minerals.
(c)  Calcium-41, a recently studied alternative for radiometric dating.
(d)  Uranium-238, used in dating very old geological formations.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question hinges on a specific radioisotope. The passage describes Calcium-41 as a rare, long-lived radioisotope with a half-life of 99,400 years.  Its use in radiometric dating, along with the method Atom-Trap Trace Analysis (ATTA), is highlighted. Carbon-14, Potassium-40, and Uranium-238 are also used in radiometric dating, but the question specifically targets the lesser-known Calcium-41 and its properties as described. The question tests factual recall of a specific isotope and its application.


**6. The use of which of the following substances as an incendiary agent in military ammunition, while not banned, is considered a war crime if used in civilian areas?**

(a)  Tantalum, a rare metal with high corrosion resistance.
(b)  Supercritical carbon dioxide, used in enhanced oil recovery.
(c)  White phosphorus, a chemical that spontaneously catches fire in air.
(d)  Graphene, an allotrope of carbon with various applications.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question focuses on the controversial use of white phosphorus.  The text explicitly mentions white phosphorus's use as an incendiary agent in military ammunition and highlights that while its use isn't banned, employing it in populated civilian areas is considered a war crime.  The other options are incorrect.  Tantalum, supercritical carbon dioxide, and graphene have industrial and scientific applications but are not directly linked to this specific war crime context. The question tests factual recall of a specific chemical's military use and its ethical considerations.


**7.  Which of the following battery types utilizes sodium ions as charge carriers, offering advantages of abundance and lower cost compared to its more widely used counterpart?**

(a)  Lithium-ion battery, currently dominant in rechargeable energy storage.
(b)  Sand battery, using sand to store thermal energy.
(c)  Sodium-ion battery, a promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries.
(d)  Biofuel-based battery, using organic materials for energy storage.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question centers on the comparison of battery technologies. The passage directly contrasts sodium-ion batteries with lithium-ion batteries, highlighting the advantages of sodium-ion batteries in terms of cost and the abundance of sodium.  Sand batteries store thermal energy, not electrochemical energy, and biofuel-based batteries are not described in the given text. The question tests conceptual understanding of different battery types and their comparative advantages.


**8.  The transesterification process is primarily associated with the production of which of the following biofuels?**

(a)  Ethanol, an alcohol used as a petrol substitute.
(b)  Biodiesel, a renewable alternative to conventional diesel.
(c)  Biogas, produced from the anaerobic digestion of organic matter.
(d)  Hydrogen, a clean energy source with various applications.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The question tests the knowledge of biofuel production methods.  The passage clearly states that transesterification is the chemical process used to convert vegetable oils or animal fats into fatty acid methyl esters (FAMEs), which is biodiesel. Ethanol production involves fermentation, biogas is produced through anaerobic digestion, and hydrogen production involves various methods including electrolysis. The question tests factual recall of a specific biofuel production method.


**9.  Which of the following is NOT a key component of a lithium-ion battery?**

(a)  Graphite, used as the anode material.
(b)  Lithium oxide, often used in the cathode.
(c)  Electrolyte, facilitating ion movement between electrodes.
(d)  Sodium ions, crucial for charge transport.


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The question assesses understanding of lithium-ion battery components.  The passage details the components of lithium-ion batteries, including graphite anode, lithium oxide cathode, and electrolyte.  Sodium ions are the charge carriers in sodium-ion batteries, not lithium-ion batteries. The question tests factual recall of battery components and differentiates between similar battery technologies.



**10.  Which of the following statements accurately describes a key characteristic of graphene?**

(a) It is a poor conductor of heat and electricity.
(b) It has low surface area, limiting its applications.
(c) It exhibits poor biocompatibility, restricting its biomedical use.
(d) It possesses high surface area and excellent thermal conductivity.


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The question focuses on the properties of graphene. The passage explicitly describes graphene as having a high surface area, good biocompatibility, strong mechanical strength, excellent thermal conductivity, and fast electron transportation. Options (a), (b), and (c) contradict these stated properties. The question tests factual recall of graphene's key properties.


Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging and requires a detailed understanding of the concepts.


**1.  A celestial phenomenon characterized by brief, intense bursts of radio waves lasting mere milliseconds, often originating from distant galaxies and exhibiting frequency dispersion during their interstellar journey.  Which of the following best describes this phenomenon?**

(a) Gamma-Ray Burst (GRB)
(b) Quasi-Moon
(c) Fast Radio Burst (FRB)
(d) Blazar


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description perfectly matches the characteristics of a Fast Radio Burst (FRB).  FRBs are extremely short-lived and powerful bursts of radio waves detected from extragalactic sources. The mention of frequency dispersion is a crucial characteristic of FRBs, caused by the interaction of the radio waves with the interstellar medium.  Gamma-ray bursts are high-energy events, while quasi-moons are asteroids with unique orbital characteristics around Earth. Blazars are active galactic nuclei powered by supermassive black holes, emitting high-energy radiation across the electromagnetic spectrum, but not characterized by the millisecond duration and frequency dispersion mentioned in the question stem.


**2.  A type of galaxy powered by a supermassive black hole and known for its exceptionally bright and energetic emissions, often observed by astronomical observatories like the Indian Astronomical Observatory in Hanle, Ladakh. Which term correctly identifies this type of galaxy?**

(a) Quasi-satellite
(b) Blazar
(c) Coronal Hole
(d) Pulsar


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The description clearly points to a blazar.  Blazars are a specific type of active galactic nuclei (AGN) powered by supermassive black holes, known for their extreme brightness and powerful emissions across the electromagnetic spectrum. The mention of the Indian Astronomical Observatory observing a blazar further strengthens this identification.  Quasi-satellites are asteroids with specific orbital relationships to a planet. Coronal holes are regions on the Sun’s corona, and pulsars are rotating neutron stars emitting beams of radiation.


**3. An independent navigation satellite system developed by ISRO, providing coverage over India and extending up to 1500 km beyond its boundaries, offering both standard and restricted services.  What is the name of this navigation system?**

(a) GAGAN
(b) NavIC
(c) GPS
(d) GLONASS


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The question describes NavIC (Navigation with Indian Constellation), India's indigenous navigation satellite system. Its coverage area, services offered (Standard Position Service and Restricted Service), and developer (ISRO) all align with the description.  GAGAN is a GPS augmentation system, while GPS and GLONASS are foreign navigation systems.


**4.  A phenomenon occurring in locations between the tropics where, due to the Sun's position directly overhead, the shadows of vertical objects momentarily disappear. What is the name of this phenomenon?**

(a) Gravitational Lensing
(b) Zero Shadow Day
(c) Tidal Locking
(d) Solar Flare


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**  The description precisely defines a "Zero Shadow Day." This occurs when the Sun is directly overhead, resulting in the absence of shadows for vertically positioned objects. This phenomenon is specific to locations between the tropics and is related to the Sun's apparent movement throughout the year. Gravitational lensing is a phenomenon related to light bending around massive objects. Tidal locking describes the synchronization of a celestial body's rotation and orbital period. A solar flare is a sudden burst of energy from the Sun.


**5.  A region above and adjacent to national airspace, extending from approximately 18 km to 160 km above sea level, characterized by an atmosphere too thin for most aircraft but too dense for satellites to maintain stable orbits. What is this region called?**

(a) Exosphere
(b) Ionosphere
(c) Near-Space
(d) Magnetosphere


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description precisely defines "Near-Space." It's a region where the atmosphere is too thin for conventional aircraft but too dense for satellites to maintain stable orbits.  This makes it a unique operational domain for specialized technologies. The exosphere is the outermost layer of Earth's atmosphere. The ionosphere is a region where atmospheric gases are ionized by solar radiation. The magnetosphere is the region surrounding Earth dominated by its magnetic field.


**6. Which of the following is NOT a component of the Gaganyaan mission?**

(a) LVM3 launch vehicle
(b) Environmental Control and Life Support System (ECLSS)
(c) Semi-cryogenic engine CE-20
(d)  Navigation with Indian Constellation (NavIC)


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** While NavIC is an important Indian navigation system, it is not directly a component of the Gaganyaan mission itself. The Gaganyaan mission uses its own navigation and communication systems.  The LVM3, ECLSS, and the CE-20 cryogenic engine are all integral parts of the Gaganyaan mission's design and execution.


**7.  A project by the Virgo Consortium involving full-hydro large-scale structure simulations and all-sky mapping to interpret next-generation observations in cosmology. What is the name of this project?**

(a) FEAST
(b) LIGO-India
(c) FLAMINGO
(d)  Euclid Space Telescope


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description accurately reflects the FLAMINGO project.  The acronym and its focus on large-scale structure simulations, all-sky mapping, and interpretation of next-generation observations align perfectly with the provided details. FEAST is a finite element analysis software, LIGO-India is a gravitational wave observatory, and the Euclid Space Telescope is a space-based observatory for studying dark energy and dark matter.


**8. Which of the following best describes the primary function of a coronagraph?**

(a) To magnify light from distant objects.
(b) To block out intense light from a central object to observe fainter surrounding structures.
(c) To study the elemental composition of celestial bodies.
(d) To detect and measure gravitational waves.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** A coronagraph's main purpose is to block the bright light from a central celestial object (like the Sun) to allow observation of fainter features in its corona or immediate surroundings. Telescopes generally magnify light, while spectrometers analyze elemental composition, and gravitational wave detectors measure gravitational waves.


**9.  The most detailed map of dark matter, created using data from the Atacama Cosmology Telescope (ACT), revealing insights into the universe's “lumpiness” and expansion rate, is based on which fundamental model of cosmology?**

(a) Big Crunch Model
(b) Steady-State Model
(c) Standard Model of Cosmology (SMC)
(d) Oscillating Universe Model


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description refers to the Standard Model of Cosmology (SMC). This model is the prevailing cosmological model that explains the universe's evolution from the Big Bang, incorporating dark matter and dark energy.  The map's findings corroborate predictions within the SMC.  The other options are alternative cosmological models that have been superseded by the SMC.


**10.  The region of a black hole beyond the event horizon, where spacetime is rotating due to the black hole's spin, is known as what?**

(a) Schwarzschild Radius
(b) Singularity
(c) Ergosphere
(d) Event Horizon


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The ergosphere is the region outside the event horizon of a rotating black hole where spacetime itself is dragged around by the black hole's rotation.  The Schwarzschild radius defines the event horizon's boundary. The singularity is the point of infinite density at the black hole's center. The event horizon is the boundary beyond which nothing, not even light, can escape.


Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on Science and Technology.  Each question is designed to be challenging and test a range of cognitive skills, with detailed explanations provided.


**1.  A recent study highlighted the potential of a specific isotope for radiometric dating, surpassing the limitations of Carbon-14.  Which isotope was this?**

(a) Potassium-40
(b) Uranium-238
(c) Calcium-41
(d) Argon-40

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly mentions a recent study demonstrating the use of Calcium-41 in radiometric dating as an alternative to Carbon-14, due to its longer half-life (99,400 years compared to Carbon-14's 5,700 years).  This makes it suitable for dating much older materials.  Potassium-40, Uranium-238, and Argon-40 are also used in radiometric dating, but the question specifically refers to a *recent* study highlighting an alternative to Carbon-14, making Calcium-41 the only correct answer.  The other options, while relevant to radiometric dating in general, do not address the specific advancement described in the passage.


**2. The National Green Hydrogen Mission in India aims to achieve a significant reduction in reliance on a particular type of energy import. What type of import is it primarily targeting to reduce?**

(a) Natural Gas
(b) Coal
(c) Crude Oil
(d) Uranium

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The National Hydrogen Mission's stated goals include reducing reliance on fossil fuel imports. While the mission is broader than just crude oil, the text explicitly mentions a projected reduction of over Rs. 1 lakh crore annually in fossil fuel imports.  Given the scale of India's crude oil imports, it is the most significant fossil fuel import the mission aims to impact. Natural gas and coal are also imported, but the emphasis on reducing import reliance by a substantial amount points directly to crude oil. Uranium is used in nuclear power, but it's not explicitly mentioned in the context of the Hydrogen Mission's import reduction goals.


**3.  A novel approach to pandemic preparedness, the PRET Initiative, utilizes a strategic framework for addressing infectious diseases. This approach centers on which key factor for categorization of pathogens?**

(a) Genetic Similarity
(b) Geographic Origin
(c) Mode of Transmission
(d) Severity of Symptoms

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description of the PRET initiative highlights its innovative approach by leveraging the same systems, capacities, knowledge, and tools for groups of pathogens based on their *mode of transmission*. This suggests a categorization based on respiratory, vector-borne, or foodborne transmission routes. While genetic similarity, geographic origin, and symptom severity might be considered in disease management, the core of the PRET Initiative's strategic framework, as described, lies in the categorization by transmission mode.


**4. The Food Safety and Standards Authority of India (FSSAI) has been instrumental in promoting the conversion of a specific waste product into a biofuel.  Which waste product is this?**

(a) Agricultural Residues
(b) Municipal Solid Waste
(c) Used Cooking Oil
(d) Industrial Wastewater

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage specifically mentions the FSSAI's initiative, "Repurpose Used Cooking Oil (RUCO),"  which aims to collect used cooking oil and convert it into biodiesel.  While agricultural residues and municipal solid waste can be used in biofuel production, the question directly links the FSSAI to a specific waste-to-biofuel program focused on used cooking oil. Industrial wastewater is not directly associated with this specific FSSAI initiative.


**5. Which technology, utilizing a specific type of wave, allows for both the detection and treatment of cancer cells, as described in a recent study?**

(a) Photoacoustic Imaging using ultrasound waves
(b) Magnetic Resonance Imaging (MRI)
(c) Positron Emission Tomography (PET) scan
(d) X-ray Computed Tomography (CT) scan

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:** The passage describes a study using hybrid nanoparticles that leverage photoacoustic properties.  These nanoparticles absorb light and generate ultrasound waves for detection, and also produce heat (photothermal property) for cancer cell treatment.  MRI, PET, and CT scans are imaging technologies, but they don't employ the combined photoacoustic and photothermal mechanisms using ultrasound waves as described in the study.


**6. The CRISPR/Cas9 gene editing technology has been successfully applied to a specific Indian crop, resulting in a variety with reduced pungency. Which crop is this?**

(a) Bt Cotton
(b) Indian Mustard
(c) Brinjal
(d) Rice

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The passage clearly states that Indian researchers developed a low-pungent mustard variety using CRISPR/Cas9 gene editing technology.  Bt cotton, brinjal, and rice are also subjects of genetic modification research, but the question specifically focuses on a successful application of CRISPR/Cas9 for reducing pungency in an Indian crop, which is Indian mustard.


**7.  A global organization jointly established by the WHO and FAO sets international food standards to protect consumer health and ensure fair trade practices. What is the name of this organization?**

(a) World Trade Organization (WTO)
(b) Food and Agriculture Organization (FAO)
(c) World Health Organization (WHO)
(d) Codex Alimentarius Commission (CAC)

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The passage describes the Codex Alimentarius Commission (CAC) as an international food standards body jointly established by the WHO and FAO.  While the WTO, FAO, and WHO are relevant organizations, only the CAC specifically fulfills the description of setting international food standards for consumer health and fair trade.


**8. The Indian government's initiative aimed at promoting electric vehicles and establishing charging infrastructure is known by what acronym?**

(a) NEMMP
(b) FAME
(c) GII
(d) GIP

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The passage mentions the FAME India Scheme (Faster Adoption and Manufacturing of (Hybrid &) Electric Vehicles) as a key policy mechanism under the National Electric Mobility Mission Plan (NEMMP) 2020.  While NEMMP is the overall plan, FAME is the specific scheme focused on electric vehicle adoption and infrastructure. The other options, GII (Gender Inequality Index) and GIP (Genome India Project), are unrelated initiatives.


**9. A rare blood clotting disorder, sometimes linked to a specific COVID-19 vaccine, is known by what acronym?**

(a) LSD
(b) TTS
(c) AMR
(d) VITT

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The passage mentions Thrombosis with Thrombocytopenia Syndrome (TTS), also known as Vaccine-induced Immune Thrombotic Thrombocytopenia (VITT), as a rare side effect associated with the AstraZeneca COVID-19 vaccine (Covishield).  LSD (Lumpy Skin Disease), AMR (Antimicrobial Resistance), and VITT (Vaccine-induced Immune Thrombotic Thrombocytopenia) are related to different health contexts. The question specifically asks for the acronym used in the passage, which is TTS.


**10.  A newly unveiled WHO digital health promoter prototype utilizes generative AI for public health information dissemination.  What is the name of this prototype?**

(a) COVINET
(b) S.A.R.A.H.
(c) SPECS 2030
(d) PRET

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The passage introduces S.A.R.A.H. (Smart AI Resource Assistant for Health) as a WHO prototype leveraging generative AI for public health information.  COVINET, SPECS 2030, and PRET are other WHO initiatives, but they are not AI-powered digital health promoters.


Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on difficult questions with detailed explanations.  The questions aim for a diverse range of cognitive skills and avoid simple factual recall where possible.


**1.  Concerning gene-editing technologies and their applications in agriculture, which statement is accurate?**

(a)  CRISPR/Cas9 technology exclusively introduces foreign genetic material into target organisms.
(b)  The Indian development of low-pungent mustard involved SDN3 methods, resulting in a genetically modified organism (GMO) distinct from conventionally bred varieties.
(c)  High glucosinolate levels in Indian mustard are beneficial for livestock health and pose no significant risks.
(d)  SDN1 and SDN2 gene-editing techniques always produce results indistinguishable from conventional breeding methods, regardless of the specific edits made.

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Option (d) is correct because SDN1 and SDN2 methods, by definition, do not involve the introduction of foreign genetic material. This makes the resulting genetic modifications essentially indistinguishable from those achievable through traditional breeding techniques.  However, the precise outcome depends heavily on the specific genes targeted and the nature of the edit. While aiming for indistinguishability, unforeseen consequences can still arise.

Option (a) is incorrect because CRISPR/Cas9 can be used for both gene knockouts (removing existing genes) and gene insertions (introducing new ones).  It's not limited to only introducing foreign genetic material.

Option (b) is incorrect because the low-pungent mustard development utilized CRISPR/Cas9, but the text specifically states that SDN1 and SDN2 methods *do not* involve alien genetic material and can lead to results indistinguishable from conventional breeding. The question implies a false dichotomy between SDN methods and GMOs.

Option (c) is incorrect because high glucosinolate levels in Indian mustard are explicitly linked to goiter and internal organ abnormalities in livestock, highlighting the need for the gene-editing effort.


**2. Regarding the James Webb Space Telescope (JWST) and its scientific capabilities, which statement is NOT true?**

(a)  The JWST operates primarily in the infrared spectrum.
(b)  The JWST's primary mirror is significantly larger than that of the Hubble Space Telescope.
(c)  The JWST is capable of directly imaging exoplanets with high resolution, easily distinguishing their atmospheric composition.
(d)  The JWST's location at the Sun-Earth L2 Lagrange point minimizes interference from Earth's light and heat.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) is incorrect because while the JWST can observe exoplanets, directly imaging them with high enough resolution to easily determine atmospheric composition is challenging.  The exoplanets are extremely faint compared to their host stars, requiring sophisticated techniques like coronagraphy to block out starlight.  The resolution, while improved over previous telescopes, might not always be sufficient for detailed atmospheric analysis in all cases.

Option (a) is correct as infrared observation is a key strength of JWST, allowing it to see through dust clouds and observe objects that are too cool to emit much visible light.

Option (b) is correct, the JWST's larger primary mirror significantly boosts its light-gathering capacity and resolution compared to Hubble.

Option (d) is correct, the L2 point provides a stable orbital position that is shielded from Earth's light and heat, crucial for infrared observations.


**3.  Which of the following statements accurately reflects aspects of the Chandrayaan-3 mission and its significance?**

(a) Chandrayaan-3 successfully achieved a soft landing on the far side of the Moon.
(b)  The mission's primary objective was to collect lunar soil samples and return them to Earth.
(c)  Chandrayaan-3's lander utilized a unique propulsion system not previously employed in lunar missions.
(d)  The successful soft landing demonstrated India's advanced capabilities in space exploration and lunar technology.

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Option (d) is correct. The successful soft landing of Chandrayaan-3 was a significant technological achievement, demonstrating India's capabilities in precise navigation, control, and landing systems in a challenging lunar environment.  This boosts India's standing in the global space community.

Option (a) is incorrect; Chandrayaan-3 landed on the near side of the moon.

Option (b) is incorrect; while sample collection might have been a secondary goal (not explicitly mentioned in the provided text), the primary focus was on demonstrating a successful soft landing.

Option (c) is incorrect; the text does not provide specific details on the uniqueness of the propulsion system compared to other lunar missions.


**4. Concerning the applications and challenges of hydrogen as an alternative fuel, which statement is FALSE?**

(a) Hydrogen fuel cells convert hydrogen directly into electricity, offering higher efficiency than direct combustion in internal combustion engines (ICEs).
(b)  "Green" hydrogen production uses renewable energy sources to power electrolysis, minimizing carbon emissions.
(c)  The low density of hydrogen requires significant compression or cryogenic liquefaction for efficient storage and transportation.
(d)  Hydrogen production from fossil fuels (e.g., steam methane reforming) is inherently carbon-neutral, making it a sustainable option.

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Option (d) is false.  Hydrogen production from fossil fuels, while possible, generates significant carbon dioxide emissions unless coupled with carbon capture and storage (CCS) technologies.  "Grey" and "blue" hydrogen refer to this process without and with CCS respectively.  Therefore, it's not inherently carbon-neutral and thus not a sustainable option without substantial mitigation efforts.

Options (a), (b), and (c) are all accurate statements reflecting the advantages and challenges associated with hydrogen as a fuel source.


**5.  Related to the concept of subduction zones and their geological impact, which statement is accurate?**

(a) Subduction zones are exclusively found in the Pacific Ocean's "Ring of Fire".
(b)  The subduction zone beneath the Gibraltar Strait is predicted to cause the complete closure of the Atlantic Ocean within the next million years.
(c)  Subduction zones are characterized by the collision of two less dense continental plates.
(d)  The process of subduction contributes significantly to the creation of volcanoes and earthquakes.

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Option (d) is correct because subduction, where one tectonic plate slides beneath another, is a primary driver of volcanic activity and seismic events.  The friction and melting of subducted material create magma, leading to volcanic eruptions, and the movement of plates along the subduction zone generates significant stress, resulting in earthquakes.

Option (a) is incorrect; while the Ring of Fire has numerous subduction zones, they are also found in other parts of the world.

Option (b) is incorrect; the predicted timescale is 20 million years, not one million.

Option (c) is incorrect; subduction usually involves a denser oceanic plate subducting beneath a less dense continental or oceanic plate.


These questions aim for a higher difficulty level by requiring deeper understanding and careful consideration of the nuances within the provided information.  They avoid simple direct recall and instead focus on analysis, evaluation, and application of the knowledge.


Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging and requires a nuanced understanding of the material.

**1.  A novel propulsion system utilizes a continuous detonation wave instead of deflagrative combustion, potentially offering enhanced efficiency and power.  Which technology best fits this description?**

(a) Ion Thruster Engine
(b) Radioisotope Thermoelectric Generator (RTG)
(c) Rotating Detonation Rocket Engine (RDRE)
(d) Semi-Cryogenic Engine (SCE-200)

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The description clearly points to the Rotating Detonation Rocket Engine (RDRE).  The question highlights the key differentiating feature: the use of a continuous detonation wave for propulsion.  This contrasts with traditional rocket engines that rely on deflagrative combustion.  Ion thrusters utilize electrostatic acceleration of ions, RTGs leverage radioactive decay for heat-to-electricity conversion, and SCE-200 is a liquid rocket engine; none of these employ continuous detonation waves as their primary propulsion mechanism. The RDRE's use of this innovative combustion method is explicitly mentioned in the text as a key advancement, making (c) the only accurate answer.  The other options represent different propulsion technologies with distinct operational principles.


**2.  Which type of battery technology utilizes sodium ions (Na+) as charge carriers, offering advantages in terms of material abundance and lower cost compared to a more established alternative?**

(a) Lithium-Ion Battery
(b) Sand Battery
(c) Sodium-Ion Battery
(d) Vanadium Flow Battery

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The question directly describes sodium-ion batteries.  The text explicitly states that sodium-ion batteries use sodium ions as charge carriers and highlights their cost and abundance advantages over lithium-ion batteries.  Sand batteries store thermal energy, not electrochemical energy, while vanadium flow batteries use vanadium redox reactions for energy storage—neither employs sodium ions. Therefore, option (c) is the only correct answer. The detailed explanation of sodium-ion battery operation further reinforces this choice.  The other options are distinct energy storage technologies with different mechanisms and materials.


**3.  This type of reactor, capable of producing more fissile material than it consumes, is exemplified by India's indigenous Prototype Fast Breeder Reactor (PFBR). What is this reactor type called?**

(a) Pressurized Heavy Water Reactor (PHWR)
(b) Small Modular Reactor (SMR)
(c) Thorium Reactor
(d) Fast Breeder Reactor (FBR)

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The question centers on the defining characteristic of a reactor that produces more fissile material than it uses.  The text explicitly identifies this as a Fast Breeder Reactor (FBR) and specifically mentions the PFBR as an example.  PHWRs use a different fuel cycle and do not breed fissile material.  SMRs are characterized by their size and modularity, not their fuel breeding capabilities. While thorium reactors utilize thorium, their primary characteristic isn't the breeding of fissile material in the same way as FBRs. Thus, option (d) is the correct and only option that accurately reflects the reactor type described.  The other options are different types of reactors with different operational principles and fuel cycles.


**4.  An airborne observatory, jointly operated by NASA and the German Aerospace Centre (DLR), utilized a telescope mounted on a modified Boeing 747 SP aircraft to study infrared light from celestial objects. What is the name of this observatory?**

(a)  ITER
(b) SOFIA
(c)  ALPHA
(d)  NIF

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The description uniquely identifies the Stratospheric Observatory for Infrared Astronomy (SOFIA). The question details its key characteristics: an airborne observatory, joint operation by NASA and DLR, use of a modified Boeing 747 SP, and focus on infrared astronomy.  ITER is a nuclear fusion project, ALPHA is a CERN experiment, and NIF is a laser-driven inertial confinement fusion facility; none of these fit the description.  Therefore, only SOFIA matches all the specifications provided in the question.  The other options are unrelated projects or facilities in different fields of science and technology.


**5.  Which technology, utilizing excess renewable energy to heat sand and store it as thermal energy for later release, is primarily applied in heating and industrial processes requiring thermal energy?**

(a)  Sodium-Ion Battery
(b)  Sand Battery
(c)  Vanadium Flow Battery
(d)  Lithium-Ion Battery

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The question describes the operational principle of a sand battery. The detailed description of its function—using sand's thermal properties to store and release heat—clearly matches the sand battery's technology.  The other options are electrochemical energy storage systems, not thermal energy storage.  Therefore, (b) is the only correct response.  The applications mentioned (heating and industrial thermal processes) further confirm this.  The other options are unrelated energy storage technologies.


**6.  The Artemis Accords, established in 2020, aim to guide civil space exploration and utilize principles based on which foundational treaty?**

(a)  The Outer Space Treaty of 1967
(b)  The Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons
(c)  The Antarctic Treaty System
(d)  The Montreal Protocol

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The question specifically asks about the foundational treaty upon which the Artemis Accords are based. The text explicitly states that the Artemis Accords build upon the Outer Space Treaty of 1967. The other options are international agreements dealing with nuclear weapons, Antarctica, and ozone depletion respectively, and are not relevant to the context of the Artemis Accords. Therefore, (a) is the correct answer. The other options are legally and thematically distinct international agreements.


**7.  Which Indian organization, established in 2003 under the Department of Atomic Energy, is primarily responsible for constructing and operating Fast Breeder Reactors for electricity generation?**

(a)  ISRO
(b)  DRDO
(c)  BHAVINI
(d)  NPCIL

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The question asks for the specific organization responsible for FBR construction and operation within the Indian Department of Atomic Energy. The text clearly identifies Bharatiya Nabhikiya Vidyut Nigam Limited (BHAVINI) as the entity fulfilling this role.  ISRO is focused on space research, DRDO on defense research and development, and NPCIL on nuclear power plant operation, though not specifically FBRs.  Therefore, BHAVINI is the only correct option. The other organizations have different mandates within the broader context of science and technology in India.


**8.  This method of charging uses electromagnetic fields to transfer energy between coils without a physical connection, and can be categorized into static, quasi-dynamic, and dynamic types depending on vehicle movement during charging.  What is this method called?**

(a)  Capacitive Charging
(b)  Wireless Charging/Induction Charging
(c)  V2G Charging
(d)  Fast Charging

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The question describes the principle of wireless or inductive charging. The detailed explanation of the process—transferring energy using electromagnetic fields between coils without physical contact—clearly matches the definition of induction charging.  Capacitive charging uses electric fields, V2G charging involves vehicle-to-grid energy transfer, and fast charging refers to the speed of charging, not the method itself. Therefore, (b) is the correct answer.  The categorization into static, quasi-dynamic, and dynamic charging further reinforces the identification of induction charging.


**9.  The Indian Space Research Organisation (ISRO) successfully conducted a test of this technology in April 2023, involving the autonomous landing of a vehicle carried to a specific altitude by an Indian Air Force Chinook helicopter.  Which technology was being tested?**

(a)  SSLv
(b)  Reusable Launch Vehicle Autonomous Landing Mission (RLV LEX)
(c)  Agnibaan SOrTeD
(d)  POEM-2

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The question describes the RLV LEX test, specifying the key details: the successful autonomous landing, the use of a Chinook helicopter for transport, and the involvement of ISRO.  The other options are different space-related projects and missions.  Only RLV LEX directly matches all the conditions presented. Therefore, (b) is the only correct option. The other options represent different space-related missions with different goals and technologies.


**10. Which material, abundant in India, is not fissile but can be converted into a fissile material (specifically Uranium-233) and holds significant potential for India's energy future?**

(a)  Plutonium-239
(b)  Uranium-235
(c)  Thorium
(d)  Deuterium

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The question highlights the unique properties of thorium as a fertile material. The text explicitly mentions thorium's abundance in India, its non-fissile nature, and its transmutation into fissile Uranium-233.  Plutonium-239 and Uranium-235 are already fissile materials. Deuterium is a fuel for fusion, not fission.  Therefore, only thorium fits the description. The other options are either already fissile or used in different nuclear processes.


Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  The questions are designed to be challenging and test various cognitive skills, focusing on factual recall, analysis, and conceptual understanding.  Each question includes a detailed explanation.


**1.  Which technology utilizes a rotating mirror made of liquid, offering a cost-effective alternative to traditional solid glass mirrors for astronomical observations, particularly suitable for zenith observations and continuous sky surveys?**

(a)  Giant Metrewave Radio Telescope (GMRT)
(b)  Himalayan Chandra Telescope (HCT)
(c)  International Liquid-Mirror Telescope (ILMT)
(d)  James Webb Space Telescope (JWST)

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The International Liquid-Mirror Telescope (ILMT) is explicitly described in the text as utilizing liquid mercury (or similar low-melting point alloys) as a rotating mirror.  This technique offers significant cost advantages and simplifies construction compared to traditional solid mirrors. Its suitability for zenith observations (looking straight up) and continuous sky surveys is also highlighted. The other options are incorrect: GMRT uses a radio array, HCT is an optical-infrared telescope with a solid mirror, and JWST is a space-based telescope.  The question tests factual recall and conceptual understanding of telescope technologies.


**2. Which of the following applications is NOT directly associated with Perovskite materials, based on the provided information?**

(a)  High-efficiency solar cells with potential for low-cost production.
(b)  Light-emitting diodes (LEDs) and lasers across a wide range of colors due to tunable bandgaps.
(c)  High-sensitivity photodetectors and direct X-ray detectors for medical imaging and security.
(d)  Vanadium flow batteries for renewable energy storage.

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The text details various applications of Perovskites in solar cells, LEDs, lasers, and photodetectors, emphasizing their tunable properties.  Vanadium flow batteries, however, are explicitly linked to Vanadium, a separate material with its own distinct applications. The question assesses the ability to distinguish between the applications of different materials and demonstrates conceptual understanding.


**3.  Which of the following accurately describes the primary function of the DAGGER model developed by NASA researchers?**

(a)  Analyzing images of the Sun in white light using a novel methodology.
(b)  Predicting geomagnetic disturbances worldwide, specifically those caused by solar storms, with a 30-minute lead time.
(c)  Exploring the chemistry and habitability of Saturn's moon Titan.
(d)  Removing arsenic and metal ions from water.

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The text clearly states that the DAGGER model uses AI to analyze spacecraft data on solar wind and predicts geomagnetic disturbances caused by solar storms, providing a 30-minute warning. The other options are incorrect:  Equal Contrast Technique (ECT) analyzes solar images, the Dragonfly mission targets Titan, and AMRIT technology is for water purification.  This question tests factual recall and understanding of specific technological applications.


**4.  What is the primary propellant combination used in the Semi-Cryogenic Engine (SCE-200) being developed by ISRO?**

(a)  Liquid oxygen (LOX) and liquid hydrogen (LH2)
(b)  Liquid oxygen (LOX) and RP-1 kerosene
(c)  Triethylaluminum and Triethylboron
(d)  Ammonium nitrate and metallic aluminum powders

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The text specifies that the SCE-200 uses liquid oxygen (LOX) and RP-1 kerosene as propellants. Option (a) describes cryogenic engines, (c) is a starter fuel for a different engine type, and (d) is a solid propellant combination.  The question tests specific knowledge of rocket propulsion systems and their fuel types, demanding factual recall and distinguishing between different propellant types.


**5. Which of the following space missions is NOT directly associated with NASA's New Frontiers Program?**

(a) New Horizons
(b) Juno
(c) OSIRIS-Rex (and OSIRIS-APEX)
(d) Chandrayaan-3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly mentions that New Horizons, Juno, and OSIRIS-Rex (including its extended mission, OSIRIS-APEX) are part of NASA's New Frontiers Program. Chandrayaan-3 is an ISRO mission, not a NASA mission. This tests factual recall and understanding of space exploration programs.


**6. Which of the following best describes the primary function of the IceCube Neutrino Observatory in Antarctica?**

(a)  Studying the origin and evolution of Jupiter.
(b)  Exploring the chemistry and habitability of Titan.
(c)  Observing cosmic rays, studying dark matter, and investigating neutrino properties.
(d)  Bringing back lunar samples from the far side of the Moon.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The text explicitly states that the IceCube Observatory's primary aim is to observe cosmic rays, study dark matter, and understand neutrinos. The other options describe different space missions with unrelated objectives. This question tests factual recall of scientific research facilities and their functions.


**7. Which Indian organization is responsible for developing the AMRIT technology for removing arsenic and metal ions from water?**

(a)  Vikram Sarabhai Space Centre (VSSC)
(b)  Indian Institute of Astrophysics (IIA)
(c)  Indian Institute of Technology Madras (IIT Madras)
(d)  Liquid Propulsion Systems Centre (LPSC)

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The text explicitly credits IIT Madras with the development of AMRIT technology. This question tests factual recall of specific technological developments and the organizations involved.


**8. Which of the following is NOT a characteristic feature commonly associated with OLED display technology?**

(a)  Self-lit pixels
(b)  Susceptibility to burn-in
(c)  High brightness compared to QLED
(d)  Excellent contrast and black levels

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The text indicates that OLEDs have excellent contrast and black levels due to self-lit pixels and that they are susceptible to burn-in.  However, QLEDs are described as brighter than OLEDs. This question assesses the understanding of display technologies and their comparative features.


**9. Which of the following is the most accurate description of a "quasi-moon" or "quasi-satellite," as discussed in the text?**

(a)  A type of electromagnetic radiation observed in radio-wave frequencies.
(b)  A large, bright feature extending outward from the Sun's surface.
(c)  An asteroid that orbits the Sun in a similar timeframe as Earth, with slight gravitational influence from Earth.
(d)  A type of galaxy powered by a supermassive black hole.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The text defines a quasi-moon as an asteroid sharing a similar orbital period with Earth but experiencing only minor gravitational interaction. The other options describe different astronomical phenomena. This question tests the understanding of lesser-known astronomical terms and concepts.


**10. Which country is credited with the development of the ICUBE-Q orbiter, a cubesat included in the Chang'e-6 lunar probe?**

(a)  India
(b)  United States
(c)  Russia
(d)  Pakistan

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The provided text explicitly mentions that the ICUBE-Q orbiter, a cubesat, was developed by Pakistan and included in the Chang'e-6 mission.  This demonstrates factual recall of international space collaborations.

These questions aim for a higher difficulty level by demanding precise recall of facts and nuanced understanding of the concepts.  The distractors are carefully chosen to be plausible but ultimately incorrect, requiring careful consideration of the provided information.


Here are some challenging multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, designed to test various cognitive skills relevant to the UPSC exam.  Each question includes a detailed explanation justifying the correct answer and explaining why the other options are incorrect.

**1.  A novel method of altering an organism's DNA, potentially impacting traits and disease risk, uses site-directed nucleases (SDNs) to make precise changes to the genome.  Which of the following best describes this technology and its key characteristic(s)?**

(a)  Gene-drive Technology, primarily used for population control in insects.
(b)  Genome Editing, characterized by the use of SDNs to introduce, delete, or substitute nucleotides, potentially involving foreign genetic material.
(c)  Genome Sequencing, focused on determining the complete DNA sequence of an organism.
(d)  CAR-T cell therapy, a form of immunotherapy targeting cancer cells.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The question describes genome editing, a precise technology that uses site-directed nucleases (SDNs) to modify an organism's DNA.  Option (b) accurately captures this definition, highlighting the use of SDNs to make changes—insertions, deletions, or substitutions—at specific locations within the genome. It also correctly notes that this process can sometimes involve the introduction of foreign genetic material (SDN3), though SDN1 and SDN2 do not.

Option (a) is incorrect because while gene-drive technology is a form of genome editing, it specifically aims to spread a modified gene through a population, not simply alter an individual organism's DNA. Option (c) is incorrect as genome sequencing is about determining the order of nucleotides, not modifying them. Option (d) is incorrect because CAR-T cell therapy is an immunotherapy technique, not a method of genome modification.


**2.  A technology that uses excess renewable energy to heat sand, storing the thermal energy for later release, primarily for heating applications, is known as:**

(a)  Battery Energy Storage System (BESS)
(b)  Sodium-ion Battery
(c)  Sand Battery
(d)  Lithium-ion Battery


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The description clearly points to a thermal energy storage system using sand. Option (c), "Sand Battery," accurately reflects this technology.  Sand batteries utilize the thermal properties of sand to store heat generated from renewable energy sources. This stored heat can then be released on demand for various applications, mainly heating systems and industrial processes needing thermal energy.

Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they describe different types of batteries that store electrical energy, not thermal energy.  BESS is a general term encompassing various technologies, while sodium-ion and lithium-ion batteries are specific electrochemical energy storage solutions.


**3.  Which of the following is NOT a method used in the production of biofuels?**

(a)  Transesterification
(b)  Hydrogenation
(c)  Electrolysis (for green hydrogen)
(d)  Retrotranscription


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Transesterification is a key process in biodiesel production, hydrogenation enhances bio-oil properties, and electrolysis produces green hydrogen which can be used as a fuel or to power biofuel production processes.  Retrotranscription, however, is a molecular biology process involved in the replication of retroviruses and the creation of cDNA, not a method for biofuel production.  Therefore, option (d) is the correct answer.  The other options are all established methods for biofuel creation or processing.


**4.  A continuous stream of charged particles, predominantly electrons, protons, and alpha particles, emanating from the Sun's corona, significantly influencing space weather and Earth's magnetosphere, is called:**

(a)  Solar Flare
(b)  Coronal Mass Ejection (CME)
(c)  Solar Wind
(d)  Gamma Ray Burst (GRB)


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The description perfectly matches the characteristics of the solar wind.  Option (c) is the correct answer.  The solar wind is a constant flow of charged particles from the Sun, impacting Earth's magnetic field and causing various space weather phenomena.

Options (a) and (b) are incorrect because solar flares and CMEs are more intense, episodic events, not continuous streams of particles.  Option (d) is incorrect; GRBs are high-energy bursts of gamma radiation originating from distant galaxies, unrelated to the Sun's regular particle emissions.


**5.  The Indian Space Research Organisation (ISRO) has developed a launch vehicle designed for cost-effectiveness, flexibility, and the efficient deployment of multiple small satellites into Low Earth Orbit (LEO). Which launch vehicle fits this description?**

(a)  Polar Satellite Launch Vehicle (PSLV)
(b)  Geosynchronous Satellite Launch Vehicle Mk III (GSLV Mk III)
(c)  Small Satellite Launch Vehicle (SSLV)
(d)  Reusable Launch Vehicle (RLV)**


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The question describes the characteristics of a launch vehicle designed specifically for small satellites and cost-efficiency.  Option (c), the Small Satellite Launch Vehicle (SSLV), aligns perfectly with this description.  The SSLV is explicitly designed to launch multiple small satellites into LEO at a lower cost than larger launch vehicles.

The PSLV (a) is a versatile vehicle but not primarily designed for small satellites and cost optimization in the same way as the SSLV. The GSLV Mk III (b) is a heavy-lift vehicle, not ideal for small satellites. The RLV (d) is focused on reusability, not necessarily small satellite launches.


**6.  Which of the following is NOT a component of a Lithium-ion battery?**

(a) Graphite anode
(b) Lithium oxide cathode
(c) Electrolyte
(d) Sodium ions


**Correct Answer:** (d)


**Explanation:**

Lithium-ion batteries utilize lithium ions as charge carriers.  A graphite anode, lithium oxide cathode (or similar lithium-containing cathode material), and an electrolyte are essential components. Sodium ions are the charge carriers in sodium-ion batteries, not lithium-ion batteries.  Therefore, option (d) is the correct answer.


**7.  The process of heating biomass in the absence of oxygen to break down organic materials into bio-oil, syngas, and biochar is known as:**

(a)  Transesterification
(b)  Hydrogenation
(c)  Pyrolysis
(d)  Cracking


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The description accurately defines pyrolysis, a thermochemical process used in biofuel production.  Pyrolysis involves the thermal decomposition of organic materials in an oxygen-deficient environment.  This process yields bio-oil, syngas (synthesis gas), and biochar as primary products.  The other options describe different processes used in biofuel production but not the specific process described in the question.


**8. Which of the following statements about the National Hydrogen Mission in India is INCORRECT?**

(a) It aims to produce 5 MMT of green hydrogen annually by 2030.
(b)  It focuses solely on hydrogen production from fossil fuels.
(c) It aims to attract over Rs. 8 lakh crore in investments.
(d) It seeks to reduce India's reliance on fossil fuel imports.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The National Hydrogen Mission primarily focuses on *green* hydrogen production using renewable energy sources.  Option (b) is incorrect as it states the mission relies solely on fossil fuels, which is contrary to its core objective. The other options correctly reflect the mission's goals and targets.


**9. The Indian government initiative aimed at promoting sustainable transportation, reducing fossil fuel dependence, and fostering a domestic electric vehicle (EV) industry is called:**

(a) GOBAR DHAN Scheme
(b) National Electric Mobility Mission Plan (NEMMP) 2020
(c) FAME India Scheme
(d) Pradhan Mantri JI-VAN Yojana


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The National Electric Mobility Mission Plan (NEMMP) 2020 is the overarching government strategy to promote electric vehicles in India. While FAME India is a crucial *part* of NEMMP, providing incentives, NEMMP is the broader, encompassing policy framework. The other options are unrelated to electric vehicle promotion.


**10.  Which of the following is NOT a primary objective of the National Policy on Biofuels (2018) and its amendments?**

(a)  Reducing India's dependence on imported petroleum products.
(b)  Promoting the use of advanced biofuels.
(c)  Encouraging the use of only edible crops for biofuel production.
(d)  Boosting farmer income through increased demand for feedstock.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The National Policy on Biofuels emphasizes the use of *non-edible* feedstocks to avoid competition with food production.  Option (c) is incorrect; the policy actively discourages reliance solely on edible crops for biofuel production.  The other options accurately reflect the policy's objectives.


Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging and requires a nuanced understanding of the subject matter.

**1.  A colorless, odorless, non-flammable, non-corrosive, and extremely cold element used in food preservation and cryotherapy poses a risk of cold burns and frostbite if handled improperly. Identify this element.**

(a) Methanol
(b) Ethylene
(c) Liquid Nitrogen
(d) Glycerol

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The description clearly points to liquid nitrogen.  Liquid nitrogen is known for its cryogenic properties (-196 °C), making it suitable for freezing and transporting food.  However, its extremely low temperature poses a significant risk of severe cold burns and frostbite upon direct skin contact. Methanol is a liquid with a distinct odor and is toxic. Ethylene is a gas used in fruit ripening. Glycerol is a viscous liquid, not known for its extreme cold properties.  The question tests factual recall and the ability to link properties with potential risks.  The distractors are plausible because they are all substances relevant to the food or scientific domains.


**2.  A recent study highlighted the correlation between a specific food-related index and increased risks of type II diabetes and cardiovascular diseases. This index measures how rapidly a carbohydrate-containing food elevates blood sugar levels. Which index is being described?**

(a) Glycemic Load (GL)
(b) Glycemic Index (GI)
(c) Body Mass Index (BMI)
(d) Dietary Fiber Index (DFI)

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The description clearly defines the Glycemic Index (GI). The question tests conceptual understanding of the GI and its implications for human health.  Glycemic Load (GL) is related but considers both the GI and the amount of carbohydrates. BMI is a measure of body fat, while DFI assesses dietary fiber intake, neither of which directly measures the rate of blood sugar increase.  The distractors are related concepts in nutrition and health, making the question challenging.


**3.  A rare condition characterized by blood clots (thrombosis) and a low platelet count (thrombocytopenia) has been linked to a specific COVID-19 vaccine.  This condition can affect various organs, including the brain, abdomen, and lungs. What is this condition called?**

(a) Meningitis
(b) Thrombosis with Thrombocytopenia Syndrome (TTS)
(c) Avian Influenza
(d)  Vaccine-Induced Immune Thrombotic Thrombocytopenia (VITT)

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The description precisely describes Thrombosis with Thrombocytopenia Syndrome (TTS), also known as Vaccine-induced Immune Thrombotic Thrombocytopenia (VITT). The question tests factual recall of a specific medical condition and its association with a vaccine. Meningitis is an inflammation of brain and spinal cord membranes, Avian Influenza is a bird flu, and VITT is a synonym for TTS. The question effectively uses synonyms as distractors to increase difficulty.


**4. Which of the following is a non-invasive medical imaging technique that utilizes a large magnet and radio waves to produce detailed images of internal body structures without using ionizing radiation?**

(a) X-ray
(b) Positron Emission Tomography (PET)
(c) Magnetic Resonance Imaging (MRI)
(d) Computed Tomography (CT) scan

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The question describes Magnetic Resonance Imaging (MRI).  The key features are non-invasive nature, use of large magnets and radio waves, and absence of ionizing radiation.  X-rays, PET scans, and CT scans all involve ionizing radiation. The question tests factual recall of medical imaging techniques and their underlying principles. The distractors are all other common medical imaging modalities, increasing the difficulty by requiring precise knowledge of each technique.


**5.  A type of electric propulsion used in spacecraft that ionizes a neutral gas to create positive ions, which are then accelerated using electricity to generate thrust, is known as:**

(a) Rotating Detonation Rocket Engine (RDRE)
(b) Ion Thruster Engine
(c) Radioisotope Thermoelectric Generator (RTG)
(d)  Cryogenic Engine

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The description accurately depicts an Ion Thruster Engine. The question assesses conceptual understanding of spacecraft propulsion systems.  The other options represent different propulsion technologies. RDRE uses detonation waves, RTGs use radioactive decay for power generation, and cryogenic engines utilize cryogenic propellants. The distractors are other relevant propulsion systems, making the question challenging.


**6. The Artemis Accords, established in 2020, are a set of non-binding principles intended to guide civil space exploration and utilization. Which of the following is NOT a key commitment under the Artemis Accords?**

(a) Peaceful Purposes
(b) Common Infrastructure
(c)  Exclusive Resource Claiming
(d) Mitigation of Debris

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Exclusive Resource Claiming is NOT a commitment under the Artemis Accords. The Accords emphasize the peaceful use of space and sustainable resource utilization, explicitly discouraging exclusive claims. The question tests understanding of international space law and cooperation.  The distractors are all actual key elements of the Accords, requiring careful reading and understanding of the principles.


**7. A continuous stream of charged particles emanating from the Sun's corona, primarily composed of electrons, protons, and alpha particles, traveling at speeds of approximately one million miles per hour and extending throughout the solar system, is referred to as:**

(a) Solar Flare
(b) Solar Winds
(c) Coronal Mass Ejection (CME)
(d) Sunspots

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The description precisely defines Solar Winds.  The question assesses factual recall and the ability to distinguish between different solar phenomena. Solar flares are intense bursts of radiation, CMEs are large expulsions of plasma, and sunspots are cooler, darker areas on the sun's surface.  The distractors are closely related solar phenomena, increasing the difficulty level.


**8.  A class of materials with a common crystal structure (ABX₃) exhibiting versatile and tunable properties, used in solar cells, LEDs, lasers, and photodetectors is known as:**

(a)  Vanadium
(b)  Perovskite
(c)  Carbon Nanotubes
(d)  Graphene

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The description clearly refers to Perovskites.  The question tests conceptual understanding of material science and its applications. Vanadium is a chemical element, carbon nanotubes and graphene are allotropes of carbon, each with unique properties.  The distractors are other materials used in various technologies, increasing the difficulty level and requiring specific knowledge of material properties and applications.


**9.  Which of the following is a type of fuel cell that directly converts the chemical energy of methanol into electricity, offering advantages such as liquid fuel, high energy density, and compact size?**

(a)  Hydrogen Fuel Cell
(b)  Solid Oxide Fuel Cell (SOFC)
(c)  Direct Methanol Fuel Cells (DMFCs)
(d)  Proton Exchange Membrane Fuel Cell (PEMFC)

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The question precisely describes Direct Methanol Fuel Cells (DMFCs).  The question tests factual recall of fuel cell types and their characteristics. Hydrogen fuel cells use hydrogen gas, SOFCs operate at high temperatures, and PEMFCs use a proton exchange membrane.  The distractors are other types of fuel cells, requiring specific knowledge of their functionalities to answer correctly.


**10.  A method of heating biomass in the absence of oxygen, breaking down organic materials into bio-oil, syngas, and biochar, is called:**

(a)  Transesterification
(b)  Hydrogenation
(c)  Pyrolysis
(d)  Cracking

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The description defines Pyrolysis. The question tests knowledge of biofuel production methods. Transesterification is used in biodiesel production, hydrogenation adds hydrogen to bio-oil, and cracking involves breaking down larger molecules.  The distractors are other biofuel production techniques, requiring specific understanding of each process to correctly identify pyrolysis.


Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on Science and Technology.  Each question is designed to be challenging and assess various cognitive skills, with detailed explanations provided.


**1.  A novel mustard variety, characterized by significantly reduced pungency compared to traditional Indian mustard, has been developed.  This achievement is primarily attributed to which biotechnological advancement?**

(a)  Traditional cross-breeding techniques focusing on selective breeding for desirable traits.
(b)  Genetic modification involving the introduction of foreign genes to alter glucosinolate levels.
(c)  Genome editing utilizing CRISPR/Cas9 technology to modify existing genes.
(d)  Induced mutagenesis employing radiation or chemical agents to create desirable mutations.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly states that the new low-pungent mustard variety was produced through gene editing of the 'Varuna' variety using CRISPR/Cas9 technology.  This technique directly targets and modifies specific genes within the organism's genome, unlike traditional breeding methods which rely on random combinations of genes. Option (b) is incorrect because while genetic modification can alter traits, the passage specifies genome editing as the precise method. Option (a) is too general and doesn't reflect the specific technological advancement used. Option (d) is a different genetic modification technique and is not the one used in this case. The development highlights the precision and efficiency of genome editing in crop improvement, a significant area in agricultural biotechnology and a topic of relevance to India's food security.


**2. The GenomeIndia Project, a large-scale initiative aimed at creating a reference genome for the Indian population, shares a conceptual foundation with which earlier international endeavor?**

(a)  The Human Microbiome Project, focusing on the characterization of the human gut microbiome.
(b)  The International Rice Genome Sequencing Project, dedicated to sequencing the rice genome.
(c)  The Human Genome Project, which aimed to map the entire human genome.
(d)  The ENCODE Project, focused on identifying functional elements in the human genome.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly states that the GenomeIndia Project was inspired by the Human Genome Project (HGP). Both projects share the common goal of comprehensively understanding a genome, although the scale and focus differ. The HGP was a global effort to sequence the entire human genome, while GenomeIndia focuses on the Indian population's specific genetic variations. Options (a), (b), and (d) are all significant projects in genomics but are not directly comparable to the scope and purpose of the GenomeIndia Project in terms of its overarching goal and inspiration.  Understanding the HGP's impact and the subsequent development of national genome projects like GenomeIndia is crucial for comprehending advancements in genomics and personalized medicine.


**3.  The India AI Mission, a significant government initiative, aims to bolster India's artificial intelligence ecosystem.  Which of the following is NOT a primary objective of this mission?**

(a)  Developing indigenous AI capabilities and promoting responsible AI development.
(b)  Establishing a robust AI computing infrastructure through public-private partnerships.
(c)  Prioritizing the development of narrow AI applications over broad, general-purpose AI systems.
(d)  Improving data quality and democratizing access to non-personal datasets for researchers.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage details the India AI Mission's objectives, including fostering indigenous AI capabilities, building robust computing infrastructure, improving data quality, and democratizing data access.  However, there's no mention of prioritizing narrow AI over general-purpose AI. The mission aims to develop a comprehensive AI ecosystem encompassing various AI applications, including large multimodal models (LMMs), which are examples of general-purpose AI. The other options accurately reflect the mission's stated goals.  The question tests the candidate's ability to identify nuances within the description of a large-scale government initiative and understand the strategic priorities within a national AI strategy.


**4.  Mitochondrial Replacement Therapy (MRT), a specialized IVF technique, is primarily employed to mitigate the risk of transmission of which type of genetic disorder?**

(a)  Autosomal dominant disorders affecting various bodily systems.
(b)  X-linked recessive disorders predominantly impacting males.
(c)  Mitochondrial disorders affecting energy production in cells.
(d)  Chromosomal abnormalities leading to developmental disabilities.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The text clearly states that MRT is used when there's a high risk of mitochondrial diseases being passed from mother to child. These diseases directly affect the mitochondria, the powerhouses of cells, impacting energy production. Options (a), (b), and (d) describe different types of genetic disorders not directly addressed by MRT.  The passage highlights the complex ethical and scientific considerations surrounding advanced reproductive technologies and their application in managing specific genetic conditions.


**5.  The recent approval of Casgevy and Lyfgenia, CRISPR-based gene therapies, signifies a breakthrough in the treatment of which inherited blood disorder?**

(a)  Hemophilia, characterized by impaired blood clotting.
(b)  Thalassemia, involving abnormal hemoglobin production.
(c)  Sickle cell disease, causing mis-shaped red blood cells.
(d)  Von Willebrand disease, a bleeding disorder affecting platelet function.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly mentions that these CRISPR-based gene therapies are approved for treating Sickle Cell Disease (SCD) in patients aged 12 and older. The other options represent other inherited blood disorders but are not the focus of these specific approved therapies.  This question assesses factual recall related to recent advancements in gene therapy and their specific applications in treating genetic diseases.


**6.  The World Health Organization's (WHO) CoViNet initiative represents a significant collaboration in which area of public health research and surveillance?**

(a)  Monitoring and responding to outbreaks of neglected tropical diseases.
(b)  Surveillance and research related to coronaviruses and related pathogens.
(c)  Global tracking and analysis of antimicrobial resistance patterns.
(d)  Development and deployment of new vaccines for emerging infectious diseases.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The passage describes CoViNet as a network of global laboratories specializing in human, animal, and environmental coronavirus surveillance.  The other options are important public health areas, but they are not the primary focus of the CoViNet initiative. The question tests understanding of global health initiatives and the specific expertise involved in coordinating international collaborations for disease surveillance.


**7.  Which of the following is NOT a technique employed in Mitochondrial Replacement Therapy (MRT)?**

(a)  Maternal spindle transfer (MST), involving nuclear transfer from the mother's egg to a donor egg.
(b)  Pronuclear transfer (PNT), involving pronuclei transfer from the mother's fertilized egg to a donor egg.
(c)  Cytoplasmic transfer, involving the transfer of cytoplasm containing healthy mitochondria from a donor egg.
(d)  Nuclear genome sequencing to identify specific mitochondrial DNA mutations.


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The passage details MST and PNT as the primary techniques used in MRT.  While cytoplasmic transfer might seem plausible, the passage focuses on the two named methods.  Nuclear genome sequencing is a diagnostic tool used to identify the need for MRT, not a technique within the MRT procedure itself.  The question assesses the candidate's ability to distinguish between the diagnostic and therapeutic aspects of a complex medical procedure.



**8.  The use of white phosphorus munitions in civilian areas is considered a war crime, despite the substance not being classified as a chemical weapon under which international treaty?**

(a)  The Biological Weapons Convention (BWC)
(b)  The Ottawa Treaty (Convention on Cluster Munitions)
(c)  The Chemical Weapons Convention (CWC)
(d)  The Geneva Conventions (International humanitarian law)


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly states that white phosphorus is not a chemical weapon under the Chemical Weapons Convention (CWC), even though its use in civilian areas is a war crime under international humanitarian law.  The other conventions address different categories of weapons. This question tests the understanding of international law, specifically concerning the classification of weapons and their implications under different treaties.


**9.  The Glycemic Index (GI) is a measure of which physiological response to food consumption?**

(a)  The rate at which a food raises blood pressure levels.
(b)  The rate at which a food raises blood cholesterol levels.
(c)  The rate at which a food raises blood sugar levels.
(d)  The rate at which a food raises blood triglyceride levels.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly defines GI as a measure of how quickly a carbohydrate-containing food raises blood sugar levels.  The other options are related to other metabolic parameters. This question tests the understanding of a specific nutritional concept and its relevance to health.


**10.  The National Sickle Cell Anaemia Elimination Mission in India employs a three-pillar strategy. Which of the following is NOT one of those pillars?**

(a)  Health promotion to raise awareness about the disease.
(b)  Disease prevention through genetic screening and counseling.
(c)  Holistic management and continuum of care for affected individuals.
(d)  Development of new drugs specifically targeting sickle cell anemia.


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The passage outlines the three pillars of the mission as health promotion, prevention, and holistic management.  While drug development is relevant, it's not explicitly listed as a primary pillar of the mission's strategy. This question assesses the candidate's comprehension of a national health program and its strategic framework.


Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on factual recall, analysis, and conceptual understanding.  Each question is designed to be challenging and avoids simple recall, demanding deeper understanding of the concepts.


**1.  A novel mustard variety, developed by Indian researchers, exhibits a significantly reduced pungency compared to traditional Indian mustard. This reduction is attributed to a decrease in which specific compound, bringing its level closer to that of Canola?**

(a)  Sinigrin
(b)  Glucosinolate
(c)  Erucic acid
