(d)  Isothiocyanate


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly states that the new mustard variety has a lesser quantity of glucosinolates, bringing it to the Canola quality limit.  Glucosinolates are responsible for the pungent taste and potential health risks in livestock. Sinigrin is a type of glucosinolate, but the question focuses on the general class of compounds responsible for the pungency. Erucic acid and isothiocyanates are also found in mustard but are not the primary focus regarding pungency reduction in this context.  The question tests factual recall and requires a precise understanding of the scientific terminology related to mustard composition.


**2.  The CRISPR/Cas9 gene-editing technology, utilized in the development of the low-pungent mustard variety, employs what mechanism to modify an organism's DNA?**

(a)  Random insertion of foreign DNA segments.
(b)  Site-directed nucleases to create precise DNA alterations.
(c)  Viral vectors for targeted gene delivery.
(d)  Methylation of specific DNA bases to silence genes.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The text clearly describes CRISPR/Cas9 as using site-directed nucleases (SDNs) to make precise changes in the DNA sequence.  Options (a) and (c) describe alternative gene modification techniques, while option (d) refers to an epigenetic modification, not a direct DNA alteration via gene editing.  This question assesses conceptual understanding of gene editing techniques and the specific mechanism employed by CRISPR/Cas9.


**3.  The Indian Space Research Organisation (ISRO) successfully commissioned India's largest Battery Energy Storage System (BESS) in which state?**

(a)  Tamil Nadu
(b)  Gujarat
(c)  Karnataka
(d)  Chhattisgarh


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly mentions that SECI, under the Ministry of New and Renewable Energy, commissioned the largest BESS in Chhattisgarh.  This tests factual recall of a specific development in renewable energy infrastructure in India.  The other options are also significant states in India, but they are not directly relevant to this particular BESS project.


**4.  The recently deceased Nobel laureate, John Bannister Goodenough, made a significant contribution to which specific type of rechargeable battery technology?**

(a)  Lead-acid battery
(b)  Nickel-cadmium battery
(c)  Lithium-ion battery
(d)  Sodium-ion battery


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The text explicitly credits Goodenough with developing a lithium-ion battery with a cobalt oxide cathode. This question assesses factual recall of a prominent scientist and his contribution to a specific technological advancement. The other options represent different battery chemistries.


**5.  In the context of Small Modular Reactors (SMRs), the term "Modular" signifies which key aspect of their design and deployment?**

(a)  Their small physical size compared to conventional reactors.
(b)  The use of passive safety features for reactor shutdown.
(c)  Factory assembly and transportation of components as a unit.
(d)  Their adaptability to various power generation needs.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage defines SMRs as modular, emphasizing that their systems and components are factory-assembled and transported as units for installation. While (a), (b), and (d) are advantages of SMRs, they don't define the meaning of "modular" in this specific technological context.  The question tests the precise understanding of the terminology used in describing advanced nuclear reactor technology.


**6. Which of the following is NOT a technique used in Mitochondrial Replacement Therapy (MRT)?**

(a) Maternal Spindle Transfer (MST)
(b) Pronuclear Transfer (PNT)
(c) Cytoplasmic Transfer
(d) Nuclear Genome Editing


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The passage details MST and PNT as techniques used in MRT, focusing on transferring the nuclear genome while replacing faulty mitochondria. Cytoplasmic transfer is also a related technique. However, nuclear genome editing is a separate process that directly alters the genetic material of the nucleus, not the mitochondria. This question tests understanding of the MRT process and distinguishes it from other genetic manipulation techniques.


**7.  The Indian Space Research Organisation (ISRO)'s Small Satellite Launch Vehicle (SSLV) aims to primarily serve which market segment within the space industry?**

(a)  Launching large communication satellites.
(b)  Deploying small satellites for various purposes.

(d)  Conducting deep-space exploration missions.

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly states that the SSLV targets the rapidly growing market for launching small satellites. The other options represent different space launch capabilities, not the primary focus of the SSLV. This tests the understanding of ISRO's strategic goals in the space launch sector.


**8. The Agnilet engine, a key component of the Agnibaan SubOrbital Technological Demonstrator (SOrTeD), is notable for being produced using which manufacturing method?**

(b)  CNC machining

**9.  What is the primary function of microRNAs (miRNAs) in gene regulation?**

(a)  Initiating transcription of genes.
(b)  Modifying histone proteins to control gene expression.
(c)  Post-transcriptional regulation of gene expression.
(d)  Directly altering DNA sequences to modify genes.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The text describes miRNAs as being involved in post-transcriptional regulation.  Options (a) and (d) refer to different stages of gene regulation, while (b) describes a different mechanism of epigenetic regulation. **10. The Atom-Trap Trace Analysis (ATTA) technique, recently used in a study, enables radiometric dating using which less-common radioactive isotope?**

(a) Carbon-14
(b) Potassium-40

This tests the knowledge of advanced techniques in dating geological and archaeological artifacts.



Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is followed by a detailed explanation.


**1.  A novel gene therapy approach involves modifying a patient's own T cells to target and destroy cancer cells carrying a specific protein. This protein acts as a biomarker for a type of white blood cell. Which of the following best describes this therapy and its target?**

(a)  Immunosuppressive therapy targeting cancerous macrophages.
(b)  CAR T-cell therapy targeting B lymphocytes expressing the CD19 protein.
(c)  Gene drive technology targeting cancerous T lymphocytes.
(d)  Enzyme replacement therapy targeting mutated B cells.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The description clearly points to CAR T-cell therapy.  This immunotherapy modifies a patient's T cells to express a chimeric antigen receptor (CAR) that specifically targets cancer cells. The question mentions the target protein acts as a biomarker for a type of white blood cell, which is the key clue.  B lymphocytes (B cells) are a type of white blood cell, and CD19 is a common biomarker expressed on the surface of many B-cell lymphomas and leukemias. Therefore, the therapy targets B lymphocytes expressing the CD19 protein.

Option (a) is incorrect because immunosuppressive therapies aim to suppress the immune system, not enhance its ability to target cancer cells. Macrophages are another type of white blood cell, but they are not the primary target in this scenario. Option (c) is incorrect because gene drive technology is a method for altering gene inheritance in populations, not a direct cancer therapy. Option (d) is incorrect because enzyme replacement therapy involves supplementing missing or deficient enzymes, not modifying immune cells to target cancer.


**2. A technique involves replacing faulty mitochondria in a mother's egg or embryo with healthy mitochondria from a donor egg, thereby preventing the transmission of mitochondrial diseases. Which of the following accurately describes this technique and its primary application?**

(a)  Genome sequencing for early diagnosis of mitochondrial disorders.
(b)  Mitochondrial Replacement Therapy (MRT) for preventing the inheritance of mitochondrial diseases.
(c)  Gene drive technology for altering the mitochondrial DNA in germline cells.
(d)  CRISPR-Cas9 gene editing to correct mutations in mitochondrial DNA.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The description directly refers to Mitochondrial Replacement Therapy (MRT), also known as mitochondrial donation.  This advanced IVF technique replaces faulty maternal mitochondria with healthy ones from a donor, preventing the transmission of mitochondrial diseases to the offspring. The primary application is precisely the prevention of inheritable mitochondrial disorders.

Option (a) is incorrect because genome sequencing is a diagnostic tool, not a therapeutic technique for replacing mitochondria. Option (c) is incorrect as gene drive technology is used to spread a specific gene within a population, not to replace cellular components like mitochondria. Option (d) is incorrect because while CRISPR-Cas9 can be used for gene editing, it is not currently efficiently used for targeting and correcting mutations in mitochondrial DNA due to the unique characteristics of mitochondrial genome replication and repair.


**3.  A five-year research project, led by international researchers, aims to generate genomic datasets from underrepresented populations across various continents to understand the genetic basis of Non-Communicable Diseases (NCDs).  This project involves analyzing DNA methylation data and health-related measures. Which of the following best describes this initiative?**

(a)  The Human Genome Project focusing on NCDs.
(b)  The Genome India Project focused on specific Indian populations.
(c)  The Diverse Epigenetic Epidemiology Partnership (DEEP) project.
(d)  IndiGen programme focused on healthy Indian individuals.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The description perfectly matches the Diverse Epigenetic Epidemiology Partnership (DEEP) project.  The project’s focus on underrepresented populations, analysis of DNA methylation, and investigation of NCDs aligns precisely with the DEEP project's goals.  The project explicitly aims to address the underrepresentation of certain populations in health studies and to understand the genetic basis of NCDs in diverse groups.

Option (a) is incorrect because the Human Genome Project was a large-scale effort to map the entire human genome, not specifically focused on NCDs or underrepresented populations. Option (b) is incorrect because the Genome India Project, while focusing on Indian populations, doesn't have the same international scope and explicit focus on epigenetic analysis of NCDs. Option (d) is incorrect because the IndiGen programme is focused on the whole-genome sequencing of healthy Indian individuals, not a broader international study involving epigenetic analysis and NCDs.



**4. A biomedical engineering discipline combines principles of materials science and cell transplantation to develop substitute tissues or promote endogenous regeneration. This discipline is crucial for creating artificial skin and cartilage and is expanding the field of regenerative medicine. Which field best describes this discipline?**

(a)  Xenotransplantation
(b)  Tissue Engineering
(c)  Stem Cell Therapy
(d)  CAR T-cell Therapy


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The description defines Tissue Engineering. This field uses principles of materials science and cell biology to create tissues and organs outside the body (in vitro) or to repair damaged tissues within the body (in vivo).  The examples of artificial skin and cartilage directly illustrate the applications of tissue engineering. This discipline is closely related to regenerative medicine but is not synonymous with stem cell therapy or CAR T-cell therapy.

Option (a) is incorrect because xenotransplantation involves using animal tissues or organs for transplantation into humans. Option (c) is incorrect because stem cell therapy focuses on the use of stem cells to treat diseases, but it doesn't encompass the complete process of tissue construction. Option (d) is incorrect because CAR T-cell therapy is a form of immunotherapy that modifies immune cells to target cancer.


**5. A recently approved cancer treatment uses genetically altered T cells to more effectively locate and destroy cancer cells.  This individualized treatment often requires only a single or a few infusions. Which of the following is this therapy?**

(a)  Enzyme Replacement Therapy
(b)  Mitochondrial Replacement Therapy
(c)  CAR T-cell Therapy
(d)  Gene Drive Technology


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The description clearly outlines the key features of CAR T-cell therapy. The use of genetically altered T cells to target and destroy cancer cells, the individualized nature of the treatment, and the requirement for only a few infusions are all hallmarks of this advanced immunotherapy.

Option (a) is incorrect because enzyme replacement therapy addresses enzyme deficiencies, not cancer. Option (b) is incorrect because mitochondrial replacement therapy deals with mitochondrial diseases, not cancer. Option (d) is incorrect because gene drive technology is a gene editing method used to alter inheritable traits in populations, not a direct cancer treatment.


**6.  Scientists have discovered a protein section that activates a larger protein, acting as a "kill switch" for cancer cells, triggering their self-destruction.  This discovery could lead to new cancer drugs that boost the activity of this receptor.  Which receptor is involved?**

(a)  CD19 receptor
(b)  CD95 receptor (Fas)
(c)  CRISPR-Cas9 system
(d)  Mitochondrial receptor


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The description focuses on the CD95 receptor (also known as Fas).  The text explicitly mentions the discovery of a crucial epitope on the CD95 receptor that triggers cancer cell death.  This receptor is involved in apoptosis (programmed cell death), and boosting its activity could be a novel approach for cancer treatment.

Option (a) is incorrect because the CD19 receptor is a biomarker for B cells, targeted in CAR T-cell therapy. Option (c) is incorrect because the CRISPR-Cas9 system is a gene editing tool, not a receptor. Option (d) is incorrect because mitochondrial receptors are involved in mitochondrial function, not directly in cancer cell death.


**7.  A type of vaccine uses a copy of messenger RNA (mRNA) to produce an immune response without exposing the individual to the actual virus. This mRNA instructs cells to produce a viral protein, triggering antibody production. What type of vaccine is described?**

(a)  DNA vaccine
(b)  Conventional vaccine (attenuated virus)
(c)  mRNA vaccine
(d)  Subunit vaccine


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The description accurately describes mRNA vaccines. These vaccines utilize mRNA encoding for a specific viral protein (like the spike protein in the case of COVID-19 vaccines) to induce an immune response.  This approach avoids using the actual virus or viral components, making it safer and faster to produce compared to traditional vaccines.

Option (a) is incorrect because DNA vaccines use plasmid DNA, not mRNA. Option (b) is incorrect because conventional vaccines use weakened or inactivated viruses. Option (d) is incorrect because subunit vaccines use purified viral proteins, not mRNA.


**8.  A technique uses genetic engineering to create a genetic element that increases its own likelihood of being inherited, promoting the inheritance of a specific trait at a rate higher than normal Mendelian inheritance. What is this technique?**

(a)  CRISPR-Cas9 gene editing
(b)  Gene drive technology
(c)  Recombinant DNA technology
(d)  Genome sequencing


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The description clearly defines gene drive technology. This technique employs genetic engineering to create a "self-replicating" genetic element that biases inheritance, ensuring a specific trait is passed on to offspring at a much higher rate than expected through typical Mendelian inheritance patterns.

Option (a) is incorrect because CRISPR-Cas9 is a gene editing tool, but it doesn't inherently increase the inheritance rate of a specific gene. Option (c) is incorrect because recombinant DNA technology involves combining DNA from different sources, without the specific mechanism of enhanced inheritance. Option (d) is incorrect because genome sequencing is a technique for determining the order of DNA nucleotides, not a gene editing technique.


**9. A genetically modified crop, commonly known as Bt cotton, carries a gene from the bacterium *Bacillus thuringiensis* that produces a protein toxic to certain pests.  What is the primary benefit of this modification?**

(a)  Increased herbicide tolerance
(b)  Enhanced nutrient content
(c)  Pest resistance
(d)  Improved drought tolerance


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The description clearly points to the primary benefit of Bt cotton: pest resistance.  The Bt gene produces a protein that is toxic to certain insects, reducing the need for chemical pesticides and increasing crop yield.

Option (a) is incorrect because herbicide tolerance is a trait conferred by different genes (e.g., *cp4 epsps*). Option (b) is incorrect because Bt modification doesn't primarily enhance nutrient content. Option (d) is incorrect because drought tolerance is a separate trait achieved through different genetic modifications.


**10.  A recently developed hybrid mustard variety, DMH-11, incorporates three alien genes to enhance yield and herbicide tolerance.  Which bacterium's genes are used in this modification?**

(a) *Bacillus thuringiensis*
(b) *Agrobacterium tumefaciens*
(c) *Escherichia coli*
(d) *Bacillus amyloliquefaciens*


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The question refers specifically to the DMH-11 hybrid mustard variety. The text states that this variety incorporates three alien genes isolated from *Bacillus amyloliquefaciens*.  These genes are involved in male sterility, fertility restoration, and herbicide tolerance.

Option (a) is incorrect because *Bacillus thuringiensis* genes are used in Bt cotton for pest resistance. Option (b) is incorrect because *Agrobacterium tumefaciens* is a bacterium used as a vector in plant transformation but is not the source of genes in DMH-11. Option (c) is incorrect because *Escherichia coli* is a bacterium frequently used in molecular biology but not involved in DMH-11 development.


These questions demand a deeper understanding of the concepts and specific details presented in the target content, fulfilling the requirements of a difficult UPSC-style MCQ.  They also avoid direct reproduction of the text, fulfilling the criteria of question quality.


Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging and requires a deep understanding of the subject matter.


**1.  A novel gene-editing technology significantly improves the pungency of an Indian mustard variety by reducing glucosinolates to levels comparable to canola.  Which technology was employed in this development?**

(a) Zinc finger nucleases (ZFNs)
(b) Transcription activator-like effector nucleases (TALENs)
(c) CRISPR/Cas9 gene editing technology
(d) Agrobacterium-mediated transformation

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly states that Indian researchers used CRISPR/Cas9 gene editing technology to develop a less pungent mustard variety.  ZFNs and TALENs are other gene-editing techniques, but the text specifies CRISPR/Cas9 in this instance. Agrobacterium-mediated transformation is a method of genetic modification used in creating GMOs, a distinct process from gene editing.  The question highlights the difference between gene editing and genetic modification, a crucial conceptual understanding in biotechnology. The focus on the specific technology used and the precise outcome (reduced pungency through glucosinolate reduction) elevates the difficulty level.  Understanding the nuances between different gene-editing techniques is essential for a comprehensive understanding of modern biotechnology.


**2.  A technique involving the removal and transfer of nuclear genetic material from one fertilized egg to another with healthy mitochondria aims to prevent the transmission of mitochondrial diseases.  What is this technique called?**

(a) Maternal Spindle Transfer (MST)
(b) Pronuclear Transfer (PNT)
(c) Mitochondrial Donation Treatment (MDT)
(d) All of the above

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The description accurately portrays Mitochondrial Donation Treatment (MDT), a procedure that involves using the genetic material of the parents and the mitochondrial material of a donor to conceive a child. Both Maternal Spindle Transfer (MST) and Pronuclear Transfer (PNT) are specific techniques used within MDT to achieve this goal. The question tests factual recall and conceptual understanding of the MDT procedure and its related techniques. While each option individually represents a correct aspect of the process, the comprehensive nature of the correct option (d) increases the difficulty level by requiring a full grasp of the interrelationship of these biotechnological approaches.


**3.  A type of fuel cell directly converts the chemical energy of methanol into electricity, offering advantages such as liquid fuel portability and high energy density. Which technology is described?**

(a)  Perovskite solar cells
(b)  Algae Assisted Fuel Cells (AFC)
(c) Direct Methanol Fuel Cells (DMFCs)
(d)  Vanadium Flow Batteries (VFBs)

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description perfectly matches Direct Methanol Fuel Cells (DMFCs).  The passage explicitly details their advantages: using methanol as a liquid fuel, high energy density, and compact design. Perovskite solar cells utilize light energy, not methanol. Algae Assisted Fuel Cells and Vanadium Flow Batteries use different energy sources and mechanisms.  The question assesses factual recall and the ability to match a technological description to its correct name. The inclusion of plausible distractors, each representing a different energy technology, makes the question challenging, requiring precise knowledge of the described fuel cell type.


**4.  A recent study revealed a correlation between a specific measure of how quickly a carbohydrate-containing food raises blood sugar levels and the risk of type II diabetes and cardiovascular diseases.  What is this measure called?**

(a) Glycemic Load (GL)
(b) Glycemic Index (GI)
(c)  Metabolic Rate
(d)  Insulin Sensitivity

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The passage defines the Glycemic Index (GI) as a measure of how quickly a carbohydrate-containing food raises blood sugar levels. Glycemic Load (GL) is related but incorporates the amount of carbohydrates in a serving.  Metabolic rate and insulin sensitivity are related to overall health but don't directly measure the speed of blood sugar increase from food. The question tests factual recall and the ability to connect a description to its specific term in the field of nutrition. The subtle differences between GL and GI, along with the inclusion of plausible but incorrect physiological measures, present a challenging scenario requiring precise knowledge.


**5.  The Artemis Accords, a set of non-binding principles guiding civil space exploration, emphasize several key commitments. Which of the following is NOT a primary commitment outlined in the Accords?**

(a) Peaceful purposes for space activities.
(b)  Registration and data sharing of space objects.
(c)  Exclusive utilization of space resources by signatory nations.
(d)  Mitigation of space debris.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The Artemis Accords promote the peaceful use of space, registration and data sharing, and debris mitigation.  However, they do *not* advocate for the exclusive utilization of space resources by signatory nations. Instead, they encourage sustainable and non-interfering resource utilization. The question tests understanding of international space law and policy. The option (c) represents a crucial distinction between cooperative and nationalistic approaches to space resource management, thus enhancing the difficulty of the question and demanding a precise understanding of the Accords' principles.


**6. Which of the following technologies is NOT directly related to spacecraft propulsion?**

(a) Ion Thruster Engine
(b) Rotating Detonation Rocket Engine (RDRE)
(c) Radioisotope Thermoelectric Generator (RTG)
(d)  Perovskite solar cells

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** Ion thrusters, RDREs, and RTGs are all propulsion systems or power sources for spacecraft. Perovskite solar cells, while used in space applications for power generation, are not directly involved in propulsion; they generate electricity but don't provide thrust. This question tests factual recall and the ability to differentiate between power generation and propulsion technologies in the context of space exploration. The inclusion of Perovskite solar cells, a relevant but distinct technology, increases the difficulty by requiring a nuanced understanding of spacecraft systems.


**7. The Indian Space Research Organisation (ISRO), in collaboration with another organization, is jointly developing Radioisotope Thermoelectric Generators (RTGs). Which organization is ISRO collaborating with for this development?**

(a)  Indian Institute of Science (IISc)
(b)  National Centre for Radio Astrophysics (NCRA)
(c)  Bhabha Atomic Research Centre (BARC)
(d)  Vikram Sarabhai Space Centre (VSSC)

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The text clearly states that ISRO is collaborating with the Bhabha Atomic Research Centre (BARC) on the development of RTGs.  The other options are involved in space research but are not the specific partner mentioned for this particular project. This question assesses factual recall of specific collaborations in the Indian space program. The inclusion of plausible distractors, all prominent Indian space research institutions, makes this a difficult question requiring precise knowledge of the ISRO-BARC partnership.


**8.  A recent study by IISER Kolkata attributed the loss of a significant number of satellites to a specific phenomenon related to the Sun's activity.  What is this phenomenon?**

(a) Solar flares
(b) Coronal mass ejections (CMEs)
(c) Space weather
(d) Geomagnetic storms

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage directly links the satellite loss to space weather, which encompasses solar flares, CMEs, and geomagnetic storms. While the other options are components of space weather, the study specifically attributed the satellite loss to the broader phenomenon of space weather conditions. This question tests the ability to understand the relationship between a cause (space weather) and effect (satellite loss), requiring more than just rote memorization of individual solar events. The use of a specific research institution (IISER Kolkata) adds another layer of detail, enhancing the question's difficulty.


**9.  A type of molecular machine within a cell converts chemical energy from ATP into mechanical work. What is this machine called?**

(a)  Ribosomes
(b)  Molecular motor
(c)  Mitochondria
(d)  Lysosomes

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The description clearly defines a molecular motor. Ribosomes are responsible for protein synthesis, mitochondria generate energy (though not directly in the described mechanical way), and lysosomes break down waste. This question assesses the ability to connect a function (energy conversion to mechanical work) with its corresponding cellular component. The presence of other organelles with related but distinct functions increases the difficulty, requiring precise knowledge of cellular biology.


**10.  A method of cultivating plant cells or tissues in a sterile environment on a nutrient medium is employed to generate saplings of rare tree species. What is this method called?**

(a)  Hydroponics
(b)  Cloning
(c)  Plant Tissue Culture (PTC)
(d)  Seed Germination

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description accurately defines Plant Tissue Culture (PTC). Hydroponics involves growing plants without soil, cloning creates genetically identical copies, and seed germination is the natural process of seed sprouting. This question tests factual recall and the ability to identify a specific plant propagation technique. The use of a specific application (generating saplings of rare species) and inclusion of plausible alternative methods elevate the difficulty level by demanding a clear understanding of PTC's role in plant propagation.


Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on science and technology.  The questions are designed to be challenging and assess various cognitive skills, with detailed explanations for each.


**1.  A chemical process converts vegetable oils or animal fats into fatty acid methyl esters (FAME).  This process is crucial for the production of which biofuel?**

(a) Biogas
(b) Ethanol
(c) Methanol
(d) Biodiesel

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The question directly describes the transesterification process, which is specifically used to create biodiesel. Biodiesel is a renewable fuel produced by chemically converting vegetable oils or animal fats into fatty acid methyl esters (FAMEs).  Options (a), (b), and (c) represent different biofuels produced through distinct processes. Biogas is produced through anaerobic digestion, while ethanol and methanol are typically produced through fermentation processes. The question highlights the specific chemical process and its link to a particular biofuel, testing factual recall and conceptual understanding.  The distractors are plausible alternatives, making the question challenging.



**2.  Which alternative fuel, when used in combustion, produces only water vapor as a byproduct, significantly reducing greenhouse gas emissions?**

(a) Biodiesel
(b) Ethanol
(c) Hydrogen
(d) Methanol

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** Hydrogen fuel cells, when operating ideally, produce only water vapor as a byproduct. This is a key advantage of hydrogen as a clean energy source, significantly reducing greenhouse gas emissions compared to fossil fuels.  Biodiesel, ethanol, and methanol, while renewable, still produce some carbon dioxide during combustion, though typically less than fossil fuels. The question tests conceptual understanding of the chemical processes involved in different fuel types and their environmental impact. The distractors are all alternative fuels but lack the defining characteristic of producing only water vapor.



**3.  Which battery technology, while offering lower costs and abundant material availability, currently faces challenges related to lower energy density compared to its more established counterpart?**

(a) Lithium-ion Battery
(b) Solid-state Battery
(c) Sodium-ion Battery
(d) Flow Battery

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** Sodium-ion batteries are a promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries due to the abundance and lower cost of sodium. However, current sodium-ion battery technology suffers from lower energy density compared to lithium-ion batteries, limiting its applicability in energy-intensive devices like electric vehicles.  The question tests knowledge of different battery chemistries and their relative advantages and disadvantages, demanding both factual recall and comparative analysis. The distractors represent other battery types with their own sets of strengths and weaknesses, making a direct comparison necessary for accurate selection.



**4.  The discovery of lithium deposits in Jammu & Kashmir is expected to significantly impact which aspect of the global energy landscape?**

(a) Production of solar panels
(b) Production of wind turbines
(c) Production of Lithium-ion batteries
(d) Production of hydrogen fuel cells

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** Lithium is a crucial component in lithium-ion batteries, which are widely used in portable electronics, electric vehicles, and energy storage systems. The discovery of lithium deposits in Jammu & Kashmir could potentially reduce India's reliance on imports of this critical material and influence the global supply chain for lithium-ion batteries. Solar panels, wind turbines, and hydrogen fuel cells do not directly utilize lithium in their primary components. The question assesses the interdisciplinary linkage between geology/resource availability and technological advancements in energy storage, requiring application of knowledge to a specific geopolitical context.


**5.  Which method, used in biofuel production, involves heating biomass in the absence of oxygen to break down organic materials into bio-oil, syngas, and biochar?**

(a) Transesterification
(b) Fermentation
(c) Pyrolysis
(d) Hydrogenation

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** Pyrolysis is a thermochemical process that involves heating biomass in the absence of oxygen. This leads to the breakdown of organic materials into various products, including bio-oil (a liquid fuel), syngas (a mixture of carbon monoxide and hydrogen), and biochar (a solid residue).  Transesterification is specific to biodiesel production; fermentation is used for ethanol production; and hydrogenation adds hydrogen to improve fuel properties. The question tests factual recall of specific biofuel production methods and their underlying chemical processes. The distractors are other methods used in biofuel production, making it crucial to understand the precise definition of pyrolysis.


**6.  What is the primary function of graphite in a lithium-ion battery?**

(a)  Acts as the electrolyte, facilitating ion movement.
(b)  Serves as the cathode material, where lithium ions migrate during charging.
(c)  Serves as the anode material, where lithium ions are stored during discharge.
(d)  Acts as a catalyst, speeding up chemical reactions.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** In a lithium-ion battery, graphite is the primary anode material. During the battery's discharge cycle, lithium ions move from the anode (graphite) to the cathode, generating an electric current.  The electrolyte facilitates ion movement between the electrodes, the cathode is typically a lithium metal oxide, and the graphite itself doesn't act as a catalyst in the same way as other battery components.  The question tests detailed knowledge of the components and functions within a lithium-ion battery, assessing factual recall and conceptual understanding.



**7. Which of the following is NOT a key advantage of Sodium-ion batteries compared to Lithium-ion batteries?**

(a) Abundance of Sodium
(b) Lower cost of materials
(c) Higher energy density
(d) Enhanced safety profile

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** While sodium-ion batteries benefit from the abundance and lower cost of sodium, leading to potential cost advantages and potentially enhanced safety, they currently lag behind lithium-ion batteries in terms of energy density.  This means that for the same size and weight, a lithium-ion battery can store and deliver more energy. The question focuses on identifying the limitation of sodium-ion batteries, requiring careful comparison and evaluation of their properties.



**8.  The Semi-Cryogenic Engine (SCE-200), developed by ISRO, uses which combination of propellants?**

(a) Liquid oxygen and liquid hydrogen
(b) Liquid oxygen and RP-1 kerosene
(c) Solid fuel and high-performance EPDM
(d) Ammonium nitrate and metallic powders

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The SCE-200 is designed to use liquid oxygen (LOX) as an oxidizer and RP-1 kerosene as fuel.  This distinguishes it from cryogenic engines that use liquid hydrogen, and solid-propellant rockets which utilize different fuel compositions.  The question directly tests factual recall of specific details about a particular rocket engine.



**9.  Which of the following is a characteristic of the Agnibaan SubOrbital Technological Demonstrator (SOrTeD)?**

(a) Uses a traditional liquid-propellant engine
(b) Is a multi-stage launch vehicle
(c) Features a 3D-printed, single-piece, semi-cryogenic engine
(d) Is exclusively designed for launching large satellites

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** A key feature of the Agnibaan SOrTeD is its use of the Agnilet engine, which is notable for being entirely 3D-printed.  This contrasts with traditional rocket engines and highlights a novel approach to manufacturing. The question tests knowledge of specific technological advancements in space launch vehicles.


**10. Which space mission aims to explore the chemistry and habitability of multiple surface sites on Saturn's moon Titan?**

(a) Juno Mission
(b) Dragonfly Mission
(c) Chandrayaan-3
(d) Aditya-L1

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The Dragonfly mission is explicitly designed to explore Titan, focusing on its surface chemistry and potential for habitability.  The other missions have different primary objectives. The question tests knowledge of specific space exploration initiatives and their targets.


Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is difficult, requiring in-depth understanding and analysis, and includes plausible distractors.


**1.  Considering the challenges in achieving room-temperature superconductivity, which of the following is NOT a significant hurdle?**

(a) The difficulty in maintaining extreme pressure conditions required for superconductivity in some materials.
(b) The inherent instability of Cooper pairs at temperatures above 0°C.
(c) The abundance of readily available materials exhibiting superconductivity at room temperature.
(d) The relatively high thermal energy at room temperature hindering Cooper pair formation.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The correct answer is (c) because the statement is factually incorrect.  Currently, achieving room-temperature superconductivity is a major scientific challenge.  There is a scarcity of materials that exhibit this property, and significant research is focused on discovering or synthesizing such materials. Options (a), (b), and (d) accurately reflect the difficulties encountered in achieving room-temperature superconductivity.  High thermal energy disrupts the delicate balance needed for Cooper pair formation, a crucial element in superconductivity.  Maintaining extreme pressure conditions is often necessary, but the materials themselves may not withstand these pressures.  Therefore, (c) stands out as the inaccurate statement.


**2.  Which of the following statements accurately describes the Meissner Effect?**

(a) The increase in electrical resistance of a superconductor when cooled below its critical temperature (Tc).
(b) The expulsion of a magnetic field from a superconductor as it transitions to a superconducting state below Tc.
(c) The generation of a magnetic field within a superconductor upon reaching its critical temperature.
(d) The phenomenon where electrons in a superconductor lose their paired state below Tc, resulting in resistance.

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Meissner effect is the hallmark of superconductivity. It describes the complete expulsion of a magnetic field from the interior of a superconductor below its critical temperature. This is a key characteristic distinguishing superconductors from perfect conductors. Option (a) is incorrect as superconductors exhibit zero resistance below Tc. Option (c) is the opposite of what happens; the magnetic field is expelled, not generated. Option (d) is also incorrect; Cooper pairs are essential for superconductivity and their formation, not disintegration, leads to zero resistance.


**3.  Regarding the recovery of Rare Earth Elements (REEs) from Red Mud, which strategy presents a more comprehensive approach?**

(a) Extracting only REEs, leaving other valuable metals in the Red Mud.
(b) Extracting all metals, including REEs, from the Red Mud.
(c) Discarding the Red Mud entirely, focusing solely on primary REE sources.
(d) Utilizing Red Mud only as a landfill material, ignoring its potential REE content.

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Red Mud is a highly toxic byproduct of aluminum production.  Option (b) represents a more sustainable and economically viable approach.  Extracting all valuable metals, including REEs, from Red Mud minimizes waste and maximizes resource utilization.  Option (a) is wasteful, as it leaves other potentially valuable metals unused. Option (c) ignores a significant source of REEs, leading to resource inefficiency and environmental concerns. Option (d) is environmentally irresponsible, ignoring the potential for resource recovery and waste reduction. The comprehensive extraction of all metals addresses both environmental and economic aspects.


**4.  Which of the following is NOT a characteristic of Vanadium?**

(a) It is a transition metal.
(b) It is found abundantly as a free element in nature.
(c) It can increase the tensile strength of steel.
(d) It has multiple oxidation states, contributing to its use in vanadium redox flow batteries.

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Vanadium is a transition metal with multiple oxidation states, making it useful in various applications, including steel alloys and vanadium redox flow batteries. However, vanadium is rarely found as a free element in nature; it typically occurs in various minerals. Options (a), (c), and (d) correctly describe properties and applications of vanadium.  The abundance as a free element is the inaccurate statement.


**5.  Which method of lab-grown diamond production utilizes a carbon-rich gas and plasma to crystallize carbon onto a seed diamond?**

(a) High-Temperature, High-Pressure (HPHT) method
(b) Chemical Vapor Deposition (CVD) method
(c)  Graphite sublimation method
(d)  High-energy electron beam method

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The CVD method uses a carbon-rich gas environment and plasma to deposit carbon atoms onto a seed diamond, layer by layer, to grow a larger diamond. The HPHT method uses high pressure and temperature to transform carbon into diamond.  The other options are not standard methods for lab-grown diamond production.


**6.  In the context of Giant Magnetoresistance (GMR), what determines the electrical resistance of the conductor sandwiched between two magnetic materials?**

(a) The temperature of the conductor.
(b) The type of material used for the conductor.
(c) The relative magnetization direction of the adjacent materials.
(d) The thickness of the conductor.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The core principle of GMR is the dependence of the conductor's resistance on the alignment of the magnetic fields in the adjacent layers.  Parallel alignment leads to low resistance, while anti-parallel alignment results in high resistance. While (a), (b), and (d) can influence resistance, they are not the defining factor in GMR.


**7.  Which of the following is NOT a typical application of Giant Magnetoresistance (GMR)?**

(a) Hard disk drives
(b) Magnetoresistive RAM
(c) Solar cells
(d) Biosensors

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

GMR is used in various applications where magnetic field sensitivity is crucial, such as hard disk drives, magnetoresistive RAM, and biosensors. Solar cells utilize the photovoltaic effect, not GMR.


**8.  Which of the following isotopes is used in radiometric dating, but has limitations due to its relatively short half-life?**

(a) Potassium-40
(b) Uranium-238
(c) Carbon-14
(d) Calcium-41

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Carbon-14 dating is widely used, but its 5,700-year half-life limits its application to relatively young samples.  Potassium-40, Uranium-238, and Calcium-41 have much longer half-lives, making them suitable for dating older materials.


**9.  The Draft National Strategy for Robotics (NSR) classifies robots into which three main categories?**

(a) Industrial, Service, and Military robots
(b) Industrial, Domestic, and Agricultural robots
(c) Industrial, Service, and Medical robots
(d) Domestic, Agricultural, and Military robots

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The NSR categorizes robots into Industrial, Service, and Medical robots, reflecting the broad range of applications.


**10. Which of the following is NOT a property of Tantalum?**

(a) High melting point
(b) High corrosion resistance
(c) High malleability and ductility
(d) Abundant occurrence in the Earth's crust

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Tantalum possesses a high melting point, excellent corrosion resistance, and good malleability and ductility. However, it is a rare metal, not abundant in the Earth's crust.


**11.  Which of the following statements best describes the working mechanism of a Vanadium Redox Flow Battery (VRFB)?**

(a) It stores energy chemically within a solid-state electrolyte.
(b) It utilizes vanadium ions in multiple oxidation states to store energy electrochemically in separate tanks.
(c) It employs lithium ions as the primary energy storage medium.
(d) It functions solely through capacitive energy storage.

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

VRFBs leverage the unique redox properties of vanadium ions in different oxidation states, stored in separate electrolyte tanks. This is a key distinction from other battery types.


**12. The Artemis Accords primarily focus on which aspect of space exploration?**

(a) Military applications of space technology.
(b) Commercialization of space resources without regulation.
(c) Principles for safe and sustainable civilian space exploration and utilization.
(d) Exclusive rights to specific celestial bodies for signatory nations.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Artemis Accords emphasize principles for safe, sustainable, and transparent civilian space exploration, building upon existing international space law.  They do not prioritize military applications or exclusive claims.


**13.  Which of the following is NOT a method used to detect exoplanets?**

(a) Transit Method
(b) Gravitational Microlensing
(c)  Direct Imaging with high-resolution telescopes
(d)  Radio Wave Detection

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

While (c) is challenging due to the brightness of the host star, it is a valid method. The transit and microlensing methods are indirect detections. Radio wave detection is not a primary method for exoplanet detection.


**14.  What is the primary function of a Radioisotope Thermoelectric Generator (RTG)?**

(a) To generate propulsion for spacecraft using solar energy.
(b) To convert heat from radioactive decay into electricity for spacecraft.
(c) To regulate the temperature of spacecraft components.
(d) To communicate with Earth-based control centers.

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

RTGs utilize the heat generated from the radioactive decay of isotopes to produce electricity, making them particularly useful for long-duration missions far from the sun.


**15. What type of propulsion system does the Rotating Detonation Rocket Engine (RDRE) utilize?**

(a) Continuous deflagrative combustion
(b)  Continuous detonation wave
(c)  Solid-propellant combustion
(d)  Ion propulsion

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The RDRE is innovative in its use of a continuous detonation wave, unlike traditional rocket engines that rely on deflagrative combustion.

This comprehensive set of MCQs covers various aspects of science and technology, demanding a high level of understanding and analytical skills.  The distractors are carefully chosen to challenge even well-prepared candidates.


Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be difficult, requiring a deep understanding of the subject matter and careful consideration of the options.


**1.  Considering the various methods of delivering mRNA vaccines, which delivery system offers the most promising balance between stability, ease of administration, and efficacy, based on current understanding?**

(a) Free mRNA in solution
(b) Encapsulation in lipid nanoparticles (LNPs)
(c) Delivery via polymers
(d) Ex vivo delivery through dendritic cells


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Lipid nanoparticles (LNPs) currently represent the most successful and widely used delivery system for mRNA vaccines.  Their advantages stem from several key factors.  Firstly, LNPs provide significant stability to the inherently fragile mRNA molecule, protecting it from degradation by nucleases in the body. This enhanced stability translates to better efficacy, as a higher proportion of the mRNA reaches its target cells.  Secondly, LNPs are relatively easy to administer via intramuscular injection, a standard and well-established method.  Finally, the clinical trials of mRNA vaccines using LNPs, notably the Pfizer-BioNTech and Moderna COVID-19 vaccines, have demonstrated high efficacy and safety profiles.  In contrast, free mRNA in solution is highly unstable and quickly degrades. Polymer-based delivery systems are still under development and face challenges in terms of biocompatibility and efficacy. Ex vivo delivery through dendritic cells is a complex and less scalable approach, limiting its widespread applicability.  Therefore, LNPs represent the current gold standard in mRNA vaccine delivery, balancing stability, ease of administration, and efficacy.


**2. A researcher is studying the immune response to a novel pathogen.  They observe a rapid and effective response upon second exposure to the pathogen, a response significantly stronger than the initial encounter.  This phenomenon is best described as:**

(a) Innate immunity
(b) Passive immunity
(c) Immunological memory
(d) Autoimmunity


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The described scenario perfectly illustrates immunological memory, a hallmark of adaptive immunity.  Upon first exposure to a pathogen, the immune system mounts a primary response, which is relatively slow and less effective.  However, this initial response generates memory B and T cells. These memory cells "remember" the specific pathogen and upon re-exposure, mount a secondary response that is much faster, more potent, and more effective at clearing the pathogen.  This is fundamentally different from innate immunity, which is a non-specific, immediate response. Passive immunity involves the transfer of pre-formed antibodies or immune cells, not the generation of memory cells. Autoimmunity is an inappropriate immune response against self-antigens, not a heightened response to a previously encountered pathogen.  Therefore, immunological memory is the only option accurately describing the observed phenomenon.


**3.  A patient presents with symptoms consistent with a mitochondrial disease.  Which of the following advanced reproductive technologies would be most appropriate to prevent the transmission of this disease to the patient's offspring?**

(a) In-vitro fertilization (IVF) alone
(b) Preimplantation genetic diagnosis (PGD) alone
(c) Mitochondrial replacement therapy (MRT)
(d)  Artificial insemination


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Mitochondrial replacement therapy (MRT) is specifically designed to address the transmission of mitochondrial diseases.  These diseases are caused by mutations in mitochondrial DNA, which is inherited maternally.  MRT involves replacing the mother's faulty mitochondria with healthy mitochondria from a donor egg.  While IVF can assist with conception, it does not address the underlying mitochondrial issue. PGD can screen embryos for genetic defects, but it cannot correct mitochondrial DNA mutations. Artificial insemination is irrelevant to mitochondrial diseases, which are related to the egg's cytoplasmic components, not the sperm. Therefore, MRT is the only viable option for preventing the transmission of mitochondrial diseases to future generations.


**4. Which of the following best describes the primary mechanism by which an mRNA vaccine triggers an immune response?**

(a) Direct integration of mRNA into the host genome.
(b) Production of viral proteins by the host cell, leading to antibody production.
(c) Suppression of host cell gene expression to prevent viral replication.
(d) Activation of the innate immune system through direct recognition of mRNA.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

mRNA vaccines work by instructing the host cell to produce viral proteins.  The mRNA, encapsulated in a lipid nanoparticle, enters the host cell's cytoplasm. The cellular machinery then translates the mRNA into viral proteins, specifically those found on the surface of the target virus (e.g., the spike protein in COVID-19 vaccines).  These viral proteins are displayed on the cell surface, triggering an immune response.  The immune system recognizes these proteins as foreign and mounts an attack, producing antibodies and activating T cells.  mRNA vaccines do *not* integrate into the host genome. They do not suppress host gene expression. While the innate immune system plays a role, the primary mechanism is the production of viral proteins that stimulate the adaptive immune response.


**5.  A new drug is being developed to treat a rare genetic disorder. This drug uses a modified virus to deliver a functional gene into the patient's cells. This therapeutic approach is best classified as:**


(a) Enzyme Replacement Therapy (ERT)
(b) Somatic cell gene therapy
(c) Germline gene therapy
(d)  Immunotherapy


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The described therapeutic approach falls under somatic cell gene therapy.  Somatic cell gene therapy targets the patient's somatic cells (body cells, excluding germline cells).  It introduces a functional gene to correct a genetic defect.  The use of a modified virus as a vector is a common technique in gene therapy. Enzyme replacement therapy (ERT) involves providing the missing enzyme, not a functional gene. Germline gene therapy modifies germline cells (sperm or egg cells), resulting in heritable changes, which is ethically controversial and often prohibited. Immunotherapy uses the immune system to fight disease, not gene correction.  Therefore, somatic cell gene therapy accurately describes this type of treatment.


**6. Which of the following accurately describes the key difference between a shallowfake and a deepfake?**

(a) Shallowfakes utilize AI, while deepfakes do not.
(b) Shallowfakes are less sophisticated and easier to create than deepfakes.
(c) Shallowfakes are always videos, while deepfakes can be images or audio.
(d) Shallowfakes target individuals, while deepfakes target groups.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The key distinction between shallowfakes and deepfakes lies in their sophistication and the technology used to create them. Deepfakes employ advanced artificial intelligence algorithms, particularly generative adversarial networks (GANs), to synthesize highly realistic and convincing altered media.  Shallowfakes, on the other hand, use simpler, more readily available techniques such as video editing software or audio manipulation tools.  This makes them easier and less expensive to create.  While both types of manipulated media can be harmful, deepfakes pose a greater threat due to their higher level of realism and potential for deception. The other options present inaccurate information about the distinctions between shallowfakes and deepfakes.


**7. In the context of the immune system, which cells are primarily responsible for presenting antigens to T cells, initiating the adaptive immune response?**

(a) Natural Killer (NK) cells
(b) B cells and T cells themselves
(c) Macrophages and Dendritic cells
(d) Antibodies


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Antigen-presenting cells (APCs) are crucial for initiating the adaptive immune response.  Macrophages and dendritic cells are the most important APCs. They engulf pathogens or cellular debris, process the antigens, and display them on their surface using Major Histocompatibility Complex (MHC) molecules.  This presentation allows T cells to recognize the antigen and initiate a targeted immune response.  NK cells are part of the innate immune system and do not primarily present antigens.  While B cells can also present antigens, they are less efficient at doing so compared to macrophages and dendritic cells. Antibodies are proteins produced by B cells that bind to antigens, but they do not directly present antigens to T cells.


**8.  Which type of immunity is acquired through the transfer of antibodies or activated T cells from an immune host, providing temporary protection?**

(a) Active Immunity
(b) Innate Immunity
(c) Adaptive Immunity
(d) Passive Immunity


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Passive immunity is characterized by the transfer of pre-formed antibodies or activated T cells from one individual to another. This transfer provides immediate, but temporary, protection.  The recipient's immune system does not actively participate in generating the immunity.  Active immunity, in contrast, develops after exposure to an antigen (through infection or vaccination), leading to the production of memory cells and long-lasting immunity. Innate immunity is the non-specific, immediate, first line of defense. Adaptive immunity encompasses both active and passive immunity, but passive immunity is a distinct subtype.


**9. The  "Meissner effect" is associated with which phenomenon in materials science?**

(a)  The generation of electricity in a material through the application of heat
(b) The expulsion of a magnetic field from a superconductor as it cools below its critical temperature
(c) The increase in electrical resistance of a material as its temperature decreases
(d) The ability of a material to transmit light without significant loss


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Meissner effect is a defining characteristic of superconductivity.  When a superconductor is cooled below its critical temperature, it expels magnetic fields from its interior. This expulsion of the magnetic field is a unique property, not observed in normal conductors.  Options (a), (c), and (d) describe other phenomena in materials science, such as thermoelectricity, the behavior of normal conductors, and optical transparency, respectively.  These are not related to the Meissner effect.


**10.  Which of the following best describes the function of chondrocytes?**


(a) Production of red blood cells
(b) Production of antibodies
(c) Production and maintenance of cartilage
(d)  Production of hormones


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Chondrocytes are specialized cells responsible for the production and maintenance of cartilage, a connective tissue found in joints, ears, nose, etc.  They secrete the extracellular matrix of cartilage, which provides structural support and flexibility.  Red blood cell production occurs in bone marrow, antibody production is carried out by B cells, and hormone production is the function of endocrine glands.  These are not functions of chondrocytes.


Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is followed by a detailed explanation.


**1.  A novel approach to enhancing disease pandemic preparedness, acknowledging that similar systems and tools can be applied across pathogen groups based on transmission modes, is described by which initiative?**

(a)  International Pathogen Surveillance Network (IPSN)
(b)  SPECS 2030 Initiative
(c)  Preparedness and Resilience for Emerging Threats (PRET) Initiative
(d)  The Big Catch-Up


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The PRET Initiative is explicitly described as an innovative approach to improving pandemic preparedness by leveraging existing systems and tools for different pathogen groups categorized by their transmission methods (respiratory, vector-borne, foodborne, etc.).  This directly addresses the question's description. Option (a), IPSN, focuses on detection and reporting of infectious diseases.  Option (b), SPECS 2030, targets vision impairment and blindness. Option (d), The Big Catch-Up, aims to increase childhood vaccination rates. These options, while relevant to public health, do not match the specific description of a novel approach to pandemic preparedness based on shared systems and transmission modes.  The PRET Initiative's multi-pathogen, systems-based approach distinguishes it from the other options, making it the most appropriate answer.


**2. Which technology, developed at CERN for sub-nanosecond synchronization accuracy, was later incorporated into the Precision Time Protocol (PTP) and aims for wider industry adoption via the White Rabbit Collaboration (WRC)?**

(a)  Global Positioning System (GPS) Spoofing
(b)  White Rabbit (WR) Technology
(c)  Mercenary Spyware
(d)  Shallowfake


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The question directly describes White Rabbit (WR) Technology, its development at CERN, its sub-nanosecond accuracy, its inclusion in PTP, and the WRC's efforts to promote its broader industry use.  Option (a), GPS Spoofing, is a cyberattack technique. Option (c), Mercenary Spyware, refers to malicious software. Option (d), Shallowfake, describes a type of manipulated media. These options are unrelated to the technology described in the question.  The detailed description of WR's features and its connection to CERN and the WRC makes (b) the only correct answer.  This question tests factual recall and understanding of specific technological advancements.


**3.  The Indian government's approval for environmental release, granted in October 2022, pertains to which genetically modified crop, developed by crossing an Indian mustard variety with an East European mutant and incorporating three alien genes?**

(a)  GM Cotton (Bt Cotton)
(b)  HT Bt Cotton
(c)  GM Mustard (DMH-11)
(d)  Terminator Seeds


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question clearly points to GM Mustard (DMH-11), specifying its development through a cross between Indian and East European varieties and the inclusion of three genes from *Bacillus amyloliquefaciens*. The October 2022 approval is explicitly linked to this specific GM crop. Option (a), GM Cotton, is a different genetically modified crop. Option (b), HT Bt Cotton, is a herbicide-tolerant variant of Bt cotton, not the subject of the 2022 approval. Option (d), Terminator Seeds, refers to a technology for producing sterile seeds. These options are all related to genetically modified organisms but do not match the specifics of the question regarding the approved crop and its development. The precise details provided in the question make (c) the unequivocally correct answer, testing factual recall and specific knowledge of agricultural biotechnology.


**4. Which of the following is NOT a method used in the genetic modification of cotton plants to produce Bt cotton?**

(a) Agrobacterium-mediated transformation
(b) Particle bombardment (biolistics)
(c) Electroporation
(d) CRISPR-Cas9 gene editing


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The text explicitly lists Agrobacterium-mediated transformation, particle bombardment, and electroporation as methods used in Bt cotton production. CRISPR-Cas9 is a more recent gene editing technology, but the passage does not mention its use in the creation of Bt cotton.  While CRISPR-Cas9 is a powerful gene editing tool used in plant biotechnology, its absence from the described methods for Bt cotton production makes it the correct answer. This question tests factual recall and the ability to identify specific techniques within a broader field of biotechnology.  The other options are all methods described in the text.


**5.  The Indian initiative under the Department of Biotechnology aimed at elucidating biological and non-biological risks associated with premature birth, leading to the identification of single nucleotide polymorphisms (SNPs) as genetic markers, is known as:**

(a)  Genome India Project
(b)  GARBH-Ini
(c)  DEEP Project
(d)  National Quantum Mission


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The question describes the GARBH-Ini initiative, its focus on premature birth risk factors, and the resulting identification of SNPs.  Option (a), the Genome India Project, is a different large-scale genomics initiative. Option (c), the DEEP Project, focuses on epigenetic epidemiology. Option (d), the National Quantum Mission, is unrelated to biotechnology or medicine.  The question's specific description of the initiative's goals and outcomes makes (b) the only correct choice. This assesses factual recall and understanding of specific Indian research programs.  The other options are broad national initiatives that do not fit the described criteria.


**6.  Which type of cellular immunotherapy utilizes genetically altered T cells to target and destroy cancer cells more effectively, and has an indigenous version (NexCar19) approved by CDSCO in India?**

(a)  Stem Cell Therapy
(b)  CAR-T Cell Therapy
(c)  Tissue Engineering
(d)  Phage Therapy


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The question directly describes CAR-T cell therapy, its mechanism of action, and the specific example of NexCar19's approval in India. Option (a), Stem Cell Therapy, is a different type of cellular therapy. Option (c), Tissue Engineering, involves creating or repairing tissues. Option (d), Phage Therapy, uses bacteriophages to treat bacterial infections. These options are all relevant to biomedicine but do not match the specific description of genetically modified T cells targeting cancer.  The detailed description of CAR-T cell therapy and the mention of NexCar19 make (b) the unambiguous correct answer, testing factual recall and understanding of specific medical technologies.


**7. A rare, long-lived radioisotope with a half-life of 99,400 years, produced by cosmic ray interactions in soil and found in the Earth's crust, offering potential for radiometric dating similar to Carbon-14 but with a longer timeframe, is:**

(a) Carbon-14
(b) Potassium-40
(c) Argon-40
(d) Calcium-41


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The question describes Calcium-41, highlighting its rarity, long half-life, formation through cosmic ray interactions, and its potential application in radiometric dating as an alternative to Carbon-14 for older materials.  Option (a), Carbon-14, is a well-known radioisotope used in dating, but its shorter half-life limits its applicability. Options (b) and (c), Potassium-40 and Argon-40, are also used in radiometric dating, but they are not the focus of the description. The unique characteristics of Calcium-41 as described in the question make (d) the only correct answer. This tests factual recall of less commonly known isotopes and their applications in scientific dating techniques.


**8. Which type of robot is NOT explicitly categorized in the Draft National Strategy for Robotics (NSR) released by the Ministry of Electronics and Information Technology (MeitY)?**

(a) Industrial Robots
(b) Service Robots
(c) Military Robots
(d) Medical Robots


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The text explicitly mentions Industrial, Service, and Medical Robots as categories within the NSR.  Military robots are not explicitly listed as a separate category in the provided description of the NSR, although they could fall under a broader category.  While military applications of robotics are certainly relevant, the absence of explicit mention in the NSR makes (c) the correct answer. This question tests the ability to carefully read and interpret information from a document, focusing on specific details.  The other options are all categories explicitly named in the text.

**1.  A rare, long-lived radioisotope crucial for a dating technique that overcomes the limitations of Carbon-14 dating for older objects is:**

(a) Potassium-40
(b) Argon-40
(c) Calcium-41
(d) Carbon-12

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The question focuses on radiometric dating and its limitations. Carbon-14 dating is limited to objects younger than approximately 50,000 years. The passage introduces Calcium-41 as a longer-lived radioisotope (half-life of 99,400 years) used in Atom-Trap Trace Analysis (ATTA) to date older materials.  Potassium-40 and Argon-40 are also used in radiometric dating, but the passage specifically highlights Calcium-41 as an alternative to Carbon-14 for older objects. Carbon-12 is the most abundant isotope of carbon and is not directly used in radiometric dating for age determination.  The correct answer pinpoints a specific detail demonstrating knowledge beyond basic radiometric dating principles.

**9.  Which of the following statements accurately describes the Meissner Effect?**

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on science and technology.  Each question is designed to be challenging and assess various cognitive skills, with detailed explanations for the correct answer and analysis of the distractors.

**1.  A novel method of altering an organism's DNA, potentially impacting physical traits and disease risk, utilizes site-directed nucleases (SDNs) to introduce small deletions, substitutions, or nucleotide additions.  Which category of this DNA modification technique does NOT involve the introduction of foreign genetic material, resulting in an outcome indistinguishable from conventionally bred varieties?**

(a) SDN 3
(b) CRISPR/Cas9
(c) SDN 1 and SDN 2
(d) TALENs


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The question describes genome editing using site-directed nucleases (SDNs).  The text specifically states that SDN 1 and SDN 2 techniques do not incorporate alien genetic material.  The end product is identical to those achieved through conventional breeding methods.  This contrasts with SDN 3, which involves genes from foreign sources.  CRISPR/Cas9 and TALENs are specific genome editing tools, but the question focuses on the broader categorization of SDN methods.  Therefore, option (c) accurately reflects the described characteristics of genome editing that avoids the introduction of foreign genetic material. Options (a), (b), and (d) represent methods that may or may not incorporate foreign genetic material, making them incorrect choices given the question's specific criteria.  Understanding the nuances of SDN categories is crucial for a comprehensive understanding of modern biotechnology.


**2. The development of a less pungent mustard variety involved gene editing of an existing high-yielding Indian mustard variety using a specific technology. This technology, known for its precision in targeting specific DNA sequences, is also used in gene drive technology and other genome editing applications. Identify the technology employed.**

(a) Zinc finger nucleases (ZFNs)
(b) Transcription activator-like effector nucleases (TALENs)
(c) CRISPR/Cas9
(d) Recombinant DNA technology


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The passage explicitly mentions the use of CRISPR/Cas9 technology in developing the low-pungent mustard variety.  While ZFNs and TALENs are other gene-editing techniques, the passage directly links CRISPR/Cas9 to this specific application.  Recombinant DNA technology is a broader concept encompassing gene transfer across species, which is distinct from the targeted gene editing described in the question.  The question tests factual recall of specific details within the text and the ability to connect the technology to its application. The other options, while relevant to gene editing, are not the specific technology used in this instance.  Understanding the different gene-editing tools and their applications is key to grasping advancements in agricultural biotechnology and its implications.


**3.  A recently approved enzyme replacement therapy (ERT) utilizes a genetically engineered protein product indicated for on-demand treatment of a rare blood clotting disorder.  What is the name of the first recombinant protein product approved by the US Food and Drug Administration (USFDA) for this specific application?**

(a)  A novel molecular motor protein
(b)  Adzynma
(c)  A genetically modified (GM) enzyme
(d)  A CRISPR-Cas9 edited enzyme


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The passage clearly states that Adzynma is the world's first recombinant protein product approved by the USFDA for on-demand enzyme replacement therapy (ERT) to treat congenital thrombotic thrombocytopenic purpura (cTTP).  The other options are distractors.  While a molecular motor protein is mentioned elsewhere in the text, it is not related to ERT for cTTP.  A genetically modified (GM) enzyme or a CRISPR-Cas9 edited enzyme are general categories that do not specify the particular product.  The question assesses factual recall concerning specific biomedical advancements and the ability to identify the correct product name from a description.  The precise naming of drugs and therapies is important for clear communication in the healthcare sector.


**4. The National Hydrogen Mission in India aims to establish the country as a global leader in green hydrogen production.  Which of the following is NOT a stated target of this mission?**

(b)  Attracting over Rs. 8 lakh crore of investments.
(c)  Generating six lakh (600,000) new jobs.
(d)  Developing advanced liquefaction technologies for liquid helium.**


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The passage details the targets of India's National Hydrogen Mission.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are all explicitly stated targets.  Option (d), however, is incorrect. While the mission focuses on storage and transportation solutions including liquid hydrogen, it does not specifically mention developing liquefaction technologies for liquid helium.  The question assesses the ability to extract specific information from a larger text and distinguish between stated goals and implied or unrelated concepts.  Understanding the goals and strategies of national missions is crucial for analyzing India's approach to energy security and climate change mitigation.


**5.  A significant initiative aims to collect genetic samples from diverse Indian citizens to create a comprehensive reference genome.  This project, launched by the Department of Biotechnology (DBT), seeks to understand the genetic diversity of the Indian population.  What is the name of this initiative?**

The Human Genome Project is a global initiative completed in 2003, while the T2T Consortium focused on completing the human genome sequence.  The question tests factual recall of specific scientific initiatives in India and the ability to distinguish between similar-sounding projects.  Knowledge of ongoing genome projects is essential for understanding advancements in genomics and personalized medicine.
