Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging, requiring in-depth knowledge and understanding of the subject matter.


**1.  Which of the following accurately describes the Coulomb Barrier in the context of nuclear fusion?**

(a)  A protective layer surrounding the nucleus that prevents fusion reactions from occurring.
(b) The repulsive force between two positively charged atomic nuclei that hinders their fusion.
(c) A type of energy released during fusion that is currently harnessed for commercial applications.
(d) The specific state of matter (plasma) required to initiate and sustain a fusion reaction.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Coulomb Barrier is a fundamental challenge in achieving nuclear fusion.  Atomic nuclei, being positively charged, repel each other due to the electromagnetic force. This repulsive force, described by Coulomb's Law, increases dramatically as the nuclei get closer. To overcome this repulsion and initiate fusion, extremely high temperatures and pressures are needed to provide the kinetic energy necessary to force the nuclei close enough for the strong nuclear force to take over and bind them together. Option (a) is incorrect as there is no such protective layer; (c) is wrong because the energy released in fusion currently exceeds the energy required to initiate it, but the technology to efficiently harness the net energy is still under development; (d) is partially correct, as plasma is a necessary state, but it doesn't define the Coulomb Barrier itself.


**2.  The International Thermonuclear Experimental Reactor (ITER) project primarily aims to achieve which of the following milestones?**

(a)  The commercial production of antimatter for various industrial applications.
(b)  The development of a self-sustaining chain reaction in a thorium-based breeder reactor.
(c)  The demonstration of net energy gain from nuclear fusion reactions.
(d) The construction of the world's first commercially viable small modular reactor (SMR).


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

ITER's core objective is to demonstrate the scientific and technological feasibility of producing net energy from nuclear fusion. This means achieving a point where the energy generated by the fusion reactions exceeds the energy input required to initiate and maintain the reaction.  This is a crucial step towards developing fusion power as a viable energy source. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect. Antimatter production is a separate field of research; thorium reactors are a type of fission reactor, not fusion; and while SMR development is ongoing, it's not the primary goal of ITER.


**3.  Which of the following statements correctly identifies a key characteristic of Pressurized Heavy Water Reactors (PHWRs), as employed in India's nuclear power program?**

(a) They utilize highly enriched uranium as fuel, requiring complex enrichment processes.
(b) They employ fast neutrons to efficiently breed more fissile material than consumed.
(c) They use natural uranium as fuel and heavy water as a moderator.
(d) They operate at atmospheric pressure, enhancing inherent safety features.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

PHWRs are a type of thermal reactor that uses natural uranium as fuel.  Heavy water (D2O) acts as a moderator, slowing down neutrons to increase the probability of fission in the uranium fuel. This is a key feature of India's three-stage nuclear program. Option (a) is incorrect because PHWRs use natural, not enriched, uranium; (b) describes fast breeder reactors, a different reactor type; and (d) describes a characteristic of some advanced reactor designs, not PHWRs.


**4. The Advanced Liquid Processing System (ALPS) is primarily designed for which purpose?**

(a)  Enrichment of uranium to weapons-grade levels.
(b)  Treatment of contaminated water from nuclear power plants.
(c)  The separation of isotopes of hydrogen for fusion reactors.
(d)  The production of Molybdenum-99 for medical applications.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

ALPS is a system specifically developed to treat radioactive water contaminated from nuclear accidents, such as the Fukushima Daiichi disaster.  It uses a series of chemical and physical processes to remove radionuclides, rendering the water safe for release or reuse. Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect; uranium enrichment is a different process; hydrogen isotope separation is related to fusion; and Molybdenum-99 production is a separate nuclear process.


**5. Which of the following accurately describes the significance of achieving "criticality" in a nuclear reactor?**

(a) The reactor has reached its maximum power output and is operating at full capacity.
(b) The reactor has successfully undergone its initial testing phase and is ready for operation.
(c)  The number of neutrons produced by fission reactions is sufficient to sustain a self-sustaining chain reaction.
(d) The reactor's safety systems have been fully activated and are functioning optimally.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

"Criticality" in a nuclear reactor refers to the state where the chain reaction is self-sustaining.  A sufficient number of neutrons from each fission event cause further fissions, maintaining the reaction without external neutron sources. This is a crucial condition for sustained power generation. Options (a), (b), and (d) describe different aspects of reactor operation but not the definition of criticality.


**6. Which of the following individuals is widely recognized for their significant contribution to the Manhattan Project?**

(a)  Julius Robert Oppenheimer
(b)  Albert Einstein
(c)  Enrico Fermi
(d)  Niels Bohr


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Julius Robert Oppenheimer played a central and leading role in the Manhattan Project, the top-secret American initiative during World War II to develop the first atomic bombs.  He was the scientific director of the Los Alamos Laboratory, overseeing the design and construction of the atomic weapons. While Einstein and Fermi were prominent physicists of the time, and Bohr made significant contributions to nuclear physics, Oppenheimer was the key figure in the Manhattan Project’s leadership.


**7.  What is the primary fuel used in the Prototype Fast Breeder Reactor (PFBR) at Kalpakkam, India, during its initial operational phase?**

(a) Natural uranium
(b) Thorium-232
(c) Uranium-Plutonium Mixed Oxide (MOX) fuel
(d) Highly enriched uranium


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The PFBR at Kalpakkam initially utilizes Uranium-Plutonium Mixed Oxide (MOX) fuel. This fuel blend, containing both uranium and plutonium oxides, is essential for the fast breeder reactor's ability to breed more fissile material than it consumes. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect fuel choices for this specific reactor type during its initial phase.


**8. The "Agnilet" engine, a key component of the Agnibaan SubOrbital Technological Demonstrator (SOrTeD), is notable for being:**

(a)  A hybrid engine combining solid and liquid propellants.
(b)  A fully 3D-printed, single-piece, semi-cryogenic engine.

(d)  An all-solid-propellant engine with enhanced thrust capabilities.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Agnilet engine distinguishes itself through its innovative 3D-printing technique.  Being entirely 3D-printed as a single piece makes it a significant advancement in rocket engine manufacturing, simplifying the assembly process and potentially reducing costs. The other options describe different engine types but not the unique feature of the Agnilet engine.


**9. Which of the following best describes the primary function of the International Monitoring System (IMS) established under the Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty (CTBT)?**

(a) To conduct on-site inspections of suspected nuclear test sites.
(b) To negotiate and enforce sanctions against countries violating the CTBT.
(c) To detect potential nuclear explosions through a global network of monitoring stations.
(d) To provide technical assistance to countries developing nuclear energy for peaceful purposes.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The IMS is a crucial component of the CTBT's verification regime. Its extensive network of monitoring stations globally detects seismic, infrasound, radionuclide, and hydroacoustic signals, providing early warning of potential nuclear explosions anywhere in the world.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are related to the CTBT but not the core function of the IMS.


**10.  The "ITER" project, a major international collaboration, focuses on which area of energy production?**

(a) Solar energy harnessing through advanced photovoltaic cells.
(b) Nuclear fission using thorium-based breeder reactors.
(c) Nuclear fusion energy generation.
(d) Geothermal energy extraction through deep drilling techniques.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

ITER (International Thermonuclear Experimental Reactor) is a global collaboration dedicated to developing and testing nuclear fusion technology.  Its primary goal is to achieve controlled and sustained fusion reactions to generate energy. The other options represent different energy technologies.

**14.  In the context of nuclear reactors, what does the term "moderator" refer to?**

(a) A material that absorbs neutrons to control the chain reaction.
(b) A material that reflects neutrons back into the core to enhance fission.
(c) A material that slows down neutrons to increase the probability of fission.
(d) A material that shields the reactor from radiation.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** A moderator's primary role is to slow down fast neutrons, increasing their likelihood of causing fission in the fuel.  This is crucial for maintaining a controlled chain reaction in thermal reactors.  The other options describe other reactor components or functions.


**15. Which country is home to the world's largest experimental nuclear fusion reactor, JT-60SA?**

(c) Russia
(d) Japan

**16. What is the approximate percentage of uranium-235 (U-235) in naturally occurring uranium?**

(a) 99.27%
(b) 90%
(c) 3-5%
(d) 0.7%


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** Naturally occurring uranium contains only about 0.7% U-235, the fissile isotope.  Enrichment processes are needed to increase this percentage for use in most nuclear reactors.


**17. What is the primary function of the “Tamir” interceptor missiles in the Iron Dome air defense system?**

**18.  What is the primary purpose of the "Design Linked Incentive (DLI) Scheme" within India's semiconductor mission?**

**19. Which of the following best describes the "Photolithography" process in semiconductor manufacturing?**

**22. What does the acronym "ATMP" stand for in the context of the Indian semiconductor industry?**

**23. In the context of space technology, what is the primary function of a “tokamak”?**

(d)  A type of satellite used for Earth observation.

**24. Which of the following best describes the "Goldilocks zone" in the context of exoplanets?**

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:** The Goldilocks zone, also known as the habitable zone, refers to the orbital region around a star where conditions are considered suitable for liquid water to exist on a planet's surface.  This is considered an essential factor for life as we know it.


**25. Which of the following is NOT a characteristic feature of Small Modular Reactors (SMRs)?**

**26. Which of the following is a significant advantage of thorium reactors over traditional uranium-based reactors?**

**Explanation:** Thorium reactors are known for producing significantly less long-lived radioactive waste compared to uranium-based reactors, making them a more sustainable option.

Here are some difficult multiple-choice questions (MCQs) based on the provided target content, designed to assess various cognitive skills and avoid simple guessing.  Each question includes a detailed explanation.


**1.  A novel radiometric dating technique utilizes a rare, long-lived calcium isotope found in the Earth's crust. Which isotope is this, and what is a key limitation of its use compared to a more commonly used radioisotope?**

(a) Calcium-40; its shorter half-life limits its application to younger samples.
(b) Calcium-41; its less frequent occurrence compared to carbon-14 restricts its applicability.
(c) Calcium-42; its high reactivity makes sample collection challenging.
(d) Calcium-43; its instability renders accurate dating impossible.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The correct answer is (b) Calcium-41; its less frequent occurrence compared to carbon-14 restricts its applicability.  The passage explicitly states that Calcium-41 is a rare, long-lived radioisotope used in radiometric dating,  offering an alternative to carbon-14.  A key limitation highlighted is its less frequent occurrence than carbon-14, implying that finding sufficient quantities in a sample for accurate dating would be more difficult. Option (a) is incorrect because the passage emphasizes Calcium-41's rarity, not a shorter half-life. Option (c) is incorrect as there's no mention of Calcium-42's reactivity. Option (d) is incorrect because the passage describes Calcium-41 as long-lived, implying stability for dating purposes. The comparative rarity of Calcium-41, compared to the established use of Carbon-14, makes it a more challenging, albeit potentially valuable, tool in radiometric dating.  The question tests factual recall and analytical comparison of different radioisotopes used in dating.


**2.  The Draft National Strategy for Robotics (NSR) categorizes robots into specific types. Which of the following is NOT a category of robots as defined by the NSR?**

(a) Industrial Robots
(b) Agricultural Robots
(c) Service Robots
(d) Medical Robots


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The correct answer is (b) Agricultural Robots. The passage explicitly lists Industrial, Service, and Medical Robots as the categories defined by the NSR.  While agricultural applications of robotics are certainly relevant to technological advancements, the NSR's classification, as presented in the text, does not include this specific category. Options (a), (c), and (d) are directly mentioned in the text as categories within the NSR framework. This question tests factual recall and precise understanding of the NSR's classification system.  The absence of "Agricultural Robots" from the listed categories highlights the specificity of the NSR's current focus.


**3. A new study employed hybrid nanoparticles for both cancer cell detection and treatment. What are the key properties of these nanoparticles that enable these dual functionalities?**

(a)  High thermal conductivity and biodegradability
(b) Photoacoustic and photothermal properties
(c) Magnetic resonance and radioluminescence
(d)  Electrical conductivity and high surface area


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The correct answer is (b) Photoacoustic and photothermal properties. The passage explicitly states that the hybrid nanoparticles, made of gold and copper sulfide, utilize their photoacoustic properties for detection (absorbing light and generating ultrasound waves) and their photothermal properties for treatment (producing heat to kill tumor cells).  Options (a), (c), and (d) are not directly linked to the described dual functionalities of these specific nanoparticles in the provided context. This question tests conceptual understanding and the application of nanoparticle properties to specific biomedical applications. The combination of photoacoustic and photothermal properties demonstrates a sophisticated approach to cancer treatment and diagnosis.


**4.  Which of the following statements accurately describes the mechanism by which weight loss drugs, mimicking the action of GLP-1, achieve their effect?**

(a) They directly inhibit fat absorption in the intestines.
(b) They increase insulin production and decrease glucagon production.
(c) They increase metabolic rate, leading to increased calorie expenditure.
(d) They directly suppress the brain's hunger center.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The correct answer is (b) They increase insulin production and decrease glucagon production. The passage explains that GLP-1 increases insulin production (lowering blood sugar) and reduces glucagon production (reducing blood sugar increase). Weight loss drugs that mimic GLP-1, therefore, achieve their effect through this hormonal regulation. Option (a) is incorrect because the passage doesn't mention direct fat absorption inhibition. Option (c) is incorrect; while weight loss might indirectly influence metabolic rate, the primary mechanism is hormonal. Option (d) is incorrect; the passage doesn't describe direct suppression of the hunger center. This question tests conceptual understanding of the physiological mechanisms of weight loss drugs and their relation to specific hormones.  The precise hormonal effects are crucial to understanding the drugs' efficacy.


**5. The use of which substance in food items prompted a warning from the Tamil Nadu Commissioner of Food Safety, citing potential harmful effects?**

Options (a), (b), and (d) are mentioned in the passage but are not the subject of the Tamil Nadu warning. This question tests factual recall regarding specific safety concerns and regulatory actions related to food safety.  The commissioner's warning highlights the potential risks of using cryogenic substances in food handling.

**9. What is the relationship between the Glycemic Index (GI) and the risk of Type II diabetes and cardiovascular diseases?**

(a) High GI foods reduce the risk of Type II diabetes and cardiovascular diseases
(b) There is no established relationship between GI and Type II diabetes or cardiovascular diseases.
(c) High GI foods increase the risk of Type II diabetes and cardiovascular diseases
(d) Low GI foods increase the risk of Type II diabetes and cardiovascular diseases

Options (a), (b), and (d) contradict the information given in the passage. This question tests the understanding of the relationship between dietary factors, blood sugar regulation, and the risk of chronic diseases.  The impact of GI on blood sugar control is a key aspect of nutritional science and its implications for health.


**10.  Which of the following is NOT a key provision of the Battery Waste Management Rules, 2022?**

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  The questions are designed to be challenging and assess various cognitive skills, focusing on factual recall, analysis, and conceptual understanding.  Each question includes a detailed explanation.


**1.  Regarding the delivery systems and characteristics of various gene therapies, which statement is accurate?**

(a)  Lipid nanoparticles (LNPs) are the most stable delivery system, requiring refrigeration for storage.
(b)  Direct injection into the body is the quickest development process, but efficacy and safety are unproven.
(c)  Electroporation is a delivery method associated with encapsulated mRNA, offering high efficacy and safety.
(d)  Viral or bacterial-based gene therapies offer slower development but are generally more stable at room temperature.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) accurately describes the characteristics of mRNA therapies delivered via electroporation.  Electroporation is a method used to introduce genetic material into cells by creating temporary pores in the cell membrane.  mRNA therapies using LNPs are indeed highly efficacious and have demonstrated a good safety profile in numerous clinical trials, but the LNP encapsulation itself is the key to stability and room temperature storage, not electroporation.  Option (a) is incorrect because LNPs, while offering improved stability compared to other methods, still often require cold storage. Option (b) is incorrect because direct injection lacks the precision and controlled delivery offered by other methods, making it less efficient, and its safety and efficacy haven't been established across the board.  Option (d) is partially true; viral or bacterial vectors can indeed take longer to develop, but their stability depends heavily on the specific vector and the storage conditions.  The statement that they are generally more stable at room temperature is a significant oversimplification.


**2. Which of the following accurately describes a key difference between innate and adaptive immunity?**

(a) Innate immunity is slower to respond but provides long-lasting protection, while adaptive immunity is faster but offers short-term protection.
(b) Innate immunity involves specific recognition of pathogens, while adaptive immunity involves non-specific recognition.
(c) Innate immunity is acquired through exposure to pathogens or vaccines, while adaptive immunity is present from birth.
(d) Innate immunity acts as the first line of defense, while adaptive immunity provides a secondary, more specialized response.


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Option (d) correctly defines the primary distinction between innate and adaptive immunity. Innate immunity is the body's immediate, non-specific defense mechanism, present from birth, while adaptive immunity develops over time, providing a targeted and more potent response to specific threats. Option (a) is incorrect because innate immunity is rapid but short-lived, while adaptive immunity provides slower but long-lasting protection through immunological memory. Option (b) is incorrect as innate immunity is non-specific, while adaptive immunity shows specific pathogen recognition. Option (c) reverses the roles of innate and adaptive immunity in their acquisition.


**3.  Considering the techniques involved in Mitochondrial Replacement Therapy (MRT), which statement is NOT true?**

(a)  Maternal Spindle Transfer (MST) involves transferring the mother's nucleus to a donor egg with healthy mitochondria.
(b)  Pronuclear Transfer (PNT) involves fertilizing both the mother's and donor's eggs before transferring pronuclei.
(c)  Both MST and PNT aim to prevent the transmission of mitochondrial diseases from mother to child.
(d)  PNT involves transferring the mother's entire egg cytoplasm to the donor egg, ensuring complete mitochondrial replacement.


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Option (d) is incorrect.  PNT (Pronuclear Transfer) does *not* transfer the entire egg cytoplasm; only the pronuclei (containing the nuclear genetic material) are transferred.  The donor egg's cytoplasm, containing healthy mitochondria, remains. Options (a), (b), and (c) accurately reflect the procedures and goals of MRT.  MST involves nuclear transfer, PNT involves pronuclear transfer after fertilization, and both aim to prevent mitochondrial disease transmission.


**4. Which of the following is NOT a characteristic of mRNA vaccines?**

(a) High efficacy demonstrated in recent clinical trials.
(b)  mRNA does not interact with the cell’s DNA.
(c)  Proven efficacy and safety over many years, comparable to traditional vaccines.
(d)  Potential applications in cancer therapy.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) is incorrect. While mRNA vaccines have shown high efficacy and good safety profiles in recent clinical trials, their history of use is relatively short compared to traditional vaccines.  The long-term effects and safety profiles are still under observation and evaluation. Options (a), (b), and (d) are all accurate representations of mRNA vaccine features and potential applications.  Their high efficacy is a key advantage, the non-integration with cellular DNA is a safety feature, and their application in cancer therapy is a promising area of research.


**5.  Regarding the recently completed GenomeIndia Project, which statement is accurate?**

(a)  The project aimed to sequence the genomes of 10,000 individuals representing diverse ethnic groups from across India, and data is stored at the Indian Biological Data Centre in Faridabad.
(b)  The project was primarily funded by the Council for Scientific and Industrial Research (CSIR) and led by the Centre for Brain Research, Bengaluru.
(c) The project was inspired by the Human Genome Project, which mapped approximately 92% of the human genome and was completed in 2009.
(d) The project's datasets are to be made available only to Indian researchers and institutions to safeguard genetic information.


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Option (a) correctly describes the GenomeIndia Project's aims and data storage location. The project aimed to collect 10,000 samples and create a reference genome, and the data was indeed stored at the Indian Biological Data Centre in Faridabad. Option (b) is partially correct; the project *was* led by the Centre for Brain Research, Bengaluru, but it was primarily funded by the Department of Biotechnology (DBT), not the CSIR. Option (c) is incorrect; the Human Genome Project was completed in 2003, not 2009. Option (d) is incorrect; while there are considerations for data privacy, the intent is to make the data accessible for broader research purposes, subject to appropriate ethical guidelines.


**6.  Which of the following is NOT a technique used in gene silencing?**

(a) CRISPR-Cas9
(b) RNA interference (RNAi)
(c)  Zinc Finger Nuclease (ZFN)
(d)  Reverse Transcription PCR (RT-PCR)


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Option (d) is incorrect. While RT-PCR is used for detecting RNA, it is not a gene silencing technique. Gene silencing methods directly target gene expression, while RT-PCR is a diagnostic tool. Options (a), (b), and (c) are all gene silencing techniques. CRISPR-Cas9 and ZFN are gene editing tools that can be used to disrupt gene function, and RNAi utilizes small RNA molecules to silence genes post-transcriptionally.


**7. What is NOT a component of the CRISPR-Cas9 gene editing system?**

(a) Guide RNA (gRNA)
(b) Cas9 enzyme
(c)  Restriction enzymes
(d)  DNA repair machinery


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) is incorrect. CRISPR-Cas9 does not use restriction enzymes.  Restriction enzymes are used in recombinant DNA technology to cut DNA at specific sites.  The Cas9 enzyme in CRISPR-Cas9 performs a similar function but with greater precision and guided by gRNA. Options (a), (b), and (d) are all essential components of the CRISPR-Cas9 system.  gRNA directs the Cas9 enzyme, Cas9 cuts the DNA, and the cell's DNA repair machinery is involved in the subsequent modification of the genome.


**8. Which of the following statements regarding gene drive technology is FALSE?**

(a) It increases the inheritance of a specific genetic trait beyond normal Mendelian inheritance rates.
(b) It uses a genetic element that copies itself from one chromosome to another during cell division.
(c) It is primarily used for research purposes and does not have any practical applications.
(d)  It presents several ethical and ecological challenges.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) is false. Gene drive technology has significant potential applications, including the control of disease vectors and invasive species.  However, the ethical and ecological considerations surrounding its use are substantial. Options (a), (b), and (d) accurately describe aspects of gene drive technology and its associated concerns.  The technology's mechanism relies on the biased inheritance of a modified genetic element, and its use raises important ethical and environmental questions.



Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on factual recall, analysis, and conceptual understanding.  Each question is designed to be challenging and avoids obvious or trivial answers.


**1.  Which of the following statements accurately describes a key challenge faced by satellite networks, necessitating the development of resilient technologies?**

(a)  The limited bandwidth of traditional radio frequency (RF) communication.
(b)  The absence of adequate investment in the space industry.
(c)  The presence of space debris and other environmental factors impacting satellite performance.
(d)  The lack of international cooperation in space exploration.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly highlights space debris, solar radiation, and other environmental factors as obstacles impacting satellite performance and longevity.  This directly necessitates the development of robust and resilient satellite networks capable of withstanding these challenges. Option (a) is true but is a consequence of the need for improved technology, not the primary challenge itself. Option (b) addresses a separate issue of economic feasibility, not a direct operational challenge. Option (d) is a broader issue of international relations, not a direct technical challenge for satellite networks.


**2.  Deep Space Optical Communication (DSOC) utilizes which of the following key components for enhanced communication beyond the Earth-Moon system?**

(a)  Ground-based telescopes and radio antennas for signal transmission and reception.
(b)  A flight laser transceiver on the spacecraft, a ground laser transmitter, and a ground laser receiver.
(c)  A network of orbiting satellites relaying signals between Earth and deep space probes.
(d)  High-frequency radio waves and advanced signal processing algorithms to minimize signal loss.

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The text clearly defines DSOC as utilizing a flight laser transceiver on the spacecraft, a ground laser transmitter, and a ground laser receiver. These components are specifically described as crucial for laser-based communication in deep space. Options (a), (c), and (d) describe alternative communication methods, but they do not accurately represent the core components of DSOC as described in the provided text.


**3.  Which of the following mitigation strategies is NOT employed to counteract the atmospheric effects on laser signals in deep space optical communication?**

(a)  Employing adaptive optics to compensate for atmospheric turbulence.
(b)  Utilizing infrared wavelengths less susceptible to atmospheric scattering.
(c)  Employing higher-powered lasers to overcome signal attenuation.
(d)  Establishing ground stations at higher altitudes to minimize atmospheric interference.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** While increasing laser power might seem logical, the passage emphasizes minimizing mass, volume, and power requirements.  The focus is on efficiency and mitigating atmospheric effects, not simply overpowering them. Options (a), (b), and (d) are all explicitly mentioned as strategies to reduce the impact of atmospheric distortion and power loss on laser signals.


**4.  Which of the following is NOT a harmful effect associated with the use of liquid nitrogen in food items, as highlighted by the Tamil Nadu food safety commissioner?**

(a)  Cold burns and frostbite due to rapid freezing of skin tissue.
(b)  Nausea, coma, and seizures due to ingestion.
(c)  Eye fluid freezing, leading to potential vision impairment.
(d)  Corrosion and flammability hazards.

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The passage specifically states that liquid nitrogen is non-flammable and non-corrosive.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are all direct consequences of the extremely low temperature of liquid nitrogen and its potential for causing rapid freezing of biological tissues.


**5.  Methanol (CH3OH), also known as wood alcohol, is characterized by which of the following properties?**

(a)  It is a viscous, highly colored liquid with a strong, acrid odor.
(b)  It is insoluble in water and readily forms explosive mixtures with air.
(c)  It is a colorless, fairly volatile liquid with a faintly sweet, pungent odor, completely mixable with water.
(d)  It is a solid at room temperature and is used primarily as a lubricant.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly describes methanol as a colorless, fairly volatile liquid with a faintly sweet pungent odor and its complete miscibility with water. The other options present inaccurate physical properties or applications of methanol.


**6.  The Glycemic Index (GI), proposed by Professor David Jenkins, is a measure of:**

(a)  The overall nutritional value of a carbohydrate-containing food.
(b)  The amount of fiber and protein in a food relative to its carbohydrate content.
(c)  How quickly a carbohydrate-containing food raises blood sugar levels after consumption.
(d)  The total calorie content of a food item based on its macronutrient composition.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly defines GI as a measure of how quickly a carbohydrate-containing food raises blood sugar levels. The other options describe different nutritional parameters or concepts unrelated to the core definition of GI.


**7.  Which of the following statements regarding Avian Influenza (bird flu) is INCORRECT?**

(a)  Avian influenza is caused by infection with avian influenza Type A viruses.
(b)  Influenza A viruses are classified into subtypes based on hemagglutinin (H) and neuraminidase (N) proteins.
(c)  Low pathogenic avian influenza (LPAI) viruses always cause severe disease in poultry.
(d)  The World Organisation for Animal Health (WOAH) collaborates internationally to enhance animal health.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage specifically states that LPAI viruses cause either no signs of disease or mild disease in chickens/poultry.  The other statements correctly reflect information provided in the text.


**8.  Magnetic Resonance Imaging (MRI) technology utilizes which of the following principles for producing detailed images of internal body structures?**

(a)  Ionizing radiation to penetrate and image internal tissues.
(b)  Ultrasound waves to generate echoes that are processed into images.
(c)  A large magnet and radio waves to interact with hydrogen atoms in the body.
(d)  X-rays to create shadow images of internal structures.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly states that MRI uses a large magnet and radio waves to interact with hydrogen atoms in the body to create cross-sectional images. The other options describe different medical imaging techniques.


**9.  Which of the following vaccines was NOT mentioned in the context of meningitis prevention in the provided text?**

(a)  Men5CV vaccine.
(b)  Meningococcal ACWY vaccine.
(c)  Haemophilus influenzae type b (Hib) vaccine.
(d)  Pneumococcal conjugate vaccine.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage mentions Men5CV and Meningococcal ACWY vaccines. Options (c) and (d) are not mentioned in relation to meningitis prevention in the provided text.


**10.  Which of the following is NOT a reported side effect of the AstraZeneca COVID-19 vaccine (Covishield), as admitted by the company?**

(a)  Thrombosis with thrombocytopenia syndrome (TTS).
(b)  Nausea and vomiting.
(c)  Mild fever and headache.
(d)  Severe allergic reactions.

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** While the passage mentions TTS as a rare side effect, it does not specifically mention nausea and vomiting as reported side effects of the AstraZeneca vaccine.  Options (a), (c), and (d) are common side effects of many vaccines, and while not explicitly stated for Covishield in this passage, they are plausible and frequently reported.  The question focuses on what was *explicitly not* mentioned.



**11. The S.A.R.A.H. digital health promoter prototype, unveiled by the WHO, leverages which technology for public health information dissemination?**

(a)  Blockchain technology for secure data storage and sharing.

The other options represent other relevant digital health technologies, but they are not the primary technology used by S.A.R.A.H. as described in the text.


**12.  Which of the following is a mechanism by which weight loss drugs, as discussed in the text, achieve their effect?**

(a)  Directly inhibiting fat absorption in the digestive system.
(b)  Increasing the rate of metabolism to burn more calories.
(c)  Mimicking the action of the gut hormone glucagon-like peptide 1 (GLP-1).
(d)  Suppression of the central nervous system to reduce hunger signals.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage specifically explains that weight loss drugs mimic the action of GLP-1, increasing insulin production, reducing glucagon production, suppressing appetite, and slowing digestion. The other options, while potentially relevant to weight loss, do not reflect the mechanism of action described for these drugs in the provided text.


**13.  The  Indian Space Research Organisation's (ISRO) PSLV Orbital Experimental Module-2 (POEM-2) mission utilizes which component of the Polar Satellite Launch Vehicle (PSLV)?**

**14.  The CE-20 cryogenic engine, developed by ISRO's Liquid Propulsion Systems Centre (LPSC), uses which propellants?**

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on Science and Technology.  Each question is designed to be challenging and assesses various cognitive skills, primarily factual recall and conceptual understanding.  The explanations provide detailed justifications for the correct answers and analyze the distractors.


**1.  Which biofuel production method involves heating biomass in the absence of oxygen, resulting in the breakdown of organic materials into bio-oil, syngas, and biochar?**

(a) Transesterification
(b) Hydrogenation
(c) Cracking
(d) Pyrolysis

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** Pyrolysis is a thermochemical process where biomass is heated in an oxygen-deficient environment. This process breaks down the complex organic compounds in the biomass into simpler substances, including bio-oil (a liquid fuel), syngas (a mixture of carbon monoxide and hydrogen), and biochar (a solid residue).  Transesterification is primarily used for biodiesel production, involving the reaction of fats or oils with an alcohol. Hydrogenation adds hydrogen to bio-oil to improve its quality. Cracking, similar to pyrolysis, also breaks down molecules but often uses a catalyst. The question specifically asks about the method involving the production of bio-oil, syngas, and biochar, making pyrolysis the only correct answer.


**2.  A type of fuel cell that directly converts the chemical energy of methanol into electricity, offering advantages such as liquid fuel, high energy density, and compact design, is known as:**

(a) Perovskite Fuel Cell
(b) Vanadium Flow Battery
(c) Direct Methanol Fuel Cell (DMFC)
(d) Algae Assisted Fuel Cell (AFC)

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** Direct Methanol Fuel Cells (DMFCs) are a type of fuel cell that directly oxidizes methanol to generate electricity.  This contrasts with other fuel cell types that may require intermediate steps or different fuels. The advantages mentioned – liquid fuel (methanol is a liquid), high energy density (methanol packs a lot of energy), and compact design – are all key features of DMFCs, making them suitable for portable power applications.  Perovskites are materials with a specific crystal structure used in solar cells and other applications, not fuel cells. Vanadium flow batteries are energy storage systems, not fuel cells. Algae-assisted fuel cells are a relatively newer concept involving algae for energy production.


**3.  The predominant technology for rechargeable energy storage solutions, known for its high energy density and low self-discharge rate, but with safety concerns related to its flammable electrolyte, is:**

(a) Sodium-ion battery
(b) Sand battery
(c) Lithium-ion battery
(d) Vanadium flow battery

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** Lithium-ion batteries are currently the dominant technology for rechargeable energy storage. Their high energy density allows for longer operating times on a single charge and enables the creation of compact devices. The low self-discharge rate means they retain their charge for extended periods even when not in use. However, a significant drawback is the use of a liquid and flammable electrolyte, posing safety risks in case of damage or overheating. Sodium-ion batteries are an emerging technology with lower energy density. Sand batteries primarily focus on thermal energy storage. Vanadium flow batteries are another energy storage option but with different characteristics.


**4.  Which of the following is NOT a key component of a Lithium-ion battery?**

(a) Graphite
(b) Lithium Oxide
(c) Electrolyte
(d) Vanadium Oxide

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** Graphite, lithium oxide (or a lithium metal oxide), and the electrolyte are essential components of a lithium-ion battery. Graphite serves as the anode material, lithium oxide is commonly used in the cathode, and the electrolyte facilitates the movement of lithium ions between the electrodes.  Vanadium oxide is not a typical component of a lithium-ion battery; it finds applications in other battery chemistries like vanadium flow batteries. The question tests the specific knowledge of lithium-ion battery components, making vanadium oxide the clear distractor.


**5. The process of converting vegetable oils or animal fats into fatty acid methyl esters (FAMEs), which are the chemical name for a specific biofuel, is termed:**

(a) Pyrolysis
(b) Fermentation
(c) Transesterification
(d) Hydrogenation

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** Transesterification is the specific chemical process used to produce biodiesel (FAMEs). It involves reacting vegetable oils or animal fats with an alcohol (usually methanol) in the presence of a catalyst.  Pyrolysis is a thermal decomposition process, fermentation is used in ethanol production, and hydrogenation is a process of adding hydrogen to a substance. The question focuses on the precise chemical process for biodiesel production, clearly indicating transesterification as the correct answer.


**6. Which of the following is NOT an advantage of Sodium-ion batteries compared to Lithium-ion batteries?**

(a) Abundance of Sodium
(b) Lower Cost
(c) Higher Energy Density
(d) Environmental and Safety Benefits

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** Sodium-ion batteries offer several advantages over lithium-ion batteries, including the abundance and lower cost of sodium, leading to potentially more sustainable and affordable batteries. They are also considered safer due to the more stable nature of sodium. However, a key limitation is their lower energy density compared to lithium-ion batteries, meaning they cannot store as much energy in the same volume or weight. This limits their applicability in energy-intensive devices like electric vehicles.


**7. Which of the following statements accurately describes the primary application of fuel cells in the context of energy and transportation?**

(a) Direct combustion in internal combustion engines
(b) Blending with other fuels for improved efficiency
(c) Efficient conversion of hydrogen into electricity
(d) Use as a primary energy source for traditional power plants

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The primary application of fuel cells, especially in transportation and emerging energy sectors, lies in their ability to efficiently convert hydrogen into electricity. This process is significantly cleaner than direct combustion, offering advantages in terms of reduced emissions. While fuel cells can be used in conjunction with other fuels or for direct combustion in specific applications, this is not their primary strength or area of focus in the context of the question.  Fuel cells are not typically used as the primary energy source in traditional power plants, which still largely rely on fossil fuels or other energy sources.


**8.  The Indian government's initiative aimed at establishing India as a global leader in green hydrogen production and utilization, involving targets for green hydrogen production, renewable energy capacity expansion, and investment attraction, is known as:**

(a) National Electric Mobility Mission Plan (NEMMP)
(b) FAME Mission
(c) National Hydrogen Mission
(d) IndiaAI Mission

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The National Hydrogen Mission is the Indian government's flagship program focused on establishing India as a global leader in green hydrogen production.  It sets ambitious targets for green hydrogen production, aiming to significantly increase renewable energy capacity and attract substantial investments. The NEMMP focuses on electric mobility, FAME on faster adoption of electric vehicles, and IndiaAI on artificial intelligence.  The question specifically highlights the focus on green hydrogen, making the National Hydrogen Mission the correct answer.


**9. Which one of the following is NOT a key amendment introduced in the National Policy on Biofuels - 2018?**

(a) Expansion of Feedstocks
(b) Promotion under Make in India
(c) Advancing Ethanol Blending Target
(d) Stricter regulations on the use of food crops for biofuel production

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The amendments to the National Policy on Biofuels in 2018 focused on expanding the range of feedstocks, promoting domestic production under the Make in India initiative, and advancing the target for ethanol blending.  The amendments did not introduce stricter regulations on the use of food crops; instead, they broadened the scope to include non-food feedstocks to reduce competition with food production. The question tests the specific details of the policy amendments, focusing on what was NOT included.


**10.  The discovery of which element in the Sutlej river sand in Punjab highlights its potential use as a substitute for platinum due to its high melting point and corrosion resistance?**

(a) Tantalum
(b) Vanadium
(c) Molybdenum
(d) Rhenium

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:** The discovery of tantalum in the Sutlej river sand highlights its potential applications in various industries due to its unique properties.  Tantalum is known for its high melting point, exceptional corrosion resistance, and other characteristics that make it suitable for high-temperature applications and use in electronics and semiconductors.  Vanadium, molybdenum, and rhenium also have industrial uses, but the specific context of the Sutlej river sand discovery and its potential as a platinum substitute points to tantalum.  The question tests knowledge of specific element properties and their industrial relevance.


Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on factual recall, analysis, and conceptual understanding.  Each question has a detailed explanation.  The difficulty level is primarily "difficult" due to the requirement of integrating information from various sections of the provided text and demanding a nuanced understanding of the subject matter.


**1.  A zoonotic viral disease, initially detected in Africa, now prevalent in the Middle East, Asia, and Eastern Europe, primarily affects cattle, causing fever, skin nodules, and reduced milk yield.  Its transmission is facilitated by blood-feeding insects. Which preventative measure is most effective in controlling its spread?**

(a)  Antibiotic treatment of infected cattle.
(b)  Quarantine of affected regions.
(c)  Attenuated virus vaccines.
(d)  Improved sanitation practices.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question describes an infectious disease spread by vectors and affecting livestock. The passage explicitly states that the spread of this unspecified viral disease (likely Foot-and-Mouth Disease, given the description) can be controlled through attenuated virus vaccines.  Option (a) is incorrect because antibiotics are ineffective against viruses. Option (b) is a supplementary control measure, but not the most effective primary prevention. Option (d) might help reduce the spread of some diseases, but it is not directly relevant to a vector-borne disease like the one described.  The efficacy of vaccination in controlling vector-borne diseases in livestock is a crucial concept in veterinary epidemiology and animal health management, relevant to UPSC's focus on public health and agricultural practices.


**2.  Egypt's achievement of "gold tier" status in the fight against a specific viral liver infection highlights a significant global health milestone.  This infection is transmitted through the reuse or inadequate sterilization of medical equipment.  Which virus is being referred to?**

(a)  Hepatitis A virus
(b)  Hepatitis B virus
(c)  Hepatitis C virus
(d)  Nipah virus

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage clearly states that Egypt achieved "gold tier" status in eliminating Hepatitis C.  The description of transmission via contaminated medical equipment directly points to Hepatitis C.  Options (a) and (b) are incorrect; while Hepatitis B shares transmission routes with HIV, it is not the subject of Egypt's achievement. Hepatitis A has different transmission routes.  Option (d) is irrelevant; Nipah virus has a different mode of transmission. The question tests knowledge of global health initiatives and the specific characteristics of viral infections, a relevant area for UPSC.


**3.  A zoonotic virus, causing outbreaks in Kerala and transmitted through contaminated food or direct human contact, has fruit bats as its natural hosts.  This virus's spread is exacerbated by factors including antibiotic use in animals and deforestation. Which virus is described?**

(a)  Avian Influenza A (H9N2) virus
(b)  Dengue virus
(c)  Rabies virus
(d)  Nipah virus

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The description perfectly matches the characteristics of the Nipah virus (NIV) detailed in the passage: zoonotic, outbreaks in Kerala, transmission via contaminated food and human-to-human contact, and fruit bats as natural hosts.  The mention of increased spread due to antibiotic use in animals and deforestation further reinforces this identification.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect; they are zoonotic diseases, but they do not match the specific details provided in the question.  Understanding the epidemiology of zoonotic diseases and their links to environmental factors is crucial for UPSC exams.


**4.  The Union Health Ministry closely monitors an influenza A virus subtype causing both human influenza (rarely) and bird flu.  This subtype is found globally in wild birds and is endemic in poultry in many areas.  Its transmission occurs through exposure to infected poultry or contaminated environments. Which virus is being discussed?**

(a)  H1N1 influenza virus
(b)  H9N2 avian influenza virus
(c)  Hepatitis C virus
(d)  Dengue virus

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly mentions the Union Health Ministry monitoring the H9N2 avian influenza virus outbreak in China.  The description of its characteristics—influenza A subtype, human and bird flu causation, global presence in wild birds and poultry, and transmission route—perfectly aligns with the information provided. Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect; they are different viruses with distinct characteristics and transmission mechanisms. The question assesses knowledge of influenza viruses, their subtypes, and public health surveillance mechanisms, important for UPSC.


**5.  A neglected tropical disease (NTD), also known as elephantiasis, is caused by parasitic nematodes and transmitted by mosquitoes.  This disease impairs the lymphatic system, potentially leading to the abnormal enlargement of body parts. Which disease is this?**

(a)  Noma
(b)  Lymphatic Filariasis (LF)
(c)  Dengue
(d)  Leishmaniasis

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The passage clearly defines Lymphatic Filariasis (LF) as a neglected tropical disease (NTD), also known as elephantiasis, caused by parasitic nematodes, and transmitted by mosquitoes, with the characteristic impairment of the lymphatic system and potential for body part enlargement. Options (a), (c), and (d) are other NTDs but do not fit the description of the disease in the question. This question tests knowledge of NTDs, their causes, transmission, and clinical manifestations—relevant for UPSC's focus on public health.


**6.  A therapy utilizing bacteriophages—viruses infecting and replicating only in bacterial cells—is gaining public acceptance as an alternative to antibiotics. This therapy is inherently non-toxic to human cells due to significant differences between bacterial and human cells. What is this therapy called?**

(b)  Phage therapy
(c)  Nuclear medicine
(d)  Gene therapy

**Explanation:** The passage directly describes phage therapy as the use of bacteriophages to treat bacterial infections, highlighting its non-toxicity to human cells due to cellular differences. Options (a), (c), and (d) are unrelated medical approaches. This question tests understanding of emerging therapeutic approaches and their mechanisms, a relevant aspect of science and technology for UPSC.


**7.  A quadrivalent Human papillomavirus (HPV) vaccine, developed indigenously in India, elicits an immune response comparable to Merck’s Gardasil vaccine and protects against HPV types 6, 11, 16, and 18. This vaccine is primarily intended for the prevention of which cancer?**

Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect; they are not primarily associated with HPV infection.  The question tests knowledge of vaccine development, disease prevention, and public health initiatives in India, all relevant to UPSC.


**8.  A genetic condition present at birth, inherited through two genes coding for abnormal hemoglobin, results in misshapen red blood cells that can block blood vessels, leading to various complications like stroke, eye problems, infections, and pain crises.  Which condition is being described?**

(a)  Haemophilia
(b)  Thalassemia
(c)  Sickle Cell Disease
(d)  Leukemia

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The detailed description matches Sickle Cell Disease (SCD): inherited, present at birth, caused by abnormal hemoglobin leading to misshapen red blood cells, and resulting in complications including stroke, eye problems, infections, and pain crises.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are distinct genetic or blood disorders with different underlying mechanisms and clinical manifestations.  The question tests knowledge of genetic disorders, their inheritance patterns, and clinical features—relevant for UPSC's focus on health issues.


**9.  A three-drug regimen, replacing a previous two-drug regimen, is now used to treat Pauci-Bacillary (PB) cases of a chronic infectious disease caused by *Mycobacterium leprae*. This disease affects the skin, peripheral nerves, mucosa of the upper respiratory tract, and eyes. What is the disease?**

(a)  Tuberculosis
(b)  Leprosy
(c)  Meningitis
(d)  Malaria

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The passage details the new treatment regimen for Leprosy (Hansen's disease), specifying the shift from a two-drug to a three-drug regimen for PB cases. The description of the disease's effects on the skin, nerves, mucosa, and eyes aligns with leprosy. Options (a), (c), and (d) are different infectious diseases with distinct etiologies and clinical presentations.  The question tests knowledge of specific diseases, their treatment, and public health interventions, important for UPSC.


**10.  A type of gene therapy, where therapeutic genes are transferred to a patient's somatic cells, restricts any modifications and effects to that patient, preventing inheritance by future generations. What is this type of gene therapy called?**

(a)  Germline gene therapy
(b)  Somatic cell gene therapy
(c)  Viral vector gene therapy
(d)  Non-viral vector gene therapy

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly defines somatic cell gene therapy as the type where modifications are limited to the patient's somatic cells, preventing inheritance. Option (a) is incorrect; germline gene therapy modifies germline cells (egg or sperm), leading to heritable changes. Options (c) and (d) describe methods of gene delivery, not the type of gene therapy. This question assesses understanding of gene therapy types, their mechanisms, and ethical implications—crucial for UPSC.


Here are some difficult multiple-choice questions (MCQs) based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging, requiring in-depth knowledge and careful analysis to eliminate plausible distractors.  The difficulty level is primarily achieved by demanding precise factual recall and nuanced conceptual understanding,  presenting closely related options, and necessitating a thorough understanding of the subject matter.


**1.  A new variety of mustard, less pungent due to reduced glucosinolate content, was developed using a specific gene-editing technology.  Which technology was employed?**

(a)  TALEN technology
(b)  ZFN technology
(c)  CRISPR/Cas9 gene editing technology
(d)  Meganucleases

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly states that the new low-pungent mustard variety was created using CRISPR/Cas9 gene editing technology.  TALENs, ZFNs, and meganucleases are also gene-editing tools, but they are distinct from CRISPR/Cas9 in their mechanisms and applications.  TALENs and ZFNs rely on engineered nucleases that target specific DNA sequences, while meganucleases are naturally occurring enzymes. CRISPR/Cas9 offers a simpler and more efficient approach to gene editing, making it a more widely used technology in recent agricultural advancements. The question tests factual recall of a specific detail within a larger context of biotechnology advancements.  The other options represent alternative gene editing techniques, making them plausible but ultimately incorrect distractors.


**2.  The Giant Metrewave Radio Telescope (GMRT) is operated by which research institution?**

(a)  Indian Institute of Astrophysics (IIA)
(b)  Raman Research Institute (RRI)
(c)  National Centre for Radio Astrophysics (NCRA), Pune
(d)  Tata Institute of Fundamental Research (TIFR), Mumbai (but not directly operating GMRT)

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The text clearly states that the GMRT is operated by the National Centre for Radio Astrophysics (NCRA) in Pune. While the NCRA is a part of the Tata Institute of Fundamental Research (TIFR), the operational responsibility rests with the NCRA.  The other options are prominent Indian astronomical research institutions, but they are not directly involved in the operation of the GMRT. This question tests factual recall of the specific organizational entity responsible for a particular scientific instrument.  The inclusion of TIFR as a plausible yet incorrect option enhances the difficulty level by requiring precise knowledge of the institutional structure.


**3. Which space-based gravitational wave observatory is a collaboration between ESA, NASA, and an international consortium of scientists, building upon the success of LISA Pathfinder?**

(a)  eLISA (evolved Laser Interferometer Space Antenna)
(b)  Einstein Telescope
(c)  LIGO-India
(d)  Laser Interferometer Space Antenna (LISA)

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly mentions that the Laser Interferometer Space Antenna (LISA) mission is a collaboration between ESA, NASA, and an international consortium of scientists, and that it builds on the LISA Pathfinder.  eLISA is a related but distinct concept, while the Einstein Telescope and LIGO-India are ground-based observatories. This question assesses the understanding of specific space missions and international collaborations within the field of gravitational wave astronomy. The options are carefully chosen to include closely related projects, making it challenging to distinguish the correct answer without precise knowledge.


**4.  The phenomenon where the Sun is exactly overhead, causing the shadow of symmetrical vertical objects to vanish, is known as what?**

(a)  Solar Eclipse
(b)  Equinox
(c)  Solstice
(d)  Zero Shadow Day

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The text directly defines "Zero Shadow Day" as the phenomenon described.  Solar eclipses, equinoxes, and solstices are related astronomical events, but they don't involve the vanishing of shadows due to the Sun's direct overhead position. This question tests the understanding of a specific astronomical phenomenon and its definition. The distractors are carefully chosen to be related astronomical terms, adding to the difficulty level.


**5.  What is the primary function of the Radioisotope Thermoelectric Generator (RTG)?**

The other options describe unrelated technologies or applications in space exploration. The distractors are designed to be plausible alternatives related to space technology but ultimately incorrect.


**6. Which type of engine uses a combination of liquid oxygen (LOX) and RP-1 kerosene as propellants and is being developed to enhance the payload capacity of ISRO's LVM3?**

(d)  Ion Thruster Engine

The CE-20 uses liquid hydrogen, while solid propellant and ion thruster engines utilize different propulsion mechanisms. This question tests knowledge of specific rocket engine types and their propellants, requiring detailed information from the text. The distractors are all valid rocket engine types, making it more difficult to select the correct answer without specific knowledge.


**7.  The Artemis Accords primarily aim to achieve which of the following?**
