Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on Science and Technology.  Each question is designed to be difficult, requiring in-depth knowledge and careful analysis.  The difficulty stems from the nuanced nature of the subject matter and the inclusion of plausible distractors.


**1.  Consider the following statements regarding the  Prototype Fast Breeder Reactor (PFBR):**

I. It utilizes liquid sodium as a coolant.
II. It is India's first indigenous Fast Breeder Reactor.
III.  Upon commissioning, India will become the first country to operate a commercial-scale FBR.

Which of the statement(s) is/are correct?

(a) I and II only
(b) II and III only
(c) I and III only
(d) I, II, and III


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement I is correct. The PFBR uses liquid sodium as its coolant, a key characteristic of fast breeder reactors.  Liquid sodium's high thermal conductivity allows for efficient heat transfer, crucial for the reactor's operation.  Statement II is also correct; the PFBR is indeed India's first indigenously developed fast breeder reactor, a significant achievement in the country's nuclear technology program.  Statement III is incorrect.  While the PFBR is a major step,  Russia already operates commercial-scale fast breeder reactors.  India's commissioning of the PFBR will make it only the second country after Russia to have a commercial operating FBR.  The other options are incorrect because they include the false statement III.


**2. Which of the following is NOT a key feature of the Small Satellite Launch Vehicle (SSLV)?**

(a) Cost-effectiveness
(b)  Three-stage solid propulsion configuration
(c) Payload capacity exceeding 1000 kg to Low Earth Orbit (LEO)
(d)  Flexibility in accommodating multiple payloads


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The SSLV is designed for cost-effectiveness and flexibility, enabling the launch of multiple small satellites. Its three-stage configuration, using primarily solid propulsion, contributes to its efficiency. However, its payload capacity is limited to 500 kg into a 500 km planar orbit. Option (c) incorrectly states a payload capacity significantly exceeding this limit. Options (a), (b), and (d) accurately reflect the SSLV's design and objectives.


**3. Regarding the Artemis Accords, which of the following statements is accurate?**

(a) They are a legally binding international treaty establishing strict rules for space exploration.
(b)  They primarily focus on the militarization of space and establishing territorial claims on celestial bodies.
(c)  They emphasize peaceful space exploration, data sharing, and the preservation of space heritage.
(d)  They are solely a U.S.-led initiative with no participation from other nations.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Artemis Accords are a set of principles, not a legally binding treaty.  Their core aims are to promote peaceful uses of space, encourage transparency through data sharing, and protect the historical significance of lunar and other celestial sites.  Option (a) is incorrect because the Accords are non-binding. Option (b) misrepresents the Accords' focus; they actively discourage the militarization of space and prioritize international cooperation. Option (d) is incorrect as the Accords involve multiple nations.


**4.  Which of the following statements about Radioisotope Thermoelectric Generators (RTGs) is FALSE?**

(a) They utilize the decay of radioactive materials to generate heat.
(b) They can operate effectively regardless of the spacecraft's distance from the sun.
(c) They are primarily powered by solar energy.
(d)  They provide a continuous supply of power.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

RTGs leverage the heat generated by radioactive decay to produce electricity. This makes them independent of solar energy, a crucial advantage for deep-space missions where solar power is weak or unavailable. Their continuous power output is essential for long-duration missions. Option (c) is false because RTGs do not utilize solar energy; their power source is the radioactive decay of isotopes.


**5.  Concerning the Rotating Detonation Rocket Engine (RDRE), which statement is NOT true?**

(a) It utilizes a continuous detonation wave for propulsion.
(b)  It has undergone successful hot fire testing by NASA.
(c) It relies on traditional deflagrative combustion like most current rocket engines.
(d) It is being developed using 3D printing technology.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The RDRE is a revolutionary propulsion system that uses a continuous detonation wave, unlike conventional rocket engines that rely on deflagrative combustion.  NASA has successfully tested a 3D-printed prototype. Option (c) is incorrect as the RDRE differentiates itself precisely by *not* using traditional deflagrative combustion.


**6.  The Meissner effect is directly associated with which phenomenon?**

(a)  Nuclear fission
(b) Superconductivity
(c)  Electromagnetic induction
(d)  Quantum entanglement


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Meissner effect is the expulsion of magnetic fields from a superconductor below its critical temperature. This is a defining characteristic of the superconducting state, where electrical resistance vanishes.  The other options are unrelated to the Meissner effect.


**7.  What is the primary purpose of the National Clean Air Programme (NCAP)?**

(a) To reduce water pollution in major Indian cities.
(b) To improve air quality in specified Indian cities.
(c) To manage plastic waste across India.
(d) To promote renewable energy sources.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The NCAP specifically targets improving air quality in 131 cities by reducing particulate matter concentrations.  The other options describe different environmental programs.


**8.  Which of the following is NOT a method used to detect exoplanets?**

(a) Transit Method
(b) Gravitational Microlensing
(c)  Direct Imaging with high-resolution telescopes. (Often difficult due to stellar glare)
(d)  Spectroscopic analysis of stellar atmospheres


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

While direct imaging is a goal, the brightness of the star often obscures the planet, making direct observation extremely difficult. The transit method, gravitational microlensing, and spectroscopic analysis are all established techniques for detecting exoplanets.


**9.  The "India Semiconductor Research Centre (ISRC)" is primarily focused on which technological area?**

(a) Space exploration
(b)  Nuclear energy
(c)  Semiconductor technology
(d)  Biotechnology


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The ISRC, as its name suggests, is dedicated to advancing research and development in semiconductor technologies.


**10.  The discovery of large deposits of 15 Rare Earth Elements (REEs) in Andhra Pradesh's Anantapur district is attributed to which organization?**

(a)  Indian Space Research Organisation (ISRO)
(b)  Bhabha Atomic Research Centre (BARC)
(c)  National Geophysical Research Institute (NGRI)
(d)  Geological Survey of India (GSI)


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The news report specifically credits the NGRI with this discovery.  The other organizations are involved in different scientific domains.



Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  The questions are designed to be challenging, requiring a deep understanding of the concepts and facts presented.


**1.  A novel approach in renewable energy storage involves utilizing a readily available, naturally occurring material with excellent thermal properties for heat storage, subsequently releasing this stored energy on demand. This technology primarily finds application in which sector?**

(a)  Power generation for electric vehicles
(b)  Large-scale grid stabilization for renewable energy sources
(c)  Heating and industrial processes requiring thermal energy
(d)  Portable electronic devices requiring long-lasting power

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question describes a sand battery.  Sand batteries leverage the abundance and thermal properties of sand to store heat generated from excess renewable energy.  This stored heat is then released on demand, making it particularly suitable for applications requiring thermal energy, such as industrial processes and heating systems.  Option (a) is incorrect because sand batteries are not directly involved in powering electric vehicles. Option (b) is partially correct in that they can contribute to grid stability by storing excess energy, but their primary application is not grid-scale stabilization. Option (d) is incorrect because sand batteries are not suitable for portable electronics due to their size and application.  The inherent scalability and cost-effectiveness of sand batteries, using readily available material, make them a particularly attractive solution for the thermal energy sector, aligning with sustainable development goals.


**2.  A type of fuel cell directly converts the chemical energy of a readily transportable liquid fuel into electricity, offering advantages of high energy density and compact design. Which fuel is used in this fuel cell technology?**

(a)  Hydrogen
(b)  Methanol
(c)  Ethanol
(d)  Biodiesel

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The description points to Direct Methanol Fuel Cells (DMFCs). DMFCs utilize methanol as their fuel source, offering several benefits over other fuel cell types.  Methanol is a liquid fuel, making it easier to transport and store compared to gaseous fuels like hydrogen. The high energy density of methanol allows for a compact fuel cell design, making it suitable for various applications.  Hydrogen (a) while clean, presents storage and transportation challenges. Ethanol (c) and Biodiesel (d) are primarily used as combustion fuels, not directly in fuel cells for electricity generation. DMFCs are a promising technology for portable power applications and even some transportation applications, given their advantages in terms of fuel handling and energy density.


**3.  Which of the following materials, characterized by its versatility in composition and tunable properties, finds applications in high-efficiency solar cells, LEDs, and medical imaging?**

(a)  Graphene
(b)  Vanadium
(c)  Perovskite
(d)  Tantalum

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question describes perovskite materials. Perovskites are a class of materials with a specific crystal structure (ABX3) that allows for a wide range of tunable properties, including bandgap, conductivity, and light absorption.  These properties make them ideal for various applications such as high-efficiency solar cells, LEDs, and lasers.  Their tunable bandgap allows for the generation of light across a wide range of colors.  In medical imaging, their high sensitivity makes them suitable for photodetectors and X-ray imaging. Graphene (a) is known for its electrical conductivity but its applications are not as broad as those of perovskites. Vanadium (b) is used in alloys and batteries. Tantalum (d) is a corrosion-resistant metal used in electronics and other high-temperature applications. The adaptability and potential cost-effectiveness of perovskites make them a leading material in several advanced technologies.


**4.  A recent study highlighted the use of hybrid nanoparticles, less than 8 nm in size, combining gold and copper sulfide, for both cancer cell detection and treatment.  What are the key properties of these nanoparticles that enable both diagnostic and therapeutic applications?**

(a)  High electrical conductivity and biocompatibility
(b)  Photoacoustic and photothermal properties
(c)  High surface area and catalytic activity
(d)  Magnetic resonance and radiopaque properties

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The nanoparticles described leverage photoacoustic and photothermal properties. Photoacoustic properties allow the nanoparticles to absorb light and generate ultrasound waves, facilitating cancer cell detection. Photothermal properties enable the nanoparticles to produce heat when exposed to light, killing tumor cells. This dual functionality makes them a promising tool in combined diagnostic and therapeutic approaches. While other properties might be relevant to nanoparticles in general, the question specifically points to the diagnostic and therapeutic capabilities enabled by photoacoustic and photothermal effects.  The use of light activation through endoscopy, a minimally invasive procedure, further enhances the therapeutic potential of this technology.


**5. Which of the following elements is prominently utilized as an alloying element in steel, and also finds application in advanced energy storage solutions such as vanadium flow batteries?**

(a)  Tantalum
(b)  Lithium
(c)  Vanadium
(d)  Graphite

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** Vanadium is the correct answer. Vanadium is a well-known alloying element in steel, enhancing its strength and other mechanical properties.  Furthermore, it plays a crucial role in vanadium flow batteries (VFBs), a type of redox flow battery that is gaining traction as a reliable, safe, and stable energy storage solution, particularly for renewable energy integration. Tantalum (a) is a high-melting-point metal used in specialized applications. Lithium (b) is used in lithium-ion batteries. Graphite (d) is a key component in lithium-ion battery anodes. Vanadium's dual role in established metallurgical applications and emerging energy storage technologies highlights its importance in both traditional and advanced materials science.


**6.  Which of the following methods is NOT a primary method used for producing hydrogen for energy applications?**

(a)  Steam methane reforming of natural gas
(b)  Electrolysis of water using renewable energy
(c)  Direct extraction from the atmosphere
(d)  Gasification of coal

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**  Hydrogen is not directly extracted from the atmosphere in significant quantities for energy applications. While hydrogen is abundant in water and hydrocarbons, its direct extraction from the atmosphere is not currently a viable or economically feasible method. Steam methane reforming (a) utilizes natural gas to produce hydrogen, although it generates CO2 emissions. Electrolysis of water (b) using renewable energy is a clean method for hydrogen production, generating “green” hydrogen. Gasification of coal (d) can also yield hydrogen, though it is less environmentally friendly. The lack of efficient and practical methods for direct atmospheric hydrogen extraction makes it a less relevant option compared to the established industrial processes of hydrogen generation.


**7. Which of the following statements about the Artemis Accords is INCORRECT?**

(a) They are a set of binding international treaties.
(b) They aim to ensure a safe and predictable outer space environment.
(c) They promote the peaceful use of outer space.
(d)  They encourage the sharing of scientific data.


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:** The Artemis Accords are *not* binding international treaties; they are a set of non-binding principles.  This is a crucial distinction. While they aim to foster international cooperation in space exploration,  participation is voluntary, and there are no formal legal penalties for non-compliance. The Accords do aim to establish a safe and predictable space environment (b), promote peaceful uses of space (c), and encourage scientific data sharing (d), making these options correct. The non-binding nature of the Accords allows for flexibility and broader participation but also limits their enforceability compared to legally binding treaties.


**8.  What is the primary function of the International Monitoring System (IMS) established under the Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty (CTBT)?**

(a)  To conduct on-site inspections of nuclear facilities.
(b)  To negotiate and enforce the CTBT among signatory nations.
(c)  To detect potential nuclear explosions globally.
(d)  To develop and deploy new nuclear weapons technologies.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The IMS is a global network of sensors designed to detect nuclear explosions. It uses seismic, infrasound, radionuclide, and hydroacoustic monitoring to detect the characteristic signatures of nuclear tests, regardless of their location.  While on-site inspections (a) are a part of the CTBT verification process, they are not the primary function of the IMS. The IMS does not negotiate or enforce the treaty (b); that is the role of the CTBTO and participating nations.  The IMS is not involved in developing or deploying nuclear weapons (d).  The IMS is a critical component of the CTBT's verification regime, providing a crucial early warning capability against clandestine nuclear testing.


**9.  Which of the following is NOT a key feature of the draft National Strategy for Robotics (NSR) in India?**

(a)  Classification of robots into industrial, service, and medical categories.
(b)  Designation of the Ministry of Electronics and Information Technology (MeitY) as the implementing agency.
(c)  Prioritization of the development of humanoid robots for domestic use.
(d)  Recognition of Telangana as the first state to launch a state robotics framework.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** While the NSR likely addresses various robot types, the provided text doesn't specifically highlight a prioritization of humanoid robots for domestic use (c).  The NSR does classify robots into industrial, service, and medical categories (a), designates MeitY as the implementing agency (b), and acknowledges Telangana's leading role in establishing a state robotics framework (d). The focus of the NSR is likely broader than just domestic humanoid robots, encompassing a wider range of applications and technological advancements.


**10. What is the primary mechanism by which the hybrid nanoparticles mentioned in the text kill cancer cells?**

(a)  Direct chemical reaction with cancer cell components
(b)  Generation of reactive oxygen species (ROS)
(c)  Production of heat via photothermal effects
(d)  Blocking of blood supply to the tumor

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The text explicitly states that the hybrid nanoparticles produce heat, which kills the tumor cells. While (b) ROS generation is also mentioned as an additional effect, the primary mechanism is the photothermal effect, where light triggers heat production in the nanoparticles. (a) is not mentioned in the text. (d) is not a mechanism of action of the nanoparticles.  The photothermal effect, coupled with the potential for minimally invasive light delivery methods, makes this a promising therapeutic approach.


Here are some difficult multiple-choice questions (MCQs) based on the provided target content, designed to assess various cognitive skills and adhere to the specified criteria.  Each question is followed by a detailed explanation.


**1.  Which of the following accurately describes a key difference between Maternal Spindle Transfer (MST) and Pronuclear Transfer (PNT) in Mitochondrial Replacement Therapy (MRT)?**

(a) MST involves transferring the mother's pronucleus into a donor egg before fertilization, while PNT transfers it after fertilization.
(b) MST uses a donor egg with its nucleus removed, while PNT uses a donor egg that is fertilized before pronuclear transfer.
(c) MST is primarily used to treat mitochondrial diseases caused by mutations in the maternal mitochondrial DNA, whereas PNT addresses paternal mitochondrial DNA issues.
(d) MST involves the creation of two separate zygotes, whereas PNT only uses one.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The core difference lies in the timing of nuclear transfer relative to fertilization. MST involves removing the mother's nucleus from her egg *before* fertilization, transferring it to an enucleated donor egg, and then fertilizing the reconstructed egg.  PNT, conversely, fertilizes both the mother's egg and the donor egg with the father's sperm before removing and transferring the pronuclei. Option (a) is incorrect because it reverses the order of events in MST. Option (c) is incorrect as both techniques target maternal mitochondrial DNA issues; paternal mitochondrial DNA is not directly involved. Option (d) is incorrect because while PNT involves two initially fertilized eggs, only one is ultimately used to create the embryo.  The understanding of these procedural nuances is crucial for grasping the complexities of MRT.


**2.  A researcher is studying the efficacy of different mRNA vaccine delivery systems. Which of the following delivery methods is LEAST likely to be associated with a significant inflammatory response, based on recent research concerning base modifications in mRNA constructs?**

(a) Free mRNA in solution.
(b) Encapsulation in lipid nanoparticles (LNPs).
(c) Encapsulation in polymers.
(d) mRNA delivered ex vivo through dendritic cells.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Recent research highlights the role of base modifications in reducing the inflammatory response associated with mRNA vaccines.  Lipid nanoparticles (LNPs) are a commonly used delivery method for mRNA vaccines, and their design can incorporate strategies to minimize inflammation.  While other methods like encapsulation in polymers or ex vivo delivery through dendritic cells have their own advantages and disadvantages, the research specifically points to modifications within the mRNA construct itself as a key factor in reducing inflammation.  Free mRNA in solution is particularly susceptible to degradation and unwanted immune responses, making it the least effective approach to minimize inflammation.  The question tests the candidate's understanding of both mRNA vaccine delivery and recent advancements in reducing their side effects.


**3.  Considering the mechanisms of action of weight-loss drugs that mimic glucagon-like peptide 1 (GLP-1), which of the following is NOT a direct effect of GLP-1 receptor activation?**

(a) Increased insulin production.
(b) Decreased glucagon production.
(c) Suppression of appetite.
(d) Direct stimulation of fat cell breakdown (lipolysis).


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

GLP-1 agonists work primarily by influencing glucose homeostasis and appetite regulation. They stimulate insulin secretion and suppress glucagon release, leading to improved blood sugar control.  Furthermore, they also reduce appetite by acting on the central nervous system. However, GLP-1's impact on fat metabolism is indirect; while weight loss is an outcome, it's not a direct effect of receptor activation in the same way insulin and glucagon regulation are.  Lipolysis (fat breakdown) occurs as a consequence of reduced caloric intake and improved insulin sensitivity, not as a primary direct effect of GLP-1 binding. This question tests the candidate's ability to differentiate between direct and indirect effects within a complex biological pathway.


**4.  Which of the following statements regarding the World Health Organization's (WHO) CoViNet initiative is INCORRECT?**

(a) CoViNet is a network of global laboratories focused on coronavirus surveillance.
(b) CoViNet includes laboratories from all six WHO regions.
(c) CoViNet exclusively focuses on SARS-CoV-2 surveillance.
(d) CoViNet aims to facilitate early and accurate detection of novel coronaviruses.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

CoViNet's mandate extends beyond SARS-CoV-2. While the COVID-19 pandemic spurred its creation, its scope encompasses surveillance of other coronaviruses of public health importance, including MERS-CoV and novel coronaviruses.  The network aims to enhance global preparedness for future outbreaks.  Options (a), (b), and (d) correctly reflect aspects of CoViNet's objectives and structure.  The incorrect option highlights the broader scope of the initiative beyond a single virus, testing the candidate's attention to detail and understanding of global health initiatives.


**5. Which of the following best describes the key mechanism by which RNA interference (RNAi) inhibits gene function?**

(a) RNAi directly alters the DNA sequence of the target gene, leading to a permanent change in gene expression.
(b) RNAi enhances the translation of the target mRNA into protein, leading to an overproduction of the protein.
(c) RNAi promotes the degradation of the target mRNA, thus preventing the synthesis of the corresponding protein.
(d) RNAi stimulates the immune system to attack and destroy cells expressing the target gene.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

RNAi's primary mechanism is the targeted destruction of messenger RNA (mRNA).  Short double-stranded RNA molecules (dsRNAs) bind to complementary sequences on the target mRNA, leading to its enzymatic degradation. This prevents the mRNA from being translated into protein, effectively silencing the gene.  Options (a), (b), and (d) misrepresent the mechanism.  RNAi doesn't directly modify DNA, enhance translation, or directly stimulate immune responses; its action is focused on mRNA degradation. This question tests the candidate's understanding of a specific molecular mechanism within gene regulation.


These MCQs aim for a higher difficulty level by requiring precise knowledge and the ability to differentiate between closely related concepts.  The explanations provide a detailed analysis of the correct and incorrect options, encouraging a deeper understanding of the subject matter.


Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on factual recall, analysis, and conceptual understanding.  The difficulty level is aimed at 'difficult', challenging assumptions and requiring precise knowledge.


**1.  Concerning Lab-Grown Diamonds, which assertion is accurate?**

(a) Lab-grown diamonds possess significantly lower thermal conductivity compared to natural diamonds, limiting their use in high-power electronics.
(b)  The High-Pressure, High-Temperature (HPHT) method exclusively utilizes a diamond seed for initiating crystal growth, excluding the use of other carbon sources.
(c)  The inherent impurities and structural imperfections found in natural diamonds are entirely absent in lab-grown diamonds, regardless of the production method.
(d) Lab-grown diamonds are primarily utilized for industrial applications due to their superior hardness and strength, while natural diamonds remain the preferred choice for jewelry.


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Option (d) is correct because lab-grown diamonds, due to their controlled production, often exhibit superior hardness and consistency, making them ideal for industrial tools and applications where precision and durability are paramount.  Natural diamonds, while possessing similar properties, often contain impurities and inconsistencies affecting their suitability for certain industrial uses.  Furthermore, the cost-effectiveness of lab-grown diamonds makes them a compelling alternative. Option (a) is incorrect as lab-grown diamonds possess excellent thermal conductivity, making them valuable in high-power electronics as heat spreaders. Option (b) is incorrect because while a diamond seed is commonly used, other carbon sources such as graphite can also be employed in the HPHT method. Option (c) is incorrect; while lab-grown diamonds generally have fewer impurities, they are not entirely free from structural imperfections depending on the growth process.


**2.  Which statement best reflects the advantages of Direct Methanol Fuel Cells (DMFCs)?**

(a) DMFCs offer superior energy density compared to all other fuel cell types, making them ideal for long-duration space missions.
(b) The use of methanol as a liquid fuel eliminates the need for complex storage and transportation infrastructure, making DMFCs exceptionally portable and convenient.
(c)  DMFCs are inherently more efficient in energy conversion compared to conventional combustion engines, resulting in significantly reduced greenhouse gas emissions.
(d) DMFCs are characterized by their exceptionally long lifespan and minimal maintenance requirements, making them a cost-effective solution in the long run.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Option (b) accurately highlights a key advantage of DMFCs.  The use of liquid methanol simplifies fuel handling and transportation compared to gaseous fuels. This portability is a significant advantage for various applications, including portable power devices. Option (a) is incorrect; while DMFCs offer good energy density, it is not superior to all other fuel cell types. Option (c) is incorrect, as the overall efficiency and environmental impact of DMFCs depend on the source of methanol production. Option (d) is incorrect; while DMFCs require less maintenance than some other technologies, their lifespan and cost-effectiveness are still under development and depend on various factors.


**3.  Regarding Perovskite materials, which statement is NOT true?**

(a) The versatility in composition of Perovskite materials allows for fine-tuning of their optical properties, making them suitable for LEDs and lasers.
(b) Perovskite materials are exclusively used in high-efficiency solar cells, with limited applications in other fields.
(c) The general formula for Perovskite materials is ABX₃, reflecting their characteristic crystal structure.
(d)  Alterations in the composition of Perovskite materials directly impact their electronic properties, such as conductivity and bandgap.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Option (b) is incorrect as Perovskite materials show promise in a wide range of applications beyond solar cells, including LEDs, lasers, photodetectors, and X-ray imaging, due to their tunable properties.  Options (a), (c), and (d) accurately describe key features and characteristics of Perovskite materials, highlighting their versatility and tunable properties based on their composition.


**4.  Which application is NOT directly associated with Vanadium?**

(a)  Alloying element in steel production, enhancing tensile strength.
(b)  Component in Vanadium Redox Flow Batteries (VRFBs) for renewable energy storage.
(c)  Use as a catalyst in the production of high-efficiency lithium-ion batteries.
(d)  Presence in Titanomagnetite, a primary source for vanadium extraction.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) is incorrect. While vanadium is a transition metal and plays a role in certain catalytic processes, it's not directly used as a catalyst in the production of lithium-ion batteries. Options (a), (b), and (d) accurately reflect established uses and occurrences of vanadium.


**5.  Concerning the manufacturing of semiconductors, which step involves the use of ultraviolet (UV) light?**

(a) Wafer fabrication, where sand is heated and melted to create a silicon ingot.
(b) Etching, where the degraded resist is removed to reveal the intended pattern.
(c) Assembly, where the silicon die is connected to the printed circuit board (PCB).
(d) Photolithography, where the circuit design is transferred onto the light-sensitive material.


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Photolithography utilizes UV light to expose a light-sensitive material through a mask, creating the circuit pattern on the semiconductor wafer.  The other options describe different stages of semiconductor manufacturing that do not involve UV light.


**6. Which statement about the AMRIT technology developed by IIT Madras is accurate?**

(c) It is a novel method for generating electricity from algae, contributing to renewable energy production.
(d) It is used in the production of high-purity silicon for the semiconductor industry.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The AMRIT technology specifically targets the removal of arsenic and metal ions from water.  The other options describe unrelated technologies or applications.

**8.  Which of the following is NOT a component of a soil-based microbial fuel cell (MFC)?**

(b) Cathode
(c) Electrolyte
(d) Photovoltaic cell


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

MFCs use microbes to generate electricity through electron transfer between the anode and cathode within an electrolyte.  Photovoltaic cells are not part of this process.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging, requiring detailed understanding and knowledge beyond simple factual recall.


**1.  A novel method for directly synthesizing carbon nanotubes (CNTs) on glass substrates at a relatively low temperature (750°C) utilizes which technique?**

(a) High-Pressure, High-Temperature (HPHT) method
(b) Chemical Vapor Deposition (CVD) method
(c) Plasma Enhanced Chemical Vapor Deposition (PECVD) Technique
(d) Atom-Trap Trace Analysis (ATTA)

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly states that a novel method for synthesizing CNTs on glass substrates at 750°C uses the Plasma Enhanced Chemical Vapor Deposition (PECVD) technique.  The other options are incorrect. HPHT is a method for growing diamonds, CVD is a general technique for growing thin films, and ATTA is a radiometric dating method.  The question tests factual recall and understanding of specific scientific techniques in materials science.  The low temperature mentioned in the question is a key differentiator that distinguishes PECVD from other methods that typically require much higher temperatures.  Understanding the context of CNT synthesis is crucial for correctly answering this question.


**2. Which of the following statements accurately describes the application of supercritical carbon dioxide (scCO2)?**

(a) It is primarily used in the production of lab-grown diamonds using the HPHT method.
(b) It serves as a key component in the production of green steel by replacing fossil fuels in oxygen removal.
(c) It's used as a cryogenic fluid for freezing and transporting food products, similar to liquid nitrogen.
(d) It shows potential for enhanced oil recovery (EOR) from depleted reservoirs, coupled with carbon dioxide sequestration.

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The passage clearly outlines the use of scCO2 in enhancing oil recovery and simultaneous carbon sequestration from depleted oil and gas reservoirs.  Option (a) is incorrect as scCO2 is not related to diamond production. Option (b) describes the use of hydrogen in green steel production, not scCO2. Option (c) describes the application of liquid nitrogen, not scCO2.  This question assesses conceptual understanding of scCO2's properties and its application in a specific industrial context. The ability to differentiate between the applications of various substances under pressure and temperature is vital.


**3.  The Indian Landslide Susceptibility Map (ILSM), created by IIT Delhi, incorporates which of the following factors in its assessment?**

(a)  The abundance of tantalum in river sand, indicating geological instability.
(b)  The presence of specific types of microorganisms, such as retrotransposons, in the soil.
(c)  A range of geological and environmental factors, including height, slope, and precipitation.
(d)  The concentration of ethylene in the atmosphere, correlating with increased landslide risk.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly states that the ILSM incorporates sixteen landslide conditioning factors, including height, slope, soil composition, road distance, river proximity, vegetation cover, and precipitation. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect. Tantalum in river sand (a) is unrelated to landslides, retrotransposons (b) are genetic elements, and ethylene concentration (d) is irrelevant to landslide susceptibility.  This question assesses factual recall and understanding of the methodology used in creating a geographical risk assessment model.  The ability to distinguish between relevant and irrelevant factors within a complex system is tested.


**4. Which technology is described as a proposed ultra-high-speed ground transportation system for passenger and cargo, utilizing vacuum tubes, pressurized pods, and magnetic propulsion?**

Maglev (a) uses magnetic levitation but not vacuum tubes and pressurized pods. AUV technology (c) is for underwater applications. Steel Slag Road Technology (d) is for road construction. This question tests the ability to connect a descriptive definition to a specific technology, demonstrating conceptual understanding. **5.  The "Harit Nauka" initiative in India focuses on which of the following?**

**6. Which of the following is NOT a characteristic of the Glycemic Index (GI)?**

(a) It ranks carbohydrate-rich foods on a scale of 0 to 100 based on their effect on blood sugar levels.
(b) It was proposed by Professor David Jenkins of the University of Toronto.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The GI measures the rate at which a carbohydrate-containing food raises *blood sugar* levels, not blood pressure.  The other options are all accurate descriptions of the GI as presented in the passage. This question tests detailed understanding of a specific concept in nutrition science, requiring the candidate to identify a subtle inaccuracy in a plausible distractor. The close similarity between blood sugar and blood pressure makes this a challenging but fair question.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging and requires a deep understanding of the concepts.


**1.  A colorless, odorless, non-flammable, non-corrosive, and extremely cold element used in food freezing and transportation, and cryotherapy, but poses risks of cold burns and frostbite if mishandled, is identified as:**

(a) Ethylene
(b) Methanol
(c) Liquid Nitrogen
(d) Glycerol


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The description clearly points to liquid nitrogen.  The question highlights its key properties (colorless, odorless, non-flammable, non-corrosive, extremely cold) and its applications (food freezing, cryotherapy). The mention of "cold burns and frostbite" further reinforces the identification of liquid nitrogen as the correct answer. Ethylene is used in artificial ripening, methanol is a toxic alcohol, and glycerol is a different type of compound.  The question successfully avoids trivial facts and focuses on the unique properties and risks associated with liquid nitrogen within the context of food safety and cryogenic applications. This aligns with the UPSC's emphasis on understanding both the benefits and drawbacks of scientific advancements.


**2. Which of the following is a measure of how rapidly a carbohydrate-containing food elevates blood sugar levels post-consumption, ranked on a scale of 0 to 100 relative to pure glucose (GI of 100), and proposed by Prof. David Jenkins of the University of Toronto in 1981?**

(a) Glycemic Load
(b) Glycemic Index
(c) Insulin Resistance Index
(d)  Hemoglobin A1c


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The detailed description precisely defines the Glycemic Index (GI). The question emphasizes its key features: the measurement of how quickly blood sugar rises after consuming carbohydrates, its scale (0-100), its reference point (pure glucose), and its originator (Prof. David Jenkins).  Glycemic Load (GL) uses GI but is a different measure. Insulin resistance index and Hemoglobin A1c are related to diabetes but don't directly measure the speed of blood sugar increase from food. This question tests factual recall and conceptual understanding of a specific scientific index, demanding precise knowledge beyond general awareness of diabetes management.  The distractors are plausible for someone with a superficial understanding of diabetes-related metrics.


**3.  A rare condition characterized by simultaneous blood clots (thrombosis) and low platelet count (thrombocytopenia), potentially affecting the brain, abdomen, lungs, and arteries, and sometimes associated with certain COVID-19 vaccines, is known as:**

(a) Meningitis
(b) Thrombosis with Thrombocytopenia Syndrome (TTS)
(c)  Herd Immunity
(d)  Vaccine Efficacy


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The description perfectly matches Thrombosis with Thrombocytopenia Syndrome (TTS). The question highlights the key characteristics: simultaneous blood clots and low platelet count, the organs affected, and its association with vaccines.  Meningitis is an inflammation, herd immunity is a population-level phenomenon, and vaccine efficacy is a metric. This question tests factual recall of a specific medical condition, requiring knowledge of both its symptoms and potential causal factors. The distractors are related to health but represent different concepts, making the question challenging and suitable for a high-stakes exam.


**4.  The process of cultivating undifferentiated plant cells, tissues, or organs on synthetic media in a sterile environment, leveraging the totipotency of plant cells to propagate valuable plants, study their characteristics, and produce plantlets rapidly, is termed:**

(a)  Gene Editing
(b)  Plant Tissue Culture
(c)  Recombinant DNA Technology
(d)  Genome Sequencing


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The description accurately describes plant tissue culture.  The question emphasizes its key aspects: cultivation of undifferentiated plant material on synthetic media, the use of aseptic techniques, the principle of totipotency, and the benefits (propagation, research, rapid plantlet production). The other options are related to biotechnology but represent distinct techniques.  This question tests conceptual understanding and factual recall, requiring knowledge of a specific plant biotechnology technique and its underlying principles.  The distractors are plausible for someone familiar with other biotechnological methods but lack the precision of the definition of plant tissue culture.


**5. Which of the following is a type of genetic engineering technique that modifies genes to alter Mendelian inheritance, increasing the likelihood of specific gene suites being passed to subsequent generations, and often utilizes a Cas9 enzyme and CRISPR technology?**

(a) Genome Sequencing
(b) Recombinant DNA Technology
(c) Gene Drive Technology
(d)  Enzyme Replacement Therapy


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The description perfectly fits Gene Drive Technology (GDT). The question highlights its key features: altering Mendelian inheritance, enhancing the probability of specific gene transmission, and its reliance on Cas9 and CRISPR. Genome sequencing determines the order of DNA nucleotides, recombinant DNA technology involves gene transfer, and enzyme replacement therapy addresses enzyme deficiencies.  This question assesses conceptual understanding of a cutting-edge genetic engineering technique, requiring knowledge of its mechanism and applications beyond basic genetics.  The distractors are related to genetic engineering but represent different procedures, making the question challenging and demanding a higher level of understanding.


**6. A class of materials sharing a common crystal structure (ABX₃), exhibiting versatility in composition and tunable properties like bandgap, conductivity, and light absorption, finding applications in solar cells, LEDs, lasers, and photodetectors, is known as:**

(a)  Lab-grown diamonds
(b)  Vanadium flow batteries
(c)  Perovskites
(d)  Direct Methanol Fuel Cells


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The description precisely defines perovskites.  The question highlights their key characteristics: the specific crystal structure, the tunability of their properties, and their diverse applications in various optoelectronic devices. The other options are related to materials science and energy technology but lack the defining characteristics of perovskites.  This question tests factual recall and conceptual understanding of a specific material class and its applications, requiring knowledge beyond basic materials science. The inclusion of the chemical formula (ABX₃) further increases the difficulty level. The distractors are plausible for someone familiar with other advanced materials but lack the defining features of perovskites.



**7. The process involving the transfer of pronuclei (nuclear genetic material) from a mother's fertilized egg into a donor egg with healthy mitochondria, creating an embryo with the parents' nuclear DNA and the donor's healthy mitochondria, is a technique in:**

This question tests detailed factual recall of a specific assisted reproductive technology, requiring knowledge of its intricate steps and purpose. The distractors are related to biotechnology but lack the specific details of the described procedure.


**8. A genetically modified (GM) crop carrying genes from the soil bacterium *Bacillus thuringiensis* (*Bt*), producing proteins toxic to bollworm pests, and commercially cultivated in India, is known as:**

GM mustard, Bt brinjal, and DMH-11 are other GM crops but do not fit the description. This question tests factual recall and understanding of a specific GM crop and its characteristics, requiring knowledge beyond general awareness of GMOs. The distractors are plausible for someone with general knowledge of GM crops but do not match the specific description.


**9.  A type of fuel cell that directly converts the chemical energy of methanol into electricity, offering advantages like liquid fuel transportability, high energy density, and compact design, is known as:**

**10.  Which of the following is a type of vaccine that uses messenger RNA (mRNA) to instruct cells to produce a specific viral protein, generating an immune response without introducing the actual virus, and offers advantages in rapid development and customization but faces challenges in stability and storage?**

Here are some difficult multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, designed to test various cognitive skills and adhere to the specified criteria.  Each question includes a detailed explanation.


**1.  A recently developed Indian mustard variety boasts reduced pungency due to lower glucosinolate levels, comparable to canola. Which gene-editing technology facilitated this achievement?**

(a) TALEN
(b) ZFN
(c) CRISPR/Cas9
(d) Meganucleases

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly states that the new low-pungent mustard variety was produced using CRISPR/Cas9 gene editing technology.  This technology is a powerful and precise tool for genome editing, allowing for targeted modifications to DNA sequences. TALEN, ZFN, and Meganucleases are other gene-editing techniques, but they are not mentioned in relation to this specific development.  CRISPR/Cas9's ease of use and high efficiency have made it the dominant gene-editing technology in recent years, particularly in plant biotechnology. The successful application of CRISPR/Cas9 in this instance highlights India's growing capabilities in agricultural biotechnology and the potential for developing improved crop varieties with enhanced nutritional and agronomic properties.  The reduction in glucosinolates is significant because high levels can negatively impact livestock health.


**2.  The James Webb Space Telescope (JWST) recently imaged the Sagittarius C region in the Milky Way, revealing new details about star formation.  What significant cosmological model was challenged by JWST's earlier discoveries concerning galaxy formation?**

(a) The Big Bang Theory
(b) The Steady State Theory
(c) The Standard Model of Cosmology
(d) The Inflationary Epoch Theory

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage notes that JWST's findings challenged the Standard Model of Cosmology. This model describes the evolution of the universe from the Big Bang to its present state. JWST's observations of fully formed galaxies earlier than predicted by the Standard Model suggest potential revisions may be needed to account for the discrepancies.  The Big Bang Theory is the foundation of the Standard Model, but the issue lies within the details of galaxy formation and evolution within that framework. The Steady State Theory is an older, now largely discredited model proposing a constantly expanding universe with unchanging density. The Inflationary Epoch Theory addresses the early expansion of the universe, but it's not directly challenged by the JWST's findings on galaxy formation. The JWST data emphasize the need for more refined models that incorporate the newly discovered aspects of early galaxy formation.


**3.  The Indian Space Research Organisation (ISRO) is developing the SCE-200 engine. What type of engine is this and what launch vehicle will it primarily power?**

(a) Cryogenic engine; GSLV Mk III (now LVM3) and future heavy-lift vehicles.
(b) Solid-propellant engine; SSLV
(c) Semi-cryogenic engine; LVM3 and future heavy-lift vehicles.
(d) Hybrid engine; Agnibaan SOrTeD

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage clearly identifies the SCE-200 as a Semi-cryogenic engine being developed by ISRO.  It's designed for ISRO's existing LVM3 (formerly GSLV Mk III) and future heavy-lift launch vehicles. This contrasts with cryogenic engines, which use liquid oxygen and liquid hydrogen, and solid-propellant engines, which use solid propellants. The Agnibaan SOrTeD uses a 3D-printed semi-cryogenic engine, but this is a different engine. The development of the SCE-200 represents a significant advancement in ISRO's launch vehicle technology, enabling greater payload capacity and efficiency.  The use of semi-cryogenic propellants offers a balance between performance and cost-effectiveness compared to fully cryogenic systems.  The transition to the SCE-200 will enhance India's capabilities in launching heavier satellites and payloads into orbit.


**4.  The World Health Organization (WHO) released the second edition of its global sodium benchmarks.  What is the primary aim of this initiative, and what is the WHO's recommended daily sodium intake for adults?**

(a) Reduce sugar consumption; 1500 mg/day
(b) Reduce potassium consumption; 2500 mg/day
(c) Reduce sodium consumption; 2000 mg/day
(d) Reduce trans-fat consumption; 1000 mg/day

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage states that the WHO's initiative aims to reduce sodium consumption to prevent chronic conditions linked to high blood pressure and obesity.  The WHO recommends less than 2000 mg of sodium per day for adults.  This is equivalent to less than 5 grams of salt. The other options are incorrect.  While reducing sugar, potassium, and trans-fat intake are all important for health, they are not the focus of this specific WHO initiative.  The WHO's sodium benchmarks provide reference values for various food categories to help countries track progress toward reducing population-level sodium intake.  The emphasis on sodium reduction reflects its significant contribution to hypertension and related cardiovascular diseases, a major global health concern.


**5.  A study utilized hybrid nanoparticles of gold and copper sulfide for cancer treatment. What dual therapeutic and diagnostic capabilities do these nanoparticles possess?**

(a)  Photoacoustic imaging and chemotherapy
(b) Photothermal therapy and radiotherapy
(c) Photothermal therapy and photoacoustic imaging
(d) Chemotherapy and radiotherapy

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explains that the gold and copper sulfide nanohybrids exhibit both photothermal and photoacoustic properties.  Photothermal therapy uses light to generate heat, killing tumor cells. Photoacoustic imaging utilizes light absorption to generate ultrasound waves, enabling tumor detection.  The combination of these properties makes these nanoparticles suitable for both treating and diagnosing cancer. The other options are incorrect because they don't accurately reflect the dual capabilities described.  The use of nanotechnology in cancer treatment is a rapidly evolving field, and this research highlights the potential of hybrid nanoparticles for improving both diagnostic accuracy and therapeutic efficacy.  The ability to combine both diagnostic and therapeutic functions in a single agent offers significant advantages in terms of patient care and treatment optimization.


**6.  The Draft National Strategy for Robotics (NSR), released by MeitY, categorizes robots into several types.  Which of the following is NOT a category mentioned in the NSR?**

(a) Industrial Robots
(b) Service Robots
(c)  Agricultural Robots
(d) Medical Robots

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**  The passage mentions Industrial, Service, and Medical Robots as the categories in the NSR.  While agricultural applications of robotics are certainly growing, the text doesn't list "Agricultural Robots" as a specific category within the NSR framework.  The NSR aims to develop a comprehensive national strategy for robotics, encompassing research, development, and deployment across various sectors.  The inclusion of Industrial, Service, and Medical Robots reflects the significant potential of robotics in these areas. The omission of a dedicated agricultural category may be due to the diverse nature of agricultural robotics or the fact that it might fall under the broader "Service Robots" category.


**7.  The  Agnibaan SubOrbital Technological Demonstrator (SOrTeD) rocket is notable for its innovative propulsion system. What makes this engine unique?**

(a)  It is a fully cryogenic engine.
(b) It is a solid-propellant engine.
(c) It is a hybrid engine.
(d) It is a 3D-printed, single-piece, semi-cryogenic engine.

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The passage highlights that the Agnibaan SOrTeD's Agnilet engine is entirely 3D-printed from a single piece and is semi-cryogenic. This represents a significant technological advancement in rocket propulsion. The use of 3D printing allows for faster and more cost-effective manufacturing, while the semi-cryogenic design provides a balance between performance and operational complexity. The other options are incorrect.  The Agnilet engine's unique features showcase the potential of additive manufacturing technologies in space exploration and reduce reliance on traditional manufacturing methods. The successful development and testing of this engine demonstrate India's growing capabilities in the field of space technology and its commitment to innovative solutions for accessing space.


**8. Which of the following is NOT a type of neutrino?**

(a) Electron neutrino
(b) Tau neutrino
(c)  Muon neutrino
(d)  Proton neutrino

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The passage lists electron, tau, and muon neutrinos as the three types.  Protons are not neutrinos; they are hadrons, a type of composite particle made up of quarks. Neutrinos are fundamental particles with very little mass and no electric charge. They interact weakly with matter, making them difficult to detect.  The study of neutrinos provides valuable insights into fundamental physics and astrophysical processes. The three types of neutrinos can oscillate between each other, a phenomenon that has implications for our understanding of particle physics.


**9.  The  Reusable Launch Vehicle Autonomous Landing Mission (RLV LEX) successfully demonstrated a key technological capability. What was this achievement?**

(a)  Reaching orbit
(b)  Autonomous mid-air release and landing
(c)  Reaching escape velocity
(d)  Successful docking with the International Space Station

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The RLV LEX test successfully demonstrated the autonomous mid-air release and landing of the Reusable Launch Vehicle. This is a crucial step towards developing reusable launch vehicles, which offer significant cost savings compared to traditional expendable rockets. The passage describes how the RLV was released from a helicopter and then autonomously executed its landing maneuvers. The other options are not relevant to the RLV LEX mission.  This successful test marks a significant milestone in India's space program and demonstrates its commitment to developing advanced launch technologies.  Reusable launch vehicles have the potential to revolutionize space access, making it more affordable and sustainable.


**10. The  OSIRIS-REx mission successfully collected a sample from asteroid Bennu. What is the new name and target of this mission's extended phase?**

(a) OSIRIS-APEX; asteroid Apophis
(b) OSIRIS-REX II; asteroid Vesta
(c) OSIRIS-NEXT; asteroid Eros
(d) OSIRIS-PLUS; asteroid Itokawa

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:** The passage states that the extended phase of the OSIRIS-REx mission is now called OSIRIS-APEX (OSIRIS-Apophis Explorer) and will target asteroid Apophis. The mission's success in collecting a sample from Bennu demonstrated the feasibility of collecting samples from asteroids and returning them to Earth for study. This provides valuable data for understanding the formation of the solar system and the origin of life. The new phase will further enhance our knowledge of asteroids and potentially contribute to planetary defense efforts.  The study of Apophis, a potentially hazardous asteroid, is particularly relevant in this context.


Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging and requires a deep understanding of the material.


**1.  Considering the amendments introduced in the Water (Prevention and Control of Pollution) Amendment Act, 2024, which entity now holds the authority to prescribe the manner of nomination, terms, and conditions of service for the State Pollution Control Boards (SPCB) chairman?**

(a) The respective State governments
(b) The Central Pollution Control Board (CPCB)
(c) The National Green Tribunal
(d) The Central government

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The 2024 amendment significantly altered the power dynamics regarding SPCB chairpersons.  Previously, State governments held this authority. However, the amendment explicitly transfers this power to the Central government.  Option (b) is incorrect because while the CPCB is consulted, the final decision rests with the Central government. Option (c) is incorrect as the National Green Tribunal handles appeals, not appointments. Option (a) represents the previous, now superseded, arrangement.  This question tests factual recall and understanding of legislative changes.


**2. The National Clean Air Programme (NCAP) aims to reduce concentrations of specific pollutants by a certain percentage by 2025-26.  Which pollutants are targeted for this reduction, and what is the target reduction percentage, using the base year 2017?**

(a) Ozone and Nitrogen Dioxide; 25%
(b) Sulphur Dioxide and Carbon Monoxide; 30%
(c) Particulate Matter (PM10 and PM2.5); 40%
(d) Lead and Benzene; 50%

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The NCAP specifically focuses on reducing Particulate Matter (PM10 and PM2.5) concentrations. The target is a 40% reduction compared to 2017 levels by 2025-26.  The other options present plausible but incorrect pollutants and reduction percentages, testing the candidate's precise knowledge of the NCAP's objectives.  This tests factual recall and understanding of environmental policy.


**3.  Which amendment act, passed in 2024, altered the Water (Prevention and Control of Pollution) Act, 1974, and what is a key feature of this amendment concerning penalties for violations?**

(a) The Water Resources Amendment Act; increased prison sentences for violations.
(b) The Water Pollution Control Amendment Act; introduced a system of fines instead of imprisonment.
(c) The Water (Prevention and Control of Pollution) Amendment Act; decriminalized several violations and imposed monetary penalties.
(d) The National Water Conservation Amendment Act; strengthened existing prison sentences for water pollution.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The correct answer highlights the specific name of the amendment act and its key feature of replacing imprisonment with monetary penalties for several violations. Options (a) and (b) use incorrect act titles, while (d) misrepresents the amendment's approach to penalties. This question tests factual recall and understanding of legal changes.


**4. The Plastic Waste Management (Amendment) Rules, 2024, introduced new responsibilities for local bodies. Which of the following is NOT a newly mandated responsibility for local bodies under these rules?**

(a) Conducting annual assessments of plastic waste generation.
(b) Developing infrastructure for plastic waste management.
(c) Setting minimum thickness standards for plastic carry bags.
(d) Submitting annual reports on plastic waste management infrastructure.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**  While local bodies are now responsible for assessing plastic waste, building infrastructure, and reporting progress, setting minimum thickness standards for carry bags remains under the purview of central regulations, not local bodies. This question tests the candidate's detailed knowledge of the amended rules and their division of responsibilities.


**5. The National Mission for Clean Ganga (NMCG) recently issued an amendment to the River Ganga (Rejuvenation, Protection and Management) Authorities Order, 2016. What key change does this amendment allow concerning treated effluent discharge into the Ganga river?**

(a) Complete prohibition of all effluent discharge, treated or untreated.
(b) Permission for untreated effluent discharge under strict monitoring.
(c) Permission for treated effluent discharge after exploring direct reuse options.
(d) Relaxation of all effluent discharge standards for the Ganga river.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The amendment focuses on allowing the discharge of treated effluent, but only after exploring possibilities for direct reuse.  Options (a) contradicts the amendment's purpose, (b) is incorrect as it specifically concerns treated effluent, and (d) presents an overly broad interpretation of the changes. This question assesses understanding of environmental policy and its nuances.


**6.  Which organization released the State of the Global Climate 2023 report, and what is a key finding regarding climate finance investments?**

(a) The Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC); Climate finance needs to increase by 20% by 2030.
(b) The United Nations Environment Programme (UNEP); Climate finance investments need to grow more than six times by 2030.
(c) The World Meteorological Organization (WMO); Climate finance needs to be doubled by 2030.
(d) The World Bank; Climate finance is sufficient for the 1.5°C pathway.

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The WMO released the report, and a key highlight is the need for a more than six-fold increase in climate finance investments by 2030 to align with a 1.5°C pathway.  The other options misrepresent the source or the key finding, testing the candidate's recall of specific details from the report. This question tests factual recall and understanding of climate finance.


**7.  The "Extended Producers Responsibility (EPR)" system, as amended in the Plastic Waste Management Rules, now includes which additional entities, beyond the original scope?**

(a) Consumers and Recyclers only.
(b) Manufacturers of compostable or biodegradable plastics.
(c) Importers of raw materials only.
(d) Government agencies responsible for waste management.

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The EPR system expansion specifically includes producers, importers, and brand owners of compostable or biodegradable plastics. The other options are either partially correct or entirely incorrect regarding the expansion of EPR responsibilities.  This question tests detailed knowledge of the amended rules.


**8.  In the context of the National Mission for Clean Ganga (NMCG),  what was the previous restriction on sewage discharge into the Ganga river, and what change has been introduced?**

(a) Untreated sewage discharge was permitted; now treated sewage is banned.
(b) Treated sewage discharge was permitted; now all sewage discharge is banned.
(c) All sewage discharge was prohibited; now treated effluent discharge is allowed after exploring direct reuse.
(d) No restrictions existed previously; now only treated sewage is allowed.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The NMCG amendment allows for treated effluent discharge after exploring direct reuse options, changing the previous complete prohibition of sewage discharge. This question tests the candidate's understanding of the policy shift.


**9. Regarding the  Electricity (Amendment) Rules, 2024, which category of consumers are now permitted to establish, operate, and maintain dedicated transmission lines without a license?**

(a) Residential consumers with high energy consumption.
(b) Small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs).
(c) Consumers with specified load and Energy Storage Systems.
(d) Agricultural consumers.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The amendment specifically allows consumers exceeding a certain load and utilizing Energy Storage Systems to establish their own transmission lines. This question tests knowledge of specific provisions within the amendment.


**10.  Which organization administers conventions and treaties related to patents and other intellectual property rights globally, and what is the name of the key agreement of the World Trade Organization (WTO) that regulates patents?**

(a) The World Bank; the Agreement on Trade-Related Aspects of Intellectual Property Rights (TRIPS).
(b) The World Intellectual Property Organization (WIPO); the Agreement on Trade-Related Aspects of Intellectual Property Rights (TRIPS).
(c) The United Nations; the General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade (GATT).
(d) The International Monetary Fund (IMF); the Washington Consensus.

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** WIPO administers global IP conventions, and TRIPS is the WTO agreement regulating patents. This question tests knowledge of international organizations and trade agreements related to intellectual property.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes a detailed explanation.  The difficulty level is aimed at 'difficult' by demanding precise knowledge and including plausible distractors.


**1.  A colorless, odorless, non-flammable, non-corrosive, and extremely cold element used in food preservation and cryotherapy, but poses risks of cold burns and frostbite upon direct contact, is identified as:**

(a) Methanol
(b) Ethylene
(c) Liquid Nitrogen
(d) Glycemic Index


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The description perfectly matches Liquid Nitrogen.  It's explicitly described in the text as having all those properties and applications. Methanol is a volatile liquid with a distinct odor, making (a) incorrect. Ethylene is a gas used in fruit ripening, not cryotherapy, making (b) incorrect. Glycemic Index is a measure of how quickly food raises blood sugar, not a chemical element, making (d) incorrect. The question tests factual recall of specific properties and applications of a substance.  The distractors are carefully chosen to represent other substances mentioned in the text, requiring precise knowledge to eliminate them.


**2. Which of the following is a measure of how quickly a carbohydrate-containing food raises blood sugar levels, proposed by Prof. David Jenkins of the University of Toronto in 1981, and linked to Type II diabetes and cardiovascular diseases risk?**

(a) Glycemic Load
(b) Glycemic Index
(c) Retrogradation
(d) Resistant Starch


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The question directly describes the Glycemic Index (GI).  The explanation of GI, its proposer, and its health implications are all clearly stated in the text.  Glycemic Load (GL) uses GI as a component, but it is not the primary measure described, making (a) incorrect. Retrogradation and resistant starch are factors influencing GI, not the index itself, making (c) and (d) incorrect. The question assesses conceptual understanding of a specific scientific index and its relationship to health, requiring precise recall of details.


**3.  A rare condition characterized by blood clots forming in unusual places (brain, abdomen, lungs, arteries, etc.) alongside low platelet count, sometimes associated with a specific COVID-19 vaccine, is known as:**

(a) Meningitis
(b) Avian Influenza
(c) Thrombosis with Thrombocytopenia Syndrome (TTS)
(d)  Vaccine-induced Immune Thrombotic Thrombocytopenia (VITT)


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The description accurately defines Thrombosis with Thrombocytopenia Syndrome (TTS). The text explicitly links TTS to unusual blood clot formation and low platelet count, and mentions its association with a COVID-19 vaccine. Meningitis is an inflammation of brain and spinal cord tissues, unrelated to blood clots, making (a) incorrect. Avian influenza is a bird flu, completely different from the described condition, making (b) incorrect.  VITT is a synonym for TTS, but the question asks for the term used in the provided text, making (d) incorrect.  The question tests factual recall of a specific medical condition and its characteristics, requiring the ability to differentiate it from similar-sounding or related conditions.


**4. The optical phenomenon enabling light signal propagation through optical fibers is:**

(a) Interference
(b) Scattering
(c) Total Internal Reflection
(d) Refraction


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The text directly states that total internal reflection is the responsible phenomenon. Interference, scattering, and refraction are other optical phenomena, but they are not the primary mechanism for light transmission in optical fibers, making (a), (b), and (d) incorrect.  The question tests factual recall of a specific scientific principle and its application in a technological context.


**5.  A class of materials sharing a common crystal structure (ABX₃) known for versatility in composition, tunable properties (bandgap, conductivity, light absorption), and applications in solar cells, LEDs, lasers, and photodetectors is referred to as:**

(a)  DMFCs
(b) Perovskite
(c) Lab-grown diamonds
(d) Vanadium


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The description precisely defines Perovskite materials. The text details its crystal structure, tunable properties, and diverse applications. DMFCs are fuel cells, not a class of materials with the described properties, making (a) incorrect. Lab-grown diamonds are synthetic diamonds, irrelevant to the properties mentioned, making (c) incorrect. Vanadium is a chemical element used in alloys and batteries, not a class of materials with tunable optical and electronic properties, making (d) incorrect.  The question tests conceptual understanding of a specific material class and its key characteristics and applications.


**6.  Which of the following is NOT a characteristic of methanol (CH3OH), also known as wood alcohol?**

(a) Colorless liquid
(b) High flammability
(c) Completely mixable with water
(d) Used in synthetic dyestuffs


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The text describes methanol as non-flammable. This makes (b) the correct answer. Options (a), (c), and (d) are all explicitly mentioned in the text as properties or uses of methanol. The question tests factual recall of specific properties of a chemical compound and requires careful attention to detail.


**7.  The World Health Organization (WHO) initiative aiming to reduce sodium consumption and prevent chronic conditions related to high blood pressure and obesity, providing reference values for sodium content in different food categories, is known as:**

CoViNet is a coronavirus surveillance network, irrelevant to sodium consumption, making (a) incorrect. The Codex Alimentarius Commission sets food standards, but not specifically focused on sodium, making (c) incorrect. The Global Influenza Surveillance system deals with influenza, not sodium, making (d) incorrect. The question tests factual recall of a specific WHO initiative and its objective.


**8. The Indian initiative, revised in 2021, outlining actions to handle avian influenza outbreaks, providing state-level preparedness advice, and prohibiting HPAI vaccination is the:**

**9.  A gut hormone, secreted from the distal intestine, pancreas, and central nervous system, that increases insulin production, reduces glucagon production, suppresses appetite, and slows digestion, is:**

(a) Glucagon
(b) Insulin
(c) Glucagon-like peptide 1 (GLP-1)
(d)  Enzyme


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The description perfectly matches Glucagon-like peptide 1 (GLP-1). The text details its secretion sites, actions on insulin and glucagon, and effects on appetite and digestion. Glucagon and insulin are hormones with opposing actions, making (a) and (b) incorrect. Enzymes catalyze reactions, but don't have the described hormonal functions, making (d) incorrect. The question tests conceptual understanding of a specific hormone and its physiological roles.


**10.  The technology used to create synthetic or cultured diamonds in a laboratory environment, employing either high-pressure, high-temperature (HPHT) or chemical vapor deposition (CVD) methods, is:**

The question tests factual recall of a specific technological process and its methods.
