**Explanation:** The definition of Glycemic Index is explicitly stated in the text.  It directly measures the speed at which blood sugar levels rise after consuming a carbohydrate-rich food.  Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect as they refer to different aspects of food and nutrition, not the core concept of the GI. The explanation highlights the precise definition and distinguishes it from other nutritional indices.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on Science and Technology.  Each question is designed to be challenging and assess various cognitive skills, with detailed explanations for the correct and incorrect options.


**1.  A novel approach in genetic engineering involves the precise modification of an organism's DNA sequence to alter its traits.  This method utilizes site-directed nucleases to introduce changes such as small deletions, substitutions, or nucleotide additions.  Which of the following best describes this technique?**

(a) Gene silencing
(b) Genome sequencing
(c) Genome editing
(d) Recombinant DNA technology

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question describes genome editing, a precise technique for altering DNA sequences.  Genome editing employs site-directed nucleases (SDNs) like CRISPR-Cas9 to make targeted changes in the genome.  Gene silencing (a) involves turning off gene expression, not altering the DNA sequence itself. Genome sequencing (b) is the process of determining the complete DNA sequence of an organism, not modifying it. Recombinant DNA technology (d) involves combining DNA from different sources, a broader concept than the precise targeted modification described in the question.


**2. The James Webb Space Telescope (JWST) has revolutionized our understanding of the universe.  One key feature of the JWST allows it to observe celestial objects in the infrared spectrum, providing insights otherwise unavailable with visible-light telescopes. What is the primary advantage of JWST's infrared observation capability?**

(a) Enhanced resolution for near-Earth objects
(b) Improved detection of exoplanets and their atmospheres
(c) Increased accuracy in measuring stellar distances
(d) Superior imaging of solar flares

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The JWST's infrared capabilities are particularly beneficial for observing exoplanets and their atmospheres. Infrared light can penetrate dust clouds that obscure visible light, allowing for the observation of planets forming around distant stars.  While JWST offers enhanced resolution (a), this is not its primary advantage related to infrared observation.  Stellar distance measurement (c) relies more on parallax and other techniques. Solar flares (d) are primarily observed in other wavelengths.


**3.  A groundbreaking medical technology uses a patient's own modified immune cells to target and destroy cancer cells. This therapy involves genetically engineering T cells to express chimeric antigen receptors (CARs), which bind to specific antigens on cancer cells, triggering their destruction.  What is this advanced cancer treatment known as?**

(a) Gene drive technology
(b) CRISPR-Cas9 gene editing
(c) CAR-T cell therapy
(d)  Mitochondrial replacement therapy

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description clearly outlines CAR-T cell therapy, a type of immunotherapy.  Gene drive technology (a) is used for altering gene frequencies in populations, not directly treating cancer in individuals. CRISPR-Cas9 (b) is a gene-editing tool, but CAR-T therapy is a specific application using modified immune cells. Mitochondrial replacement therapy (d) addresses mitochondrial diseases, not cancer.


**4.  A cutting-edge mission, the Jupiter Icy Moons Explorer (JUICE), is designed to explore Jupiter and its icy moons, searching for potential subsurface oceans and signs of life. Which of the following is a primary scientific objective of the JUICE mission?**

(a) To study the formation of asteroids
(b) To investigate the potential habitability of Jupiter's icy moons
(c) To map the surface features of Jupiter's Great Red Spot
(d) To analyze the composition of solar wind near Jupiter

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The JUICE mission's primary focus is on the potential habitability of Jupiter's icy moons, particularly Europa, Ganymede, and Callisto.  Asteroids (a) are different celestial bodies. The Great Red Spot (c) is a feature of Jupiter itself, not the moons. Solar wind analysis (d) is a broader space physics objective, not a main focus of JUICE's icy moon exploration.


**5. The concept of "dark matter" refers to a mysterious substance that constitutes a significant portion of the universe's mass but does not interact with light or electromagnetic radiation.  What technique would be most suitable for mapping the distribution of dark matter in the universe?**

(a) Radio astronomy
(b) Gravitational lensing
(c) Optical spectroscopy
(d) X-ray diffraction

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** Gravitational lensing is the most effective method for mapping dark matter.  Dark matter's gravitational influence bends light from distant objects, revealing its presence and distribution. Radio astronomy (a) studies radio waves from celestial objects, not directly detecting dark matter. Optical spectroscopy (c) analyzes light's spectral composition, while X-ray diffraction (d) studies crystal structures, neither directly related to dark matter detection.


**6.  The field of epigenetics investigates heritable changes in gene expression that do not involve alterations to the underlying DNA sequence. Which of the following mechanisms is NOT a primary component of epigenetic regulation?**

(a) DNA methylation
(b) Histone modification
(c) Non-coding RNA
(d) Gene mutation

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** Epigenetic modifications alter gene expression without changing the DNA sequence itself. DNA methylation (a), histone modification (b), and non-coding RNA (c) are all key epigenetic mechanisms. Gene mutation (d), however, directly changes the DNA sequence and is therefore not an epigenetic process.


**7.  Artificial intelligence (AI) has shown tremendous potential in various applications, but it also raises ethical concerns, particularly regarding deepfakes. What is a deepfake?**

(a) A type of malware that infects computer systems
(b) A sophisticated algorithm used in facial recognition systems
(c) A synthetic media created using AI to convincingly portray someone saying or doing something they did not
(d) A method for encrypting sensitive data using quantum computing

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** Deepfakes are AI-generated synthetic media that can realistically manipulate video or audio to make someone appear to say or do something they never did. Malware (a) is malicious software. Facial recognition (b) is a separate AI application. Quantum encryption (d) is a cybersecurity technique.


**8.  The development of  "three-parent babies" involves advanced reproductive technologies aimed at preventing the transmission of mitochondrial diseases from mother to child. What is the primary technique used in creating a "three-parent baby"?**

(a) Cloning
(b) Gene therapy
(c) Mitochondrial replacement therapy
(d) In-vitro fertilization (IVF)

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**  Mitochondrial replacement therapy is the specific technique used to create "three-parent babies" by replacing a mother's faulty mitochondria with healthy ones from a donor. Cloning (a) is a different reproductive technology. Gene therapy (b) targets gene defects, not mitochondrial problems. While IVF (d) may be part of the process, it is not the core technique addressing mitochondrial inheritance.


**9.  The field of biotechnology has witnessed significant advancements in gene editing, including the development of CRISPR-Cas9 technology. What is the primary function of the Cas9 enzyme in the CRISPR-Cas9 system?**

(a) To synthesize new DNA sequences
(b) To cleave DNA at specific locations guided by a gRNA
(c) To copy DNA from one location to another
(d) To regulate gene expression by binding to promoter regions

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The Cas9 enzyme acts as molecular scissors, cutting DNA at a specific location determined by the guide RNA (gRNA). It doesn't synthesize DNA (a), copy DNA (c), or directly regulate gene expression (d). These are separate functions within genetic engineering.


**10.  The concept of "Net Energy Gain (NEG)" is crucial in evaluating the viability of energy sources, particularly for nuclear fusion. What does "Net Energy Gain" signify in the context of nuclear fusion research?**

(a) The amount of energy produced exceeds the energy required to initiate and sustain the fusion reaction.
(b) The total energy produced during the fusion reaction is equal to the energy used in the process.
(c) The energy used to initiate the fusion reaction exceeds the energy produced.
(d) The fusion reaction produces no net energy, only heat.

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:** Net Energy Gain means the energy output from the fusion reaction surpasses the energy input needed to start and maintain the reaction. Option (b) describes energy balance, not a net gain. Option (c) indicates a net energy loss. Option (d) is incorrect because fusion reactions produce a significant amount of energy.


These questions are designed to be challenging, requiring a deep understanding of the concepts and facts within the provided target content.  The detailed explanations highlight the nuances and potential distractors, making them suitable for UPSC-level preparation.


**1.  A novel, less pungent mustard variety, comparable in pungency to Canola, has been developed.  Which gene-editing technology was primarily used in its creation?**

(a) TALENs (Transcription Activator-Like Effector Nucleases)
(b) ZFNs (Zinc Finger Nucleases)
(c) CRISPR/Cas9
(d) SDN 1

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly states that the new low-pungent mustard variety was produced through gene editing of the 'Varuna' variety using CRISPR/Cas9 technology.  CRISPR/Cas9 is a revolutionary gene-editing tool known for its precision and efficiency in targeting specific DNA sequences.  This technology allows scientists to make precise changes to an organism's genome, in this case, reducing the glucosinolate content responsible for the pungent flavor in mustard. TALENs and ZFNs are other gene-editing techniques, but the passage specifically highlights CRISPR/Cas9 as the method used in this instance. SDN 1, while a type of site-directed nuclease, does not specify the precise technology employed; CRISPR/Cas9 is a more specific and accurate answer based on the provided information. The development of this low-pungent mustard demonstrates the potential of gene editing in improving crop characteristics and addressing consumer preferences. The success of this endeavor also underscores the growing importance of biotechnology in agricultural innovation and food security.


**2.  The Genetic Engineering Appraisal Committee (GEAC) plays a crucial role in the approval process of a particular type of crop. What is the primary legal basis for GEAC's authority?**

(a) The Seeds Act, 1966
(b) The Protection of Plant Varieties and Farmers' Rights Act, 2001
(c) The Environment Protection Act, 1986
(d) The Biotechnology Regulatory Authority of India Act, 2022

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The text clearly mentions that Genetically Modified (GM) crops require environmental clearance from the Genetic Engineering Appraisal Committee (GEAC), established under the Environment Protection Act, 1986.  The Environment Protection Act provides the overarching legal framework for environmental regulation in India, and GEAC's function in assessing the environmental impact of GM crops falls directly under this Act. While the Seeds Act, the Protection of Plant Varieties and Farmers' Rights Act, and the (hypothetical) Biotechnology Regulatory Authority of India Act all relate to agricultural biotechnology, they do not directly grant GEAC its authority regarding environmental clearance. The Environment Protection Act, 1986, is the key legislation defining GEAC's mandate in this context, emphasizing the importance of environmental considerations in the development and release of GM crops.  This highlights the multi-faceted regulatory landscape governing agricultural biotechnology in India, balancing innovation with environmental protection.


**3.  A novel enzyme replacement therapy (ERT) has recently received approval. What specific condition is this therapy designed to treat?**

(a) Hemophilia
(b) Cystic fibrosis
(c) Congenital thrombotic thrombocytopenic purpura (cTTP)
(d) Huntington's disease

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly states that the US Food and Drug Administration (USFDA) approved Adzynma, the first recombinant protein product for on-demand ERT, to treat congenital thrombotic thrombocytopenic purpura (cTTP). cTTP is a rare and life-threatening blood clotting disorder.  The approval of Adzynma represents a significant advancement in the treatment of cTTP, offering a new therapeutic option for patients suffering from this debilitating condition.  The other options, while representing serious genetic disorders, are not the target of this specific ERT.  This highlights the ongoing efforts in developing innovative therapies for rare diseases, leveraging advancements in biotechnology and genetic engineering. The approval process underscores the rigorous standards and evaluations conducted by regulatory bodies like the USFDA to ensure the safety and efficacy of novel therapies.


**4.  A particular genetic engineering technique alters Mendelian inheritance patterns to increase the likelihood of specific genes being passed to the next generation. What is the name of this technology?**

(a) Recombinant DNA technology
(b) Genome sequencing
(c) Gene-drive technology (GDT)
(d) CRISPR technology

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description perfectly matches Gene-drive technology (GDT).  The passage explicitly defines GDT as a genetic engineering technique that modifies genes to alter Mendelian inheritance, increasing the probability of specific genes being inherited by offspring.  While CRISPR technology is a component of GDT (acting as a molecular scissor), and recombinant DNA technology is a broader field encompassing gene manipulation, it is GDT that specifically addresses the described alteration of inheritance patterns. Genome sequencing, on the other hand, is a process of determining the order of nucleotides in a genome, not a gene-editing technique that alters inheritance.  The development and application of GDT raise significant ethical and ecological concerns regarding its potential unintended consequences.  The passage highlights its promising applications in controlling mosquito populations but also implicitly acknowledges the need for careful consideration of its broader implications.


**5.  Two distinct techniques are commonly used in a specific reproductive technology involving three people's DNA. What are these techniques?**

(a)  In vitro fertilization (IVF) and intracytoplasmic sperm injection (ICSI)
(b)  Maternal spindle transfer (MST) and pronuclear transfer (PNT)
(c)  Gamete intrafallopian transfer (GIFT) and zygote intrafallopian transfer (ZIFT)
(d)  Preimplantation genetic diagnosis (PGD) and preimplantation genetic screening (PGS)

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly mentions Maternal Spindle Transfer (MST) and Pronuclear Transfer (PNT) as the two most common techniques used in Mitochondrial Donation Treatment (MDT), also known as three-parent baby procedures.  These techniques involve manipulating eggs or embryos to replace diseased mitochondria with healthy ones from a donor, resulting in offspring with genetic material from three individuals.  The other options represent different assisted reproductive technologies but are not specifically associated with the three-parent baby procedure. The ethical implications of MDT are complex and continue to be debated, raising concerns about genetic modification and the potential long-term effects on offspring.  The passage highlights the use of MDT to prevent the transmission of mitochondrial diseases, but also implicitly acknowledges the need for careful ethical and scientific considerations.


**6.  A type of medical imaging technology uses a large magnet and radio waves to produce detailed images of internal structures without using ionizing radiation. Which technology is this?**

(a) Computed tomography (CT) scan
(b) Positron emission tomography (PET) scan
(c) X-ray
(d) Magnetic resonance imaging (MRI)

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The description accurately describes Magnetic Resonance Imaging (MRI).  The passage clearly states that MRI is a non-invasive medical imaging test that uses a large magnet and radio waves to create detailed images of internal structures without ionizing radiation.  CT scans, PET scans, and X-rays all utilize ionizing radiation, making them different from MRI.  MRI's ability to provide detailed images without the harmful effects of ionizing radiation makes it a valuable tool in medical diagnosis.  The development of more powerful MRI machines, as mentioned in the context of Iseult, continues to improve the resolution and diagnostic capabilities of this technology, leading to advancements in medical understanding and treatment.


**7.  A type of plant tissue culture uses any part of the plant (root, stem, leaf, or flower) as a starting material for culturing purposes. What is this type of plant tissue culture called?**

(a) Seed culture
(b) Embryo culture
(c) Organ culture
(d) Cell culture

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The passage explicitly defines organ culture as the type of plant tissue culture that uses any part of a plant (root, stem, leaf, or flower) as an explant for culturing. This technique leverages the totipotency of plant cells, their ability to differentiate into any type of specialized cell, allowing for the propagation and genetic improvement of valuable plants. Seed culture and embryo culture use seeds and embryos, respectively, as starting materials, while cell culture focuses on individual cells. The development of plant tissue culture has revolutionized plant propagation, offering advantages such as rapid multiplication, disease elimination, and genetic improvement.  The passage highlights its application in propagating threatened or rare native tree species, showcasing its importance in conservation efforts.


**8.  A specific type of malicious software is installed on computing devices without the user's knowledge to monitor or steal sensitive information. What is the name of this type of software?**

(a) Ransomware
(b) Virus
(c) Spyware
(d) Malware

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The provided definition precisely describes spyware.  The passage explicitly defines spyware as malicious software installed without the user's knowledge to monitor or steal sensitive information. While ransomware, viruses, and malware are all types of malicious software, spyware specifically focuses on the covert monitoring and theft of data.  The increasing prevalence of spyware highlights the growing threat of cyberattacks and the importance of cybersecurity measures to protect personal and sensitive information.  The passage mentions mercenary spyware, a particularly insidious form targeting specific individuals, emphasizing the sophistication and potential impact of such threats.


**9.  A recently launched network of global laboratories focuses on early and accurate detection, monitoring, and assessment of various coronaviruses.  What is the name of this network?**

The other options represent different organizations and initiatives: GISRS focuses on influenza surveillance, ITER on nuclear fusion, and WOAH on animal health.  The establishment of CoViNet underscores the importance of global collaboration in pandemic preparedness and response. **10. A specific type of high-altitude, long-endurance unmanned aerial vehicle is used for aerial surveillance. What is the name of this type of vehicle?**

**3.  The text discusses a method for determining the age of objects using a radioactive isotope. This method is limited by the half-life of the isotope used.  Which isotope's limitations are discussed, highlighting its inability to date objects older than approximately 50,000 years?**

(c) Carbon-14

Here are some UPSC-style Multiple Choice Questions (MCQs) based on the provided target content, focusing on Science and Technology.  Each question is designed to be challenging and assess various cognitive skills, with detailed explanations provided.

**1.  The Chandrayaan-3 mission achieved a significant milestone by being the first to successfully perform a soft landing near which lunar region?**

(a) Lunar North Pole
(b) Lunar Equator
(c) Lunar South Pole
(d) Lunar Far Side

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**  The Chandrayaan-3 mission's successful soft landing near the lunar South Pole is a landmark achievement.  Previous lunar missions, including those from the US, Russia, and China, primarily focused on the equatorial region due to its relatively smoother terrain and abundant sunlight. The South Pole, however, presents unique scientific and strategic advantages, including permanently shadowed craters that may contain significant water ice – a crucial resource for future lunar exploration and potentially in-situ resource utilization (ISRU).  Option (a) is incorrect because Chandrayaan-1 detected water ice in the North polar region, but Chandrayaan-3's landing was not there. Option (b) is incorrect as previous missions successfully landed near the equator. Option (d) is incorrect because while the far side of the moon is scientifically interesting, Chandrayaan-3 did not land there; China's Chang'e-4 was the first to land on the far side. The South Pole's unique characteristics make it a prime target for future exploration, and Chandrayaan-3's success underscores India's leading role in lunar science.


**2. Which of the following is NOT a challenge associated with achieving a soft landing on the Moon, particularly near the South Pole?**

(a) Difficult terrain with unexpected changes.
(b) The presence of a dense lunar atmosphere hindering controlled descent.
(c) The need to drastically reduce speed from high orbital velocities.
(d) Lunar dust potentially obscuring sensors and cameras.

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**  Soft landings on the Moon present several significant challenges.  The rugged and unpredictable terrain near the South Pole increases the risk of altitude sensor errors and software glitches during the descent.  The extreme speed of lunar modules upon entering the lunar atmosphere necessitates a precise and controlled deceleration to zero velocity for a safe landing.  Lunar dust can also significantly impair the functionality of cameras and other vital sensors. However, the Moon lacks a substantial atmosphere. This absence of atmospheric drag makes controlled descent significantly more difficult, as parachutes cannot be used to slow the spacecraft's descent.  Instead, the lander relies entirely on its thrusters for precise maneuvering and braking, increasing the complexity and precision required for a successful soft landing. The other options accurately represent challenges encountered during the lunar landing process.


**3.  Aditya-L1, India's first space-based observatory-class solar mission, is uniquely positioned at which Lagrange point to study the Sun?**

(a) L2
(b) L3
(c) L4
(d) L1

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** Aditya-L1's strategic placement at the L1 Lagrange point offers a significant advantage for continuous solar observation.  Lagrange points are locations in space where the gravitational forces of two large bodies (in this case, the Sun and Earth) and the centrifugal force of a smaller object (Aditya-L1) balance each other, allowing the spacecraft to remain relatively stationary with minimal fuel consumption. While L2 is used for missions requiring minimal solar interference (e.g., James Webb Space Telescope), L1 provides a unique vantage point for uninterrupted solar observation, allowing Aditya-L1 to study various aspects of the Sun's activity without interference from Earth or the Moon. L3, L4, and L5 are other Lagrange points, but they are not optimal for continuous solar observation.  The selection of L1 demonstrates a deep understanding of orbital mechanics and strategic mission planning for solar research.


**4. What unique feature distinguishes the "agglutinates" found in lunar regolith?**

(a) They are primarily composed of volcanic glass.
(b) They are only found on the Moon.
(c) They are formed through impact events.
(d) They are rich in rare earth elements.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** Lunar regolith, the layer of loose, unconsolidated material covering the Moon's surface, is composed of various components, including rock chips, mineral fragments, impact and volcanic glasses.  Agglutinates are a unique component of lunar regolith, distinguished by their exclusive presence on the Moon. These are soil grains that are fused together by the impact of micrometeorites, creating a unique type of lunar soil. While volcanic glass and impact events contribute to lunar regolith formation, they are not unique to agglutinates.  Similarly, while some lunar materials are rich in rare earth elements, this is not a defining characteristic of agglutinates. The unique formation and exclusive presence of agglutinates on the Moon make them a valuable subject of study for understanding the Moon's geological history and evolution.


**5.  Which of the following statements accurately describes the phenomenon of tidal locking?**

(a) It results in the Moon always presenting the same face to the Sun.
(b) It is caused by the gravitational interaction between the Moon and the Sun.
(c) It leads to significant variations in the Moon's rotational speed.
(d) It is the primary cause of lunar eclipses.

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:** Tidal locking is a phenomenon where the gravitational forces between two celestial bodies cause one body to rotate at the same rate as its orbital period around the other.  In the case of the Earth-Moon system, tidal locking results in the Moon always presenting the same face to the Earth.  This synchronization between the Moon's rotation and its orbit around Earth is due to the gravitational pull exerted by both bodies on each other, causing a distortion in their shapes and slowing down the Moon's rotation. While the Sun's gravity influences the Moon's orbit, the primary driver of tidal locking is the gravitational interaction between the Earth and the Moon. The Moon's rotational speed is essentially constant due to tidal locking, and tidal locking is not directly involved in causing lunar eclipses, which are caused by the alignment of the Sun, Earth, and Moon. The synchronous rotation resulting from tidal locking is a fundamental aspect of the Earth-Moon system's dynamics.


**6.  What is the primary function of the Visible Emission Line Coronograph (VELC) payload onboard Aditya-L1?**

(a) To study the Sun's low-energy X-ray emissions.
(b) To observe the Sun's upper atmospheric dynamics.
(c) To measure the solar wind's particle and plasma environment.
(d) To analyze the Sun's magnetic field.


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The Visible Emission Line Coronograph (VELC) is one of the seven payloads onboard Aditya-L1, designed to study the dynamics of the Sun's upper atmosphere (chromosphere and corona).  VELC specifically focuses on spatially resolved observations of the solar disk in the near-UV band, providing crucial data on chromospheric and coronal heating, the physics of partially ionized plasma, and the initiation of coronal mass ejections (CMEs) and solar flares.  Other payloads, such as SoLEXS and HEL1OS, are focused on X-ray emissions, while ASPEX and PAPA study the in-situ particle and plasma environment.  The advanced capabilities of VELC are crucial for understanding the complex processes driving solar activity and their impact on space weather.  The mission's focus on the upper atmospheric dynamics highlights the importance of studying these regions for a comprehensive understanding of solar behavior.


**7. What is the primary application of Atom Trap Trace Analysis (ATTA) as highlighted in the context of a recent study?**

(a) Detecting trace amounts of water on the Moon.
(b) Analyzing the composition of lunar regolith.
(c) Using Calcium-41 for radiometric dating.
(d) Measuring the age of asteroids.


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** A recent study demonstrated the potential of using Calcium-41, a rare long-lived radioisotope of calcium, for radiometric dating.  Atom Trap Trace Analysis (ATTA) is a technique used to accurately measure the abundance of Calcium-41 in samples, enabling the determination of their age. This is significant because traditional methods using Carbon-14 have limitations in dating materials older than approximately 50,000 years.  ATTA offers a potential alternative, expanding the range of materials and timeframes that can be accurately dated. While Calcium-41 can be found in the soil and is relevant to the study of the Earth's crust, this study specifically demonstrated its application in radiometric dating using ATTA. The technique is not directly applied to detecting lunar water, analyzing regolith composition, or dating asteroids, although the principle of radiometric dating could be applied in those contexts with different isotopes.  The successful application of ATTA to Calcium-41 dating represents a significant advancement in the field of radiometric analysis.


**8.  Which of the following is NOT a component of lunar regolith?**

(a) Rock chips
(b) Mineral fragments
(c) Agglutinates
(d)  Crystalline silicon


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** Lunar regolith is a complex mixture of materials formed over billions of years by various processes.  It comprises rock chips, mineral fragments, impact glasses, and volcanic glasses. Agglutinates are a unique type of soil formed by the fusion of soil grains due to micrometeorite impacts.  However, crystalline silicon, while a common element in various rocks and minerals, is not explicitly listed as a primary component of lunar regolith in the provided text. While silicon might be present in trace amounts within the minerals that constitute the regolith, it is not identified as a major constituent. Therefore, crystalline silicon is not a primary constituent of lunar regolith, as defined by the provided information.  The other options are all explicitly mentioned components of the lunar regolith.  Understanding the composition of lunar regolith is critical for planning future lunar missions and resource utilization.

**1.  A recent study highlighted the potential of a rare, long-lived radioisotope found in the Earth's crust for radiometric dating, offering an alternative to a more commonly used but limited isotope.  Which radioisotope is this study focused on?**

(a) Carbon-12
(b) Potassium-40
(c) Calcium-41
(d) Argon-40

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question focuses on a specific recent scientific advancement in radiometric dating.  While Carbon-14, Potassium-40, and Argon-40 are all used in radiometric dating, the passage explicitly mentions a study using Calcium-41 as a novel approach.  This highlights the evolving nature of dating techniques and the search for methods to overcome limitations of existing ones.  Option (a), Carbon-12, is the most abundant isotope of carbon and is not used for dating due to its stability. Options (b) and (d) are indeed used in radiometric dating, but the question specifically asks about the radioisotope highlighted in the *recent* study, which is Calcium-41. The ability to accurately recall this specific detail from the provided text demonstrates a strong grasp of the subject matter.

**4.  A process involving a fluid state of carbon dioxide held at or above its critical temperature and pressure has shown promise in a specific industrial application.  What is this process used for?**

**6.  Which of the following is NOT a key element of the proposed hyperloop transportation system?**

**7.  A method of altering the DNA of organisms, including plants, bacteria, and animals, often using site-directed nucleases, is described.  What is this method called?**

(a) Gene cloning
(b) Genome sequencing
(c) Genome editing
(d) Genetic fingerprinting

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question tests understanding of genetic engineering techniques. The description accurately reflects the definition and applications of genome editing, which involves altering an organism's DNA using tools like site-directed nucleases (SDNs) to make precise changes.  The other options represent different genetic techniques with distinct purposes. Gene cloning focuses on creating copies of a specific gene, genome sequencing determines the order of bases in DNA, and genetic fingerprinting uses DNA for identification purposes.  Correctly identifying genome editing demonstrates a clear understanding of its core principles.


**8.  Which of the following is NOT a component of a Radioisotope Thermoelectric Generator (RTG)?**

(a) Radioisotope Heater Unit (RHU)
(b) Solar panels
(c) RTG (Heat-to-Electricity Conversion)
(d) Batteries

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** This question assesses knowledge of a specific type of power generation system used in space exploration.  The description of an RTG clearly outlines its components: a Radioisotope Heater Unit (RHU) for heat generation, a heat-to-electricity conversion mechanism (often using thermocouples), and batteries for storing the generated electricity.  Solar panels are not a component of an RTG, as RTGs are designed to function independently of sunlight, making them suitable for deep space missions. The correct identification of this detail shows a strong understanding of RTG technology.


**9.  What type of lens is used in a magnifying glass?**

(a) Concave lens
(b) Plano-concave lens
(c) Convex lens
(d) Concavo-convex lens


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** This question assesses basic understanding of optics. A magnifying glass uses a convex lens to enlarge the image of an object.  Convex lenses converge light rays, while concave lenses diverge them.  Plano-concave and concavo-convex lenses are variations of concave lenses and would not magnify an object.  The ability to recall this fundamental optical principle is essential.


**10.  What is the name of the law which states that equal volumes of all gases, under the same conditions of temperature and pressure, contain equal numbers of molecules?**

(a) Graham's Law
(b) Avogadro's Law
(c) Boyle's Law
(d) Charles's Law

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** This question tests knowledge of fundamental gas laws. Avogadro's Law directly states the relationship between volume and the number of molecules in a gas under constant temperature and pressure. The other options describe different gas laws: Graham's Law relates gas diffusion rates, Boyle's Law relates pressure and volume, and Charles's Law relates volume and temperature.  Knowing this specific law demonstrates a solid understanding of basic chemistry principles.



Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging, requiring detailed knowledge and understanding of the subject matter.


**1.  A colorless, odorless, non-flammable, non-corrosive, and extremely cold element used in food preservation and cryotherapy poses a risk of cold burns and frostbite if mishandled.  Which substance is being described?**

(a) Ethylene
(b) Methanol
(c) Liquid Nitrogen
(d) Ethanol


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description perfectly matches the properties and applications of liquid nitrogen, a cryogenic fluid used in freezing and transporting food.  Its extremely low temperature (-196 °C) makes it a potent cryogenic agent but also a significant hazard, capable of causing severe cold burns and frostbite upon direct skin contact. Ethylene is a gas used in fruit ripening, methanol is a toxic alcohol, and ethanol is an alcohol used as an antidote for methanol poisoning – none of these fit the description.


**2.  The rapid fluctuation in blood sugar levels caused by the consumption of certain carbohydrate-rich foods can strain the body's insulin production and utilization, potentially leading to complications for individuals with diabetes and cardiovascular issues in the long run.  This characteristic is measured by which index?**

(a) Glycemic Load (GL)
(b) Glycemic Index (GI)
(c)  Body Mass Index (BMI)
(d)  Metabolic Equivalent of Task (MET)


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The question describes the Glycemic Index (GI), a measure of how quickly a carbohydrate-containing food raises blood sugar levels.  High-GI foods cause rapid spikes in blood sugar, which can be problematic for people with diabetes because their bodies struggle to regulate these spikes effectively. While Glycemic Load (GL) considers both GI and carbohydrate quantity, the core concept described pertains to GI. BMI and MET are unrelated measures of body composition and energy expenditure, respectively.


**3. A recent scientific study has highlighted a correlation between the rate at which a carbohydrate-containing food elevates blood glucose levels and the heightened risk of type 2 diabetes and cardiovascular diseases. This relationship is primarily assessed using which of the following?**

(a)  The amount of dietary fiber in the food
(b)  The glycemic index (GI) of the food
(c)  The presence of resistant starch in the food
(d)  The overall calorie content of the food


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**  The question directly refers to the core concept of the Glycemic Index (GI), which quantifies the rate at which a food raises blood sugar.  While dietary fiber, resistant starch, and calorie content influence blood sugar levels, the central focus of the study and the primary metric used is the GI. A high GI indicates a rapid rise in blood glucose, linking it directly to the increased risk of diabetes and cardiovascular problems.


**4. The World Health Organization (WHO) has unveiled a digital health promoter prototype that harnesses generative artificial intelligence (AI) to provide information on various health topics, including healthy habits and mental health, aiming to enhance public health awareness.  What is the name of this AI-powered tool?**

(a) CoViNet
(b) S.A.R.A.H.
(c)  GISRS
(d)  WHO Sodium Benchmarks


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The question describes S.A.R.A.H. (Smart AI Resource Assistant for Health), a WHO initiative leveraging generative AI to provide health information to the public. CoViNet is a coronavirus surveillance network, GISRS is a global influenza surveillance system, and WHO Sodium Benchmarks are reference values for sodium content in food – none of which are AI-powered health information providers.


**5.  The use of a specific gas for artificial ripening of fruits is permitted by the FSSAI, provided its concentration does not exceed 100 ppm.  However, direct contact of this gas with the fruits is prohibited. What is this gas?**

(a) Carbon Dioxide
(b) Oxygen
(c) Nitrogen
(d) Ethylene


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** The question describes the regulated use of ethylene gas in artificial fruit ripening.  The FSSAI guidelines clearly stipulate a maximum permissible concentration and prohibit direct contact to ensure safety and quality. The other gases mentioned are not typically used for this purpose.


**6. Which of the following is a rare condition characterized by blood clots (thrombosis) alongside a low platelet count (thrombocytopenia), sometimes associated with specific COVID-19 vaccines?**

(a) Meningitis
(b) Avian Influenza
(c) Thrombosis with Thrombocytopenia Syndrome (TTS)
(d)  Hepatitis C


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description points to Thrombosis with Thrombocytopenia Syndrome (TTS), also known as Vaccine-induced Immune Thrombotic Thrombocytopenia (VITT).  This rare condition involves unusual blood clot formation and low platelet counts, and has been linked to certain COVID-19 vaccines.  Meningitis, avian influenza, and Hepatitis C are distinct infectious diseases unrelated to this specific thrombotic condition.


**7.  A type of rechargeable flow battery utilizes vanadium ions as its active material, storing energy in two electrolyte tanks connected to a cell stack, leveraging vanadium's unique ability to exist in four different oxidation states. Which battery type is this?**

(a) Lithium-ion battery
(b)  Sodium-ion battery
(c)  Vanadium Redox Flow Battery (VRFB)
(d)  Lead-acid battery


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description precisely defines the Vanadium Redox Flow Battery (VRFB).  Its operation relies on the redox reactions of vanadium ions in different oxidation states, using two electrolyte tanks to store energy. Lithium-ion, sodium-ion, and lead-acid batteries operate on different electrochemical principles and do not employ this specific flow-based system with multiple vanadium oxidation states.


**8. The Indian government's initiative to promote the consumption of certain grains, now rebranded as "Nutri-Cereals," includes their inclusion in the POSHAN Abhiyaan and the launch of a dedicated sub-mission under the National Food Security Mission. Which grains are being referred to?**

(a) Wheat and Rice
(b) Pulses and Legumes
(c) Millets
(d) Maize and Sorghum


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The question describes the Indian government's focus on promoting millets, which have been rebranded as "Nutri-Cereals."  The initiatives mentioned—inclusion in POSHAN Abhiyaan and the sub-mission under the National Food Security Mission—directly target millets to boost their production and consumption. Wheat, rice, pulses, maize, and sorghum are other important grains, but the specific details of the initiatives clearly point to millets.


**9.  The World Organisation for Animal Health (WOAH), an international organization with 183 member countries (including India), collaborates on enhancing animal health globally and plays a crucial role in mitigating the impact of a specific highly pathogenic avian influenza subtype. Which organization is this?**

(a)  The Food and Agriculture Organization of the United Nations (FAO)
(b)  The World Organisation for Animal Health (WOAH)
(c)  The World Health Organization (WHO)
(d) The National Institute of Virology (NIV)


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The question directly names the World Organisation for Animal Health (WOAH), highlighting its role in global animal health collaboration and avian influenza management.  While FAO, WHO, and NIV are involved in various aspects of animal and human health, the question specifically points to WOAH's membership, global reach, and expertise in animal diseases, making it the most appropriate answer.


**10. A type of genome editing technology utilizes site-directed nucleases (SDNs) to introduce changes in an organism's DNA, which might involve small deletions, substitutions, or nucleotide additions.  This technology can be categorized into SDN 1, SDN 2, and SDN 3, based on whether or not alien genetic material is involved. Which genome editing technology is this?**

(a)  Gene Drive Technology
(b) Genome Sequencing
(c) Genome Editing
(d)  CRISPR-Cas9


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The description accurately defines genome editing as a technology that modifies an organism's DNA using site-directed nucleases. The categorization into SDN 1, SDN 2, and SDN 3 based on the use of foreign genetic material further reinforces the identification of genome editing. Gene drive technology, genome sequencing, and CRISPR-Cas9 are related concepts, but the comprehensive explanation in the question specifically points to the broader umbrella term "genome editing."  CRISPR-Cas9 is a *specific* type of genome editing tool.
